Ruling on Tamed Game for a Muhrim: Hanafi-Maliki Dispute
Dispute with Imam Malik on jaza' for tamed game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that killing a tamed pigeon or deer in ihram requires penalty (jaza') and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Original wild nature governs the ruling, not accidental tameness.

When a pilgrim in ihram kills a pigeon that is tame and accustomed to humans, does a penalty become due? The Hanafi and Maliki schools reach opposite conclusions based on how they define 'game' (sayd). This lesson unpacks the dispute and the Hanafi principle of giving weight to original attributes over accidental changes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school regarding a muhrim killing a tamed pigeon or deer? Confirm the hukm level (wajib) and the key reason.
The text states 'hum kahte hain' (we say) indicating the relied-upon view.
2
Identify the opposing view
What is Imam Malik's ruling and his evidence? How does he argue that a tamed pigeon is not sayd?
Maliki evidence: The pigeon cannot protect itself properly due to tameness.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the Maliki evidence? Focus on the principle of original vs. accidental attributes (اعتبار معانی اصلیہ کا کیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ عوارض کا).
Tameness is 'arid (accidental); the pigeon is originally wahshi (wild).
4
Apply the analogy
How does the text compare the tamed deer to a camel that becomes wild? Understand the parallel reasoning.
Just as a camel that goes wild remains domesticated in ruling, a tamed deer remains game.
5
Determine the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? How does this dispute affect a muhrim in practice?
Hanafi: must pay jaza'; Maliki: no penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی محرم نے پاموز کبوتر ذبح کر ڈالا تو اس پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ امام مالک کہتے ہیں کہ اس پر جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پا موز کبوتر ہلا ہوا اور لوگوں سے مانوس ہوتا ہے اٹھان اور اڑان کے سست ہونے کی وجہ سے اپنے پروں سے کماحقہ اپنی حفاظت بھی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور ایسا جانور صید کہلانے کا مستحق نہیں ہے اور جب صید نہیں تو اس کے قتل پر جزاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کبوتر اپنی اصل خلقت اور فطرت کے اعتبار سے وحشی ہوتا ہے اور اڑان کی وجہ سے اپنی حفاظت بھی کرتا ہے اگر چہ اڑان اور اٹھان ست ہو۔ اور رہا اس کا لوگوں سے مانوس ہونا تو وہ عارضی ہے۔ اور اعتبار معانی اصلیہ کا کیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ عوارض کا۔ اس لئے اس عارضی مانوس ہونے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ پس اس پر صید کی تعریف صادق آگئی اور صید کے قتل سے جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس کو ذبح کرنے پڑھی جزاء واجب ہوگی۔ مانوس ہرن کو ذبح کرنے کا حکم وَكَذَا إِذَا قَتَلَ طَيْنَا مُسْتَأْنِسًا لِأَنَّهُ صَيدُ فِي الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يُبطلهُ الْإِسْتِيْنَاسُ كَالْبَعِيرِ إِذَا يَدَلَا يَأْخُذُحُكْمَ الصَّيْدِ فِي الْحُرُمَةِ عَلَى الْمُحْرِمِ ترجمہ اور یوں ہی جب ہلی ہوئی ہرن کو ذبح کیا تو جزاء واجب ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل میں صید ہے تو اس کو ہلا ہوا ہونا باطل نہیں کرے گا۔ جیسے اونٹ جبکہ بھڑک کر وحشت کھا گیا تو وہ صید کا حکم نہیں لیتا کہ محرم پر اس کا ذبح کرنا حرام ہو جاوے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کسی بلی ہوئی ہرن کو قتل کر دیا تو محرم پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ ہرن اصل خلقت کے اعتبار سے صید ہے اور اول کا ہلا ہوا ہونا اس کو عارض ہوا ہے اس لئے ہلا ہوا ہونا اس کے صید ہونے کو باطل نہیں کرے گا جیسے ایک اونٹ ایک اہلی اور پالتو جانور ہے لیکن اگر وہ لوگوں سے بدک کر وحشت کھانے لگا تو وہ اہلی ہونے سے نہیں نکلے گا اور محرم پر حرام ہونے میں شکار کا حکم نہیں لے گا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 3, Book of Hajj. The issue is that a muhrim slaughtered a tamed pigeon, so penalty is wajib upon him. Imam Malik says penalty is not wajib. Imam Malik's evidence is that a tamed pigeon is domesticated and familiar with people, due to weakness in flying and rising it cannot properly protect itself with its wings. Such an animal does not deserve to be called game (sayd), and if it is not game then killing it does not require penalty. But we say that a pigeon in its original creation and nature is wild, and it protects itself by flying even if flight and rising are slow. As for its familiarity with people, that is accidental. Consideration is given to original meanings, not accidents. So this accidental tameness is not considered. Thus the definition of sayd applies to it, and killing game makes penalty wajib. Therefore penalty is wajib for slaughtering it. Ruling on tamed deer: Likewise if one kills a tamed deer, penalty is wajib because it is originally game, so tameness does not nullify it, just as a camel, when it becomes wild and takes on the ruling of game in prohibition for a muhrim. Translation: Similarly, when a tamed deer is slaughtered, penalty is wajib, because it is originally game, so its being tamed does not nullify it. Like a camel, when it becomes frightened and wild, it does not take the ruling of game such that slaughtering it becomes haram for a muhrim. Explanation: If a muhrim kills a tamed deer, penalty is wajib upon the muhrim. Because a deer is by original creation game, and its being tamed is accidental, so tameness does not nullify its being game. Just as a camel is a domesticated animal, but if it becomes frightened of people and becomes wild, it does not leave its domesticated status and does not take the ruling of game in prohibition for a muhrim.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim killing a tamed pigeon or deer. The Hanafi position is that jaza' is wajib, while Imam Malik holds that no penalty is due. The Hanafi argument relies on the principle that original attributes take precedence over accidental ones. A pigeon is originally wild (wahshi), and its tameness is merely accidental ('arid). Therefore it remains game (sayd) in the legal sense, and killing it in ihram triggers the penalty. To illustrate, the text compares a tamed pigeon to a deer: a deer is originally wild, and even if tamed, it is still considered game. Conversely, a camel that becomes wild does not become game for the muhrim because its original status is domesticated (ahli). The same principle applies: original nature is given weight, not accidental changes. The text then quotes the Arabic from al-Hidayah: 'وَكَذَا إِذَا قَتَلَ طَيْنَا مُسْتَأْنِسًا...' confirming the ruling.

Key Terms
صید (sayd): Game animals that are permitted to be hunted outside ihram but are prohibited for a muhrim.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation for killing game while in ihram, which may be an animal sacrifice, feeding the poor, or fasting.
مانوس (ma'nus): Tamed or domesticated animal that is accustomed to humans.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that a muhrim must pay penalty for killing a tamed pigeon?
A) Because the pigeon is originally wild and tameness is accidental
B) Because the pigeon is considered domesticated and thus not game
C) Because Imam Malik says so
D) Because the pigeon cannot fly

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, killing a tamed pigeon or deer in ihram requires penalty because the animal is originally wild and tameness is accidental.

Muhrim's Slaughter of Game is Carrion
Dispute with Shafi'i on permissibility of muhrim's slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the permissibility of meat from game slaughtered by a muhrim and explain why the prohibition is inherent, not transferred, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A muhrim's slaughter of game is never valid dhabh — the prohibition is in the act, not the intention.

In this passage, the author addresses a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the meat of game slaughtered by a muhrim. The Shafi'i school argues that if the muhrim acts as an agent for a non-muhrim, the act is attributed to the non-muhrim, making the meat halal. The Hanafi school, however, holds that the muhrim's act is inherently prohibited by the Quranic command 'Do not kill game while in ihram' (5:95), and thus it cannot serve as valid dhabh regardless of intention. Let's examine the Hanafi proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly state that the meat of game slaughtered by a muhrim is carrion (maytah) and haram for consumption by anyone, including a non-muhrim for whom it was intended.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if the muhrim slaughters on behalf of a non-muhrim, the act is transferred to the non-muhrim because the muhrim is an agent, so the meat becomes halal for that person.
3
Analyse the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafis cite Quran 5:95 which uses the word 'taqtulu' (kill) not 'tadhbahu' (slaughter), indicating the muhrim's act is not recognized as valid dhabh. Also, dhabh must be a prescribed (mashru') act; a prohibited act cannot be valid.
The verse: وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَ أَنْتُمْ حُرُم
4
Apply the analogy to Magian slaughter
The Hanafis compare the muhrim's slaughter to that of a Magian, which is invalid because the person is not qualified. Similarly, the muhrim's act is invalid because he is prohibited from killing game.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis rule the meat is haram for all; Shafi'is rule it is halal for the non-muhrim if intended for him. This affects actual consumption during Hajj/Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَبَحَ الْمُحْرِمَ صَيْدًا فَذَبِيحَتُهُ مَيْتَةٌ لَا يَحِلُّ أُكُلُهَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَحِلُّ مِمَّا ذَبَحَهُ الْمُحْرِمُ لِغَيْرِهِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلَ فَانْتَقَلَ لَهُ فِعَلَهُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الزَّكَاةَ فِعل مَشْرُوعٌ وَهَذَا فِعَل حَرَامٌ فَلَا يَكُونُ ذَكَاةً كَذَبِيحَةِ الْمُجُوسِى وَهَذَا لأنَّ الْمَشْرُوعَ هُوَ الَّذِى قَامَ مَقَامَ الْمَيْزِ بَيْنَ الدَّم کے لئے حلال ہے کیونکہ محرم دوسرے کے لئے کام کرنے والا ہے۔ پس اس کا فعل دوسرے کی طرف منتقل ہو گا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذبح کرنا مشروع فعل ہے اور محرم کا یہ فعل حرام ہے تو یہ ذبح کرنا نہ ہو گا۔ جیسے آتش پرست کا ذبیحہ۔ اور یہ اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ذبح مشروع وہی آسانی کے واسطے خون اور گوشت کے درمیان جدائی کرنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ پس حلال ہونا معدوم ہو گا ذبح مشروع معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کسی شکار کو ذبح کیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ مردار ہے اس کا کھانا کسی کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر محرم نے کسی غیر محرم کے لئے ذبح کیا تو وہ ذبیحہ اس غیر محرم کے لئے حلال اور جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ محرم نے یہ عمل غیر محرم کے لئے کیا ہے۔ لہذا محرم کا یہ فعل غیر کی طرف منتقل ہو گا گویا اس کو غیر محرم نے ذبح کیا ہے اور غیر محرم کا ذبح کیا ہوا اس کے لئے حلال ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ذبیحہ غیر محرم کے لئے حلال ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذبح کرنا فعل مشروع ہے اور محرم کا ذبح کرنا فعل مشروع نہیں ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَ انتُمْ حُرُم (المائدة (۹۵) یعنی محرم کے ذبح کرنے کو قتل کہا ہے نہ کہ ذبح اس لئے محرم کا ذبح کیا ہوا ذبح نہ ہوگا جیسے مجوسی کا ذبح کیا ہوا جانور ذبح نہیں کہلائے گا۔ اور محرم کا ذبح کرنا حرام اس لئے ہے کہ جانور کے بدن کا خون نجس ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس خون کو الگ کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ اس کا گوشت کھانے کے قابل ہو سکے۔ اور خون اور گوشت کے درمیان امتیاز پیدا کرنا نہایت دشوار کام ہے اس لئے آسانی کے واسطے خون اور گوشت کے درمیان امتیاز پیدا کرنے کے لئے ذبح مشروع کو قائم مقام کر دیا اور کہا کہ اگر ذبح مشروع نہیں ہوا تو خون گوشت سے الگ نہیں ہوا۔ اور اس گوشت کا کھانا حرام ہے۔ پس ذبح مشروع کے معدوم ہونے سے حلال ہونا معدوم ہو جائے گا حاصل یہ ہوا کہ جب محرم کا ذبح مشروع نہیں ہے تو اس کا ذبیحہ حرام اور مردار ہو گا اور مردار کا کھانا کسی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا کھانا محرم اور غیر محرم کسی کے لئے جائز نہ ہوگا۔
And when a muhrim slaughters game, his slaughtered animal is carrion; eating it is not permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: That which a muhrim slaughters for another is permissible, because he is an agent [for that other], so his action is transferred to him. And our evidence is that slaughter (dhabh) is a prescribed act, and this act [of the muhrim] is prohibited, so it is not valid dhabh, like the slaughter of a Magian. And this is because the prescribed slaughter stands in place of separating blood from flesh for ease; so permissibility is absent due to the absence of prescribed slaughter. Translation: And when a muhrim slaughters game, his slaughtered animal is carrion; eating it is not permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i said that what a muhrim slaughters for a non-muhrim is permissible for that non-muhrim, because the muhrim acts for another, so his act is transferred to that person. Our evidence is that slaughter is a prescribed act, and the muhrim's act is prohibited, so it is not valid slaughter, like the slaughter of a Magian. And this is because prescribed slaughter is what stands in place of separating blood from flesh for ease; so permissibility is absent due to the absence of prescribed slaughter. Explanation: If a muhrim slaughters game, his slaughtered animal is carrion; its consumption is not permissible for anyone. Imam al-Shafi'i says that if a muhrim slaughters for a non-muhrim, that slaughtered animal is permissible and lawful for that non-muhrim. Because the muhrim performed this action for the non-muhrim, therefore his action is transferred to the other, as if the non-muhrim slaughtered it, and what is slaughtered by a non-muhrim is permissible for him. So this slaughtered animal would be permissible for the non-muhrim. Our evidence is that slaughter is a prescribed act, and the muhrim's slaughter is not a prescribed act, because Allah says: 'And do not kill game while you are in ihram' (Al-Ma'idah 5:95). He called it killing, not slaughter. Therefore what a muhrim slaughters is not valid slaughter, like the slaughter of a Magian is not considered slaughter. And the muhrim's slaughter is prohibited because the blood in the animal's body is impure; thus it is necessary to separate it so that the meat becomes edible. And creating a separation between blood and meat is very difficult; therefore, for ease, prescribed slaughter is made to stand in place of separating blood and meat, and it is said that if prescribed slaughter did not occur, the blood is not separated from the meat, and eating that meat is prohibited. Thus with the absence of prescribed slaughter, permissibility is absent. The conclusion is that when a muhrim's slaughter is not prescribed, his slaughtered animal is prohibited and carrion, and eating carrion is not permissible for anyone; therefore its consumption is not permissible for either the muhrim or the non-muhrim.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage addresses the second issue: a muhrim's slaughter of game is not valid dhabh; the animal becomes carrion (maytah) and is unlawful for everyone. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the muhrim slaughters on behalf of a non-muhrim, his action is considered as that of the non-muhrim, so the meat is halal for the latter. The Hanafi response is based on the Quranic verse (5:95) which calls the muhrim's killing 'qatl' (killing) and not 'dhabh' (slaughter). Therefore the act is prohibited and cannot be considered valid dhabh. Valid dhabh is a prescribed act (shar'i) that stands in for the difficult task of separating blood from flesh. Since the muhrim's act is prohibited, it cannot fulfill that role. The text compares it to the slaughter of a Magian (Majusi), which is also invalid. Thus the Hanafi view is that no one may eat from it, not even the non-muhrim for whom it was slaughtered. This demonstrates the strong link between the legitimacy of the act and the permissibility of the meat.

Key Terms
ذبیحہ (dhabihah): The animal that has been slaughtered according to shari'ah; a valid dhabh renders it halal.
میتہ (maytah): Carrion; an animal that died without proper Islamic slaughter, or was slaughtered in a prohibited manner, making it impermissible to eat.
مشروع (mashru'): Legally prescribed; an act sanctioned by the Lawgiver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the muhrim's slaughter of game not valid (not considered dhabh) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the animal is not killed properly
B) Because the Quran calls it 'killing' not 'slaughtering'
C) Because the muhrim did not face the Qibla
D) Because the muhrim did not say Bismillah

Key Takeaway
The muhrim's slaughter of game is never valid dhabh because the Quran calls it killing, and a prohibited act cannot be the basis for lawful meat.

Muhrim Eating from His Own Slaughter: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Additional Penalty
Intra-Hanafi dispute on penalty for muhrim eating own slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding whether a muhrim who slaughters game and eats from it must pay an additional penalty, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Eating one's own slaughter violates ihram separately: Abu Hanifa says yes, Sahibayn say no.

This passage presents a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school about the scope of ihram prohibitions. Does a muhrim who illegally slaughters game commit a second violation by eating from it? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold different views. Understanding their proofs (dalil) and the practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf) sharpens your ability to apply the principles of taklif and causality in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and all positions
The act is: a muhrim slaughters game (which is prohibited) and then eats from that slaughter. All Hanafi imams agree that slaughtering requires a penalty (jaza' al-sayd). The dispute is about an additional penalty for eating.
Note that the passage also states that if another muhrim eats, there is no penalty by consensus.
2
State the ruling of each imam
Abu Hanifa: wajib to pay the market value (qimat) of what he ate. Sahibayn: no financial penalty, only istighfar (seeking forgiveness).
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil) for each side
Sahibayn argue that the meat is carrion (maytah); eating carrion only requires istighfar, not compensation. Abu Hanifa responds that for the slaughterer, the prohibition is twofold: it is carrion, and additionally it is a mahzur (prohibition) of his ihram because his ihram caused the meat to become carrion.
Abu Hanifa links the prohibition of eating directly to the muhrim's own ihram, treating it as a separate violation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, the muhrim must pay the value of the meat he ate in addition to the jaza' al-sayd. According to Sahibayn, he only pays the jaza' al-sayd and seeks forgiveness.
This is a financial difference: additional liability vs. none.
5
Note the tarjih (if any)
The passage does not specify which view is mufta bihi. Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah. Later Hanafi works may prefer one view, but the text here presents the ikhtilaf without resolution.
Students should be aware that unresolved ikhtilaf exists within the school.

And if the muhrim who slaughtered eats from that anything, then upon him is the value of what he ate according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said there is no penalty upon him for what he ate. And if another muhrim eats from it, there is nothing upon him in the opinion of all of them. Their evidence is that this is carrion, so nothing is incumbent upon him for eating it except seeking forgiveness. And it is like if another muhrim ate it. And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that its prohibition is due to its being carrion as we mentioned, and due to it being a prohibition of his ihram, because his ihram removed the game from being lawful and removed the slaughterer from being eligible for dhabh. So the prohibition of consumption through these intermediaries is attributed to his ihram, unlike another muhrim, because the consumption of another is not among the prohibitions of his ihram. Translation: And if the muhrim who slaughtered eats from that anything, then upon him is the value of what he ate according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Sahibayn) said there is no penalty upon him for what he ate. And if another muhrim eats from it, there is nothing upon him according to all Hanafis. The evidence of the two is that this is carrion, so nothing is incumbent upon him for eating it except seeking forgiveness. And it is like if another muhrim ate it. And Abu Hanifa's evidence is that its prohibition is due to its being carrion as we mentioned, and due to it being a prohibition of his ihram, because his ihram removed the game from being lawful and removed the slaughterer from being eligible for dhabh. So the prohibition of consumption through these intermediaries is attributed to his ihram, unlike another muhrim, because the consumption of another is not among the prohibitions of his ihram. Explanation: The issue is that if the muhrim who slaughtered eats from his own slaughtered animal, even though eating carrion is prohibited, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the value of the meat he ate is wajib upon him. Note that this value is separate from the penalty for the game (jaza' al-sayd). However, it is necessary that if he ate after having paid the penalty for the game, then the value of the eaten meat is additionally wajib. And if the penalty for the game [is not yet paid? the text cuts off].
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding whether a muhrim who slaughters game and then eats from it owes any additional penalty. All agree that if another muhrim eats, no penalty is due. Abu Hanifa holds that the slaughtering muhrim must pay the value of what he ate, in addition to any other penalties. The Sahibayn hold that since the meat is carrion, eating it only requires istighfar; no financial penalty. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is twofold: first, the meat is prohibited because it is carrion (a general prohibition), and second, because the muhrim's own ihram caused the game to become carrion (since his slaughter was invalid). Thus the prohibition is directly linked to his ihram, making eating it an additional violation of ihram. For another muhrim, eating the same meat is simply eating carrion, which does not specifically violate his ihram; thus only istighfar is needed. The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, the slaughtering muhrim owes the market value of the meat he consumed, in addition to the penalty for killing the game. The text adds a note clarifying that this value is separate from the jaza' al-sayd; if he already paid the jaza', he still owes the value for eating.

Key Terms
قیمت (qimat): Market value of the meat consumed, to be paid as compensation.
ممنوعات احرام (mamnunat al-ihram): Prohibitions of ihram, which include hunting (and by extension, eating the hunted game).
استغفار (istighfar): Seeking forgiveness from Allah; the only required action according to Sahibayn for the muhrim eating his own slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does a muhrim who eats from his own slaughter not owe an additional penalty?
A) Because the meat is carrion, and eating carrion only requires istighfar
B) Because the penalty for killing the game already covers the eating
C) Because the muhrim is allowed to eat what he kills
D) Because the meat is not considered carrion if slaughtered by a muhrim

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on whether eating one's own illegal slaughter creates an additional ihram violation requiring compensation; the practical difference is a financial payment versus mere repentance.

8 min
The Muhrim's Slaughter and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Eating from It
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Muhrim's slaughter and penalty for eating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a Muhrim's slaughter and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the penalty if the slaughterer eats from it.

Core Idea
A Muhrim's slaughter is carrion; eating it by the slaughterer triggers a penalty only in Abu Hanifa's view.

The Hanafi school unanimously holds that a Muhrim's slaughter is invalid, making the animal carrion (maytah) and forbidden for everyone. However, the school's founding imams differ on a consequential question: if the Muhrim himself consumes from that carrion, is he liable for a penalty beyond seeking forgiveness? Imam Abu Hanifa answers yes, while his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) answer no. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and identifies the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Establish the general rule
Understand why a Muhrim's slaughter is invalid. The Quranic verse 'Do not kill game while you are in Ihram' (5:95) indicates that the Muhrim's act is not proper slaughter (dhabh) but mere killing. Therefore, the animal does not become permissible; it is carrion.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon within the school.
2
Identify the point of dispute
The disagreement concerns whether the Muhrim who slaughters must pay a penalty if he eats from his own invalid slaughter. Abu Hanifa says yes (pay the value); the Sahibayn say no (only istighfar).
If another Muhrim eats, all agree no penalty is due.
3
Analyze the proof of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn argue that the animal is carrion. Eating carrion only requires seeking forgiveness (istighfar), not a monetary penalty. They analogize it to a different Muhrim eating, who also incurs no penalty.
They see no additional Ihram violation beyond the general prohibition of carrion.
4
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa distinguishes two aspects of prohibition: (1) the animal is carrion, and (2) eating it is a violation of the Muhrim's own Ihram prohibitions, because his Ihram caused the invalidity. Therefore, a penalty (the meat's value) is due as compensation for violating Ihram.
For a different Muhrim, the prohibition is only carrion; no Ihram violation of that Muhrim is involved.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a Muhrim eats from his own slaughter, Abu Hanifa imposes payment of the meat's value; the Sahibayn require only istighfar. If he ate before paying the original jaza' al-sayd (if the animal was game), the value is subsumed; if after, it must be paid separately.
The text does not give a clear tarjih; both views are preserved.

احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے احرام ہی نے شکار کے جانور کو محل ذبح ہونے سے نکال دیا اور اس نے محرم کو ذبح کا اہل ہونے سے نکال دیا ہے۔ پس ان واسطوں سے اس ذبیحہ کی حرمت اس کے احرام کی طرف منسوب ہوگی۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ محرم کا اپنے ذبیحہ میں سے کھانا احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے ہے اور احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے کسی ممنوع کا ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر اس کھائے ہوئے گوشت کی قیمت بطور ضمان واجہ بہ ہو گی۔ برخلاف دوسرے محرم کے کیونکہ اس کا کھانا اس کے احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہے۔ پس جب اس ذبیحہ میں سے کھانا اس دوسرے محرم کے ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہے تو اس پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Hajj. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume three. If a Muhrim slaughters for a non-Muhrim, that slaughtered animal is lawful and permissible for that non-Muhrim. Because the Muhrim performed this act for the non-Muhrim. Therefore, the Muhrim's action will be transferred to the other, as if the non-Muhrim slaughtered it, and that which is slaughtered by a non-Muhrim is lawful for him. So this slaughtered animal will be lawful for the non-Muhrim. Our evidence is that slaughtering is a prescribed act, and the Muhrim's slaughtering is not a prescribed act because Allah Almighty said: 'And do not kill game while you are in Ihram' (Al-Ma'idah: 95), meaning that the Muhrim's slaughtering is called killing, not slaughter. Therefore, the Muhrim's slaughter will not be considered slaughter, just as an animal slaughtered by a Magian is not called a slaughter. And the Muhrim's slaughter is forbidden because the blood of the animal's body is impure. So it is necessary to separate this blood so that its meat becomes edible. And distinguishing between blood and meat is very difficult. Therefore, for ease, the prescribed slaughter has been made a substitute to create distinction between blood and meat, and it is said that if the prescribed slaughter does not occur, the blood is not separated from the meat, and eating that meat is forbidden. So with the absence of prescribed slaughter, lawfulness ceases. The conclusion is that when the Muhrim's slaughter is not prescribed, his slaughtered animal is forbidden and carrion, and eating carrion is not permissible for anyone. Therefore, it is not permissible for either the Muhrim or the non-Muhrim to eat it. The ruling on the compensation if the Muhrim slaughterer eats something from it: And if the Muhrim slaughterer eats something from it, then according to Abu Hanifa, he must pay the value of what he ate, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: there is no compensation upon him for what he ate. And if another Muhrim eats from it, there is nothing upon him according to all of them. The proof of the two is that this is carrion, so eating it requires nothing except seeking forgiveness, and it is like when another Muhrim eats it. Abu Hanifa's proof is that its prohibition is due to it being carrion as we mentioned, and due to it being a prohibition of his Ihram, because his Ihram removed the game from being lawful to be slaughtered and removed the slaughterer from being qualified for slaughtering with regard to compensation? So the prohibition of consumption through these means is attributed to his Ihram, unlike another Muhrim, because his consumption is not among the prohibitions of his Ihram... So the prohibition of consumption through these means is attributed to his Ihram, unlike another Muhrim, because the consumption of the other Muhrim is not among the prohibitions of his Ihram. It should be remembered that this value is separate from the compensation for the game. However, if he ate after paying the compensation for the game, then the value of the eaten meat will be obligatory separately. And if he ate before paying the compensation for the game, then the value of the eaten meat will be included in the compensation for the game; there is no need to pay separately. Just as no liability is incurred upon him by the eating of another Muhrim, likewise no liability will be incurred upon this Muhrim slaughterer by his eating. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the prohibition of the Muhrim's slaughtered animal is from two aspects: one is because it is carrion as we mentioned, and the other is because it is among the prohibitions of Ihram. Because his Ihram removed the game animal from being eligible for slaughter and removed the Muhrim from being qualified for slaughter. So through these means, the prohibition of this slaughtered animal is attributed to his Ihram. Therefore, it is established that the Muhrim's eating from his own slaughtered animal is among the prohibitions of Ihram, and committing a prohibition of Ihram necessitates compensation. Hence, upon him, the value of the eaten meat is obligatory as a guarantee. Unlike another Muhrim, because his eating is not among the prohibitions of his Ihram. So when eating from this slaughtered animal is not among the prohibitions of that other Muhrim, then no guarantee is obligatory upon him.)
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on an animal slaughtered by a Muhrim and the penalty if that Muhrim eats from it. The text first establishes that a Muhrim's slaughter is invalid: the animal becomes carrion (maytah), forbidden for all. The Quranic verse 'Do not kill game while in Ihram' indicates that the Muhrim's killing is considered 'qatl' (killing), not proper slaughter (dhabh). Consequently, the animal is like that slaughtered by a Magian, which is also invalid. The author then presents the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The Sahibayn argue that since the animal is carrion, eating it only requires istighfar (seeking forgiveness) and no monetary penalty, just as if another Muhrim ate it. Abu Hanifa, however, distinguishes that the prohibition has two dimensions: (1) the animal is carrion, and (2) it is a violation of the Muhrim's own Ihram prohibitions, because his Ihram caused the animal to lose its eligibility for valid slaughter. Therefore, the act of eating is attributed to his Ihram violation, which requires a penalty (the value of the meat). If another Muhrim eats, it is not attributed to that Muhrim's Ihram, so no penalty. The commentary further clarifies that if the Muhrim ate before paying the original compensation for the game (jaza' al-sayd), the value of the meat is subsumed; if after, it must be paid separately. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but both views are preserved in the school.

Key Terms
محرم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of Ihram for Hajj or Umrah, with all associated restrictions.
ذبیحہ (dhabīḥah): An animal that has been slaughtered in the prescribed Islamic manner.
میتہ (maytah): Carrion; an animal that died or was slaughtered in an invalid manner, making it impermissible to eat.
جزاء (jazā’): Compensation or penalty, particularly for violations of Ihram such as hunting or consuming game.
احرام (iḥrām): The sacred state entered for Hajj or Umrah, involving specific dress and prohibitions.
صید (ṣayd): Game, i.e., wild animals that are permissible to hunt and eat when not in Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is required of a Muhrim who eats from the animal he slaughtered while in Ihram?
A) Payment of the value of what he ate
B) Only seeking forgiveness (istighfar)
C) A penalty of one sheep
D) Nothing, because the meat is halal

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim's slaughter is invalid, making the animal carrion; the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the penalty for the slaughterer who eats turns on whether his eating is a separate Ihram violation.

Ruling on a Muhrim Eating Game Meat Slaughtered by a Halal
Inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik on Muhrim eating game meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for a Muhrim eating game meat and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the lam al-tamlik reinterpretation.

Core Idea
A Muhrim may eat game meat hunted by a non-Muhrim unless he indicated or ordered — intention of the hunter doesn't matter.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools on whether a Muhrim may eat game meat if a non-Muhrim hunted it specifically for him. The Hanafi position is clear: it is permissible as long as the Muhrim did not indicate the game or order the hunt. Imam Malik, however, prohibits it based on a literal reading of a hadith. The Hanafis respond by reinterpreting that hadith using linguistic tools, showing the depth of Hanafi usul al-fiqh in action.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that a Muhrim may eat game meat hunted by a non-Muhrim only if two conditions are met: no indication (dalalah) and no order. Otherwise, it is prohibited.
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam Malik prohibits the Muhrim from eating the meat if the non-Muhrim hunted it specifically for the Muhrim, even without indication or order.
Malik's view is based on a literal reading of the hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik cites the hadith: '...nor was it hunted for him' (la yusadu lahu). The literal meaning suggests prohibition when the hunt is done for the Muhrim.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reinterpret the lam in 'yusadu lahu' as lam al-tamlik (possession), meaning the whole animal is given as a gift, not just the meat. Alternatively, they restrict it to cases where the Muhrim commanded the hunt. The condition of no indication further clarifies.
This shows the Hanafi method of ta'wil (interpretation) based on linguistic principles.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Malik, if the hunter intended the game for the Muhrim, it is prohibited. Under Hanafi, it is allowed unless the Muhrim indicated or ordered.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

And there is no harm in a Muhrim eating the meat of game that a Halal (i.e., non-Muhrim) hunted and slaughtered, provided the Muhrim did not indicate it nor order its hunting, contrary to Malik in the case where he hunted it for the Muhrim. His evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no harm in the Muhrim eating the meat of game as long as he did not hunt it nor was it hunted for him.' Our evidence is what is narrated that the Companions discussed game meat concerning the Muhrim, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in it.' And the lam (in the narration) is the lam of possession, so it is interpreted as the game being given as a gift to him, not the meat, or its meaning is that it was hunted by his command. Then al-Quduri stipulated the condition of not indicating, and this is a specification that indicating is prohibited. The scholars said: there are two narrations on this issue. And the reason for prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada, which we have mentioned. Translation: And there is no harm that a Muhrim should eat the meat of game which a Halal, i.e., a non-Muhrim, hunted and slaughtered, provided that the Muhrim did not indicate it nor order its hunting. Imam Malik disagrees in the case where the Halal hunted it for the Muhrim. Imam Malik's evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in the Muhrim eating game meat provided he did not himself hunt it nor was it hunted for him.' And our evidence is that the Companions discussed eating game meat concerning the Muhrim, then the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no harm in it.' And the lam in the narration that Imam Malik narrated is the lam of possession, so the hadith will be interpreted that the game is given as a gift to the Muhrim, not the meat, or its meaning is that it is hunted by his command. Then al-Quduri stipulated not indicating, and this is a specification that indicating is prohibited. The scholars said: there are two narrations on this. And the reason for prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada, which we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding whether a Muhrim (person in Ihram) may eat game meat that was hunted and slaughtered by a Halal (non-Muhrim). The Hanafi position is that it is permissible provided two conditions are met: (1) the Muhrim did not indicate (dalalah) the game to the hunter, and (2) the Muhrim did not order the hunter to hunt it. Under these conditions, even if the hunter intended the game for the Muhrim, the Muhrim may eat it. The text explicitly notes the disagreement of Imam Malik in the case where the non-Muhrim hunted specifically for the Muhrim. Malik's proof is the hadith: '...nor was it hunted for him' (la yusadu lahu). The Hanafi response interprets that hadith: the lam in 'yusadu lahu' is the lam of possession (lam al-tamlik), meaning the entire game animal is given as a gift, not just the meat, or it refers to a scenario where the Muhrim commanded the hunt. Furthermore, the Hanafis rely on another hadith where the Companions discussed the matter and the Prophet (peace be upon him) simply said 'no harm'. The condition of no indication, stipulated by al-Quduri, reinforces that indicating game is prohibited. The commentary also notes that there are two narrations within the Hanafi school on the ruling of indicating, but the reason for prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada, which was previously mentioned (likely in an earlier section of the book). The overall Hanafi ruling is that as long as the Muhrim did not participate in or direct the hunt, the meat is halal for him.

Key Terms
حلال (ḥalāl): In this context, a person who is not in the state of Ihram, i.e., a non-Muhrim.
دلالت (dalālah): Indication; when a Muhrim points out game to a hunter or guides him to it.
لام تملیک (lām al-tamlīk): The letter 'lam' used to indicate ownership or possession, e.g., 'lahu' meaning 'for him' as possession.
صید (ṣayd): Game; wild animals that are permissible to hunt when not in Ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim may eat game meat hunted by a non-Muhrim as long as he did not indicate or order the hunt, even if the hunter intended it for him.

Compensation for a Muhrim Eating His Own Slaughtered Game
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for eating one's own slaughtered game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a muhrim who eats from his own slaughtered game must pay compensation, and distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A muhrim's eating from his own game is a double prohibition; the Sahibayn treat it as mere carrion.

When a person in ihram slaughters a game animal and eats from it before offering the fidyah, a debate arises among the Hanafi imams. Does he owe additional compensation for the meat he ate? This passage presents the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, illustrating how different understandings of the nature of the prohibition lead to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
State the specific situation: a muhrim slaughters a game animal while in ihram and eats from its meat before paying the penalty (jaza').
The act is both slaughtering and eating; the dispute focuses on the eating component.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that no compensation is due beyond seeking forgiveness (istighfar). They analogize to another muhrim eating from the same meat.
Their key proof: the animal is carrion, and eating carrion only requires istighfar.
3
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the muhrim must pay the value of the meat as a guarantee (daman). He distinguishes between the slaughterer and another muhrim.
His proof: the prohibition for the slaughterer is twofold – carrion and an ihram violation.
4
Analyze Each Side's Dalil
For the Sahibayn: the meat is carrion, and the same ruling applies to any eater. For Abu Hanifa: the slaughterer's eating is an additional violation of ihram prohibitions, which incurs a penalty.
The difference hinges on whether the ihram adds a separate prohibition for the slaughterer alone.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the muhrim must pay the meat's value; under the Sahibayn, no payment is required.
The passage does not specify which view is mufta bihi, so both remain transmitted.

ادا کرنے سے پہلے کھایا ہے تو کھائے ہوئے گوشت کی قیمت کا جزائے صید میں تداخل ہو جائے گا الگ سے ادا کرنے کی قطعاً ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس پر علاوہ استغفار کے قیمت وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اگر اس ذبیحہ میں سے کسی دوسرے محرم نے کچھ کھا لیا تو ان سب کے نزدیک اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرم کا یہ ذبیحہ مردار ہے اور مردار کے کھانے سے کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا علاوہ استغفار کے اس لئے محرم پر استغفار کے سوا کوئی تاوان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ اس میں سے ذیح کرنے والے کے علاوہ دوسرے محرم نے کھا لیا ہو۔ پس جس طرح دوسرے محرم کے کھانے سے اس پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا ، اسی طرح اس ذبح کرنے والے محرم کے کھانے سے بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرم کے ذبیحہ کی حرمت دو اعتبار سے ہے۔ ایک تو اس لئے کہ اس کا ذبیحہ مردار ہے جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے۔ اور دوسرے اس لئے کہ یہ بچہ احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے احرام ہی نے شکار کے جانور کو محل ذبح ہونے سے نکال دیا اور اس نے محرم کو ذبح کا اہل ہونے سے نکال دیا ہے۔ پس ان واسطوں سے اس ذبیحہ کی حرمت اس کے احرام کی طرف منسوب ہوگی۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ محرم کا اپنے ذبیحہ میں سے کھانا احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے ہے اور احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے کسی ممنوع کا ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر اس کھائے ہوئے گوشت کی قیمت بطور ضمان واجب ہو گی۔ برخلاف دوسرے محرم کے کیونکہ اس کا کھانا اس کے احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہے۔ پس جب اس ذبیحہ میں سے کھانا اس دوسرے محرم کے ممنوعات میں سے نہیں ہے تو اس پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
If he ate before performing (the sacrifice), then the value of the meat eaten will be included in the penalty for the game; there is absolutely no need to offer it separately. And the Sahibayn said that nothing besides seeking forgiveness is obligatory upon him. And if another muhrim ate from this slaughtered animal, then according to all of them nothing is obligatory upon him. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the muhrim's slaughtered animal is carrion, and eating carrion does not require any compensation besides seeking forgiveness; therefore no compensation besides seeking forgiveness is obligatory upon the muhrim. And this is like when another muhrim, other than the one who slaughtered, ate from it. So just as no guarantee is obligatory upon the other muhrim for eating, similarly no guarantee is obligatory upon this slaughtering muhrim for his eating. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that the prohibition of the muhrim's slaughtered animal is from two considerations: one, because his slaughter is carrion as we have mentioned; and second, because this is among the prohibitions of ihram. Indeed, his ihram removed the game animal from being permissible to slaughter and removed the muhrim from being eligible to slaughter. So through these means, the prohibition of this slaughtered animal is attributed to his ihram. Thus it is established that the muhrim's eating from his own slaughtered animal is among the prohibitions of ihram, and committing any prohibited act of ihram necessitates a penalty. Therefore, the value of the meat he ate is obligatory upon him as a guarantee. Contrary to another muhrim, because his eating is not among the prohibitions of his ihram. So when eating from this slaughtered animal is not among the prohibitions of that other muhrim, no guarantee is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding a muhrim who, while in the state of ihram, slaughters a game animal and then eats from it before performing the required fidyah. The Sahibayn argue that the slaughtered animal is carrion, and eating carrion only requires repentance, not monetary compensation. They draw an analogy to another muhrim eating from the same meat: no compensation is due from him, so the slaughterer should be treated similarly. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes the two cases: the prohibition for the slaughterer is twofold — the meat is carrion, and the act of slaughtering itself is a violation of ihram. Thus, his eating is an additional violation of ihram prohibitions, which triggers a penalty. For another muhrim, only the first prohibition (carrion) applies, so no penalty. Hence, Abu Hanifa holds that the value of the meat is due as a guarantee. The passage does not specify which position is mufta bihi, but it reflects the classical disagreement recorded in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
ضمان (daman): Monetary compensation or guarantee due for violating prohibitions of ihram by consuming game.
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation for hunting or consuming game while in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why does a muhrim who slaughters game and eats from it owe compensation?
A) Because the slaughterer's eating is a double violation: the meat is carrion and the act is a breach of ihram prohibitions.
B) Because the slaughterer has more money.
C) Because the other muhrim did not slaughter the animal.
D) Because the slaughterer must make up for the loss of the animal.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa requires compensation for a muhrim eating his own game; Sahibayn do not, based on whether the act is merely carrion or also an ihram violation.

Muhrim Eating Game Hunted by a Non-Muhrim: Dispute with Malik
Inter-madhhab dispute on permissibility for muhrim to eat game hunted by a non-muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a muhrim eating game hunted by a non-muhrim, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the lam al-tamlik interpretation.

Core Idea
Hanafi school permits a muhrim to eat game hunted by a non-muhrim, even if intended for him, as long as he did not guide or command.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam Malik regarding the permissibility of a muhrim consuming game hunted by a non-muhrim. Both schools rely on the same hadith but interpret it differently based on a grammatical nuance. Understanding this dispute deepens your appreciation of how usul al-fiqh shapes deriving rulings from textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
Identify the ruling and the two conditions (no guidance, no command) that make it permissible.
2
Identify the opposing Maliki position and its evidence
State the Maliki view that the muhrim cannot eat game hunted for him, and quote the hadith they use.
3
Analyze the hadith text and the role of the lam
Compare the two interpretations: Maliki reads the lam literally; Hanafi reads it as lam al-tamlik (possession).
Focus on the phrase 'yuṣāda lahu'.
4
Explain the Hanafi response and two alternative interpretations
Describe the two ways Hanafis explain the hadith: (1) the live animal is gifted, not the meat; (2) it means hunted by his command.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Conclude that in practice, Hanafis impose no compensation; Malikis require compensation for game hunted for the muhrim.

اس بارے میں مذاکرہ کر رہے تھے کہ محرم کے لئے دوسرے کسی غیر محرم کے کئے ہوئے شکار کا کھانا کیسا ہے۔ اس بحث میں کچھ آوازیں بلند ہو گئیں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنے حجرہ میں سوئے ہوئے تھے ۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیدار ہو کر فرمایا کہ کس چیز میں جھگڑ رہے ہو۔ صحابہ نے پورا واقعہ ذکر کیا تو رسولِ خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لا بأس به یعنی اس کے کھانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ امام مالک کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اُو يُصَادَ لَهُ میں لام تملیک کا ہے۔ اب ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ محرم کے لئے ایسے شکار کا گوشت کھانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے جس کو نہ تو خود شکار کیا ہو یا شکار کر کے زندہ شکار کا مالک اس کو بنا دیا ہو یعنی اگر غیر محرم نے شکار کر کے زندہ جانور محرم کو ہدیہ کر دیا تو بھی محرم کے لئے اس کا کھانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر گوشت ہدیہ کیا تو اسکے کھانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں نہ ہو سکے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری نے دلالت نہ کرنا شرط فرمایا ہے اور یہ شرط اس بات پر بصراحت دلالت کرتی ہے کہ اگر محرم نے غیر محرم کو شکار کی طرف دلالت کی تو محرم کے لئے یہ شکار حرام ہوگا۔ لیکن مشائخ متأخرین نے فرمایا ہے محرم کے دلالت کرنے کی صورت میں دور وایتیں ہیں ۔ ایک روایت تو یہ ہے کہ محرم کے لئے اس شکار میں سے کھانا حرام ہے اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ حرام نہیں ہے۔ پہلی روایت امام طحاوی کی ہے اور دوسری روایت ابو عبد اللہ جبر جانی کی ہے۔ حرمت والی روایت کی وجہ ابو قتادہ کی حدیث هَل عَنتُم هَلْ دَلَلْتُمْ هَلْ أَشَرتُم ہے۔ یہ روایت اول باب احترام میں با بالتفصیل آچکی ہے۔
And there is no harm in a muhrim eating the meat of game which a halal (non-muhrim) hunted and slaughtered, provided the muhrim did not guide him to it nor command him to hunt it, contrary to Malik in the case where he hunted it for the sake of the muhrim. His (the Prophet's) statement: 'There is no harm in a muhrim eating the meat of game as long as he did not hunt it nor was it hunted for him.' And our proof is what is narrated that the Companions discussed the meat of game concerning the muhrim, and he said: 'There is no harm in it.' And the lam in what is narrated is a lam of possession, so it is interpreted as gifting the live game to him, not the meat, or its meaning is that it is hunted by his command. Then (al-Quduri) conditioned the absence of guidance, and this is a clear indication that guidance is prohibited. They said there are two narrations regarding it, and the basis of prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada, which we have mentioned. Translation: And there is no harm that a muhrim eats the meat of game which a halal (non-muhrim) hunted and slaughtered, provided the muhrim did not guide him to it nor command him to hunt it. Imam Malik differs in the case where the halal hunted it for the muhrim. Imam Malik's evidence is the hadith: 'There is no harm in a muhrim eating the meat of game as long as he did not hunt it nor was it hunted for him.' Our evidence is that once the Companions discussed the matter, and the Prophet said: 'There is no harm in it.' And the lam in the hadith narrated by Malik is a lam of possession, so the hadith is interpreted as gifting the live game to him, not the meat, or its meaning is that it is hunted by his command. Then al-Quduri conditioned the absence of guidance, and this is a clear indication that guidance is prohibited. The later scholars said there are two narrations regarding this, and the basis of prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada, which we have mentioned at length earlier.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding a muhrim eating game hunted by a non-muhrim. The Hanafi position: it is permissible (no harm) provided the muhrim did not guide the hunter to the game nor command him to hunt. Imam Malik holds that if the non-muhrim hunted specifically for the muhrim, even without the muhrim's request, then the muhrim is liable. Both sides use hadith evidence. The Hanafi response to Malik's hadith (the 'lam' in 'yuṣāda lahu') is that it means 'hunted and given as a gift alive' or 'hunted by his command', not merely hunted for his benefit. The text then notes that guidance (dalalah) by the muhrim is clearly prohibited according to al-Quduri, but later scholars (muta’akhkhirun) report two narrations: one declaring it forbidden (based on Abu Qatada's hadith), and one not. The first is from Imam al-Tahawi, the second from Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani.

Key Terms
حلال (halal): A person not in the state of ihram.
دلالت (dalalah): Guiding or indicating the location of game to a hunter.
لام تملیک (lam al-tamlik): The letter lam indicating transfer of ownership, as in 'for him' meaning 'given to him as property'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a muhrim eats game that a non-muhrim hunted specifically for him, without the muhrim's guidance or command?
A) It is permissible and no compensation is due.
B) It is prohibited and compensation is due.
C) It is permissible only if the muhrim repents.
D) It is prohibited but no compensation is due.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a muhrim to eat game hunted by a non-muhrim as long as the muhrim neither guided nor commanded, using the lam al-tamlik interpretation to restrict the apparent general prohibition.

Halal Slaughtering Game within the Haram: Dispute with Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on penalty for a non-muhrim slaughtering game in the Haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between the penalty for a non-muhrim and a muhrim hunting in the Haram, and evaluate Imam Zufar's counter-argument.

Core Idea
The penalty for a non-muhrim hunting in the Haram is a financial guarantee, not personal expiation—fasting cannot substitute.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the penalty when a non-muhrim (halal) slaughters game within the Haram. The majority position holds that only the market value of the game must be given in charity, and that fasting is not a valid substitute. Imam Zufar disagrees, analogizing the case to a muhrim's penalty. The key legal distinction lies in whether the obligation arises from a quality of the place (amn) or from a personal state (ihram).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that the market value of the game must be given to the poor; fasting does not suffice. This is a financial guarantee (gharamah).
The ruling is wajib.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar holds that fasting is an acceptable substitute, based on analogy to the muhrim, where fasting is allowed.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Zufar's evidence is qiyas: if a muhrim can fast as expiation for hunting, then a non-muhrim should similarly be allowed to fast.
The opposing school here is a minority within Hanafism.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi majority distinguishes: the muhrim's penalty is a personal kaffarah for violating ihram (an action), so an act of worship like fasting can compensate. The non-muhrim's penalty is for destroying the Haram's attribute of safety (amn), which is a property-like loss; therefore only monetary compensation works.
The key distinction: gharamah (property assurance) vs. kaffarah (personal expiation).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under the Hanafi position, only cash charity is acceptable; under Zufar's view, fasting suffices. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the Hanafi majority.
Zufar's view is recorded but not adopted in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي صَيدِ الْحَرَمِ إِذَا ذَبَحَهُ الْحَلَالُ تَجِبُ قِيمَتُهُ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِهَا عَلَى الْفُقَرَاءِ لِأَنَّ الصَّيْدَ اسْتَحَقَ الْأُمِّن بِسَبَبِ الْحَرَمِ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثٍ فِيهِ طُولُ وَلَا يَنفَر صَيدُهَا وَلَا يُجْزِيهِ الصَّوْمُ لِأَنَّهَا غَرَامَةً وَلَيْسَتْ يكَفَّارَة فَأَشَبَهَ ضِمَانَ الْأَمْوَالِ وَهذَا لِأَنَّهُ يَجِبُ بِتَفْوِيتِ وَصْفِ فِى الْمَحَلِ وَهُوَ الْأَمَنُ وَالْوَاجِبُ عَلَى الْمُحْرِمِ بِطَرِيْقِ الْكَفَّارَةِ جَرَاء عَلَى فِعْلِهِ لِأَنَّ الْحُرَمَةِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَعْنَى فِيْهِ وَهُوَ إِحْرَامُهُ وَالصَّوْمُ يُصْلِحُ جَزَاء الْاَفْعَالِ لأَصَمَانَ المَحَالِ وَ قَالَ زُفَةٌ يُجْزِيْهِ الصَّوْمُ اِعْتِبَارًا بِمَا وَجَبَ عَلَى المُحْرِمِ وَالْفَرْقُ قَدْ ذَكَرَنَا وَهَلْ يُجْزِيْهِ الْهَدَى فَفِيْهِ رَوَايَتَانِ ترجمہ اور حرم کے شکار میں جب اس کو حلال ذبح کرے تو اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی جس کو فقیروں پر تقسیم کرے۔ کیونکہ حرم کی وجہ
And regarding the game of the Haram, when a halal (non-muhrim) slaughters it, its value is obligatory, to be given in charity to the poor, because the game has earned safety due to the Haram. He (the Prophet) said in a lengthy hadith: 'And its game shall not be hunted.' And fasting does not suffice for it because it is a financial guarantee (gharamah) and not a kaffarah, so it resembles the guarantee of property. And this is because it becomes obligatory due to the loss of a quality in the locus, namely safety (amn). And the obligation upon the muhrim is by way of kaffarah as a penalty for his action, because the prohibition is due to a meaning within him, namely his ihram. And fasting is suitable as a penalty for actions but not for the loss of a quality of a place (mahal). And Zufar said: fasting suffices for him, by analogy to what is obligatory upon the muhrim. And we have mentioned the distinction. And does the gift of a sacrificial animal (hady) suffice for him? There are two narrations regarding it. Translation: And in the game of the Haram, when a halal slaughters it, its value is obligatory, to be distributed to the poor, because of the Haram (reason).
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a non-muhrim (halal) slaughters game within the boundaries of the Haram (sanctuary of Makkah). The Hanafi position: the full market value of the game must be given in charity to the poor. This is because the Haram grants the game a right of safety (amn), and slaughtering it violates that right. The penalty is a financial guarantee (gharamah), not an expiatory offering (kaffarah). Therefore, fasting (sawm) is not acceptable as a substitute, unlike in cases where a muhrim hunts, where fasting can be a substitute. The reason: the obligation in this case is due to destroying a quality of the place (the sanctuary's sanctity), not due to a personal act requiring expiation. Imam Zufar disagrees, holding that fasting is acceptable, analogizing it to the muhrim's situation. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the muhrim's penalty is for his personal violation of ihram (an act), while here the penalty is for destroying the sanctuary's attribute of safety (a property-like loss). The text then mentions two narrations regarding whether offering a hady (sacrificial animal) suffices; details are not given here.

Key Terms
حرم (haram): The sacred sanctuary of Makkah with its boundaries where hunting is prohibited for everyone.
غرمہ (gharamah): A financial penalty or compensation for causing loss, distinct from expiatory offering.
أمن (amn): The state of safety granted to game within the Haram, which is violated by hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school not allow fasting as a substitute for the penalty when a non-muhrim slaughters game in the Haram?
A) Because the penalty is a financial guarantee for destroying the sanctuary's attribute of safety, not a personal expiation.
B) Because the non-muhrim is not in ihram.
C) Because the game belongs to the state.
D) Because fasting is only valid for intentional sins.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the penalty for a non-muhrim hunting in the Haram is a financial guarantee, not a personal expiation; fasting cannot substitute.

Muhrim Eating Game Hunted by Non-Muhrim: Hanafi vs. Maliki
Dispute between Hanafi and Maliki on Muhrim eating game hunted by non-Muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on a Muhrim eating game hunted by a non-Muhrim and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using dalil analysis.

Core Idea
No liability if no indication or command; Maliki view of intent rejected by grammatical reinterpretation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a classic fiqh dispute: Is a Muhrim liable for eating game hunted by a non-Muhrim? The Hanafi school holds that without indication or command, there is no penalty. The Maliki school argues that if the hunt was intended for the Muhrim, liability applies. Understanding the evidence and its interpretation is essential for distinguishing between valid scholarly difference and methodological error.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
Identify the ruling: permissible (mubah) and no compensation if the Muhrim did not indicate or command the hunt. Note that indication (dalalat) is a debated condition among later Hanafi scholars.
The Zahir al-Riwayah position is clear: no dam without indication or command.
2
Identify the Maliki position and its evidential basis
Imam Malik holds that if the non-Muhrim intended the hunt for the Muhrim, liability attaches regardless of command. His evidence is a hadith that seems to forbid game hunted for the Muhrim.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Maliki proof
The Hanafi response offers two reinterpretations: (1) the lam in 'la yusadu lahu' is for tamlik (ownership), so it refers to a gifted live animal, not meat; (2) it means the hunt was not done by the Muhrim's command. Both interpretations neutralise the Maliki proof.
This is a classic example of muaradah (counter-evidence) and ta'wil (interpretive deflection).
4
Examine the Hanafi own evidence and its strength
The Hanafi school relies on a separate hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'La ba'sa bihi' (no harm) when asked about eating game hunted by a non-Muhrim. This hadith directly supports permissibility.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on indication
Later mashayikh differ: Imam Tahawi holds indication makes it prohibited; Abu Abdullah al-Jarjani holds it remains permissible. The Hidayah and later tarjih tend toward prohibition when indication is present.
This shows that even within a school, subsidiary points may have ikhtilaf.

Source Text

پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمايا ہے کہ اگر غير محرم نے محرم کے لئے شکار کيا بایں طور کہ اس نے يہ نيت کی کہ شکار کر کے محرم کو کھلاؤں گا تو ايسی صورت ميں اگر محرم نے کھايا تو اسپر اس اس نے شکار کيا ہو اور نہ اس کے لئے شکار کيا گيا ہو ۔ اس حديث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر محرم کے لئے شکار کيا گيا ہو تو محرم کو اس ميں سے کھانا بھی جائز نہيں ہے۔ ہماری دليل يہ ہے کہ ايک بار صحابہ اس بارے ميں مذاکرہ کر رہے تھے کہ محرم کے لئے دوسرے کسی غير محرم کے کئے ہوئے شکار کا کھانا کيسا ہے۔ اس بحث ميں کچھ آوازیں بلند ہو گئيں اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اپنے حجرہ ميں سوئے ہوئے تھے ۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بيدار ہو کر فرمايا کہ کس چيز ميں جھگڑ رہے ہو۔ صحابہ نے پورا واقعہ ذکر کيا تو رسولِ خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمايا لا بأس به يعنی اس کے کھانے ميں کوئی مضائقہ نہيں ہے۔ امام مالک کی طرف سے پيش کردہ حديث کا جواب يہ ہے کہ اُو يُصَادَ لَهُ ميں لام تمليک کا ہے۔ اب ترجمہ يہ ہوگا کہ محرم کے لئے ايسے شکار کا گوشت کھانے ميں کوئی مضائقہ نہيں ہے جس کو نہ تو خود شکار کيا ہو يا شکار کر کے زندہ شکار کا گی۔ صاحب ہدايہ فرما تے ہيں کہ قدوری نے دلالت نہ کرنا شرط فرمايا ہے اور يہ شرط اس بات پر بصراحت دلالت کرتی ہے کہ اگر محرم نے غير محرم کو شکار کی طرف دلالت کی تو محرم کے لئے يہ شکار حرام ہوگا۔ ليکن مشائخ متأخرين نے فرمايا ہے محرم کے دلالت کرنے کی صورت ميں دو روايتیں ہيں ۔ ايک روايت تو يہ ہے کہ محرم کے لئے اس شکار ميں سے کھانا حرام ہے اور دوسری روايت يہ ہے کہ حرام نہيں ہے۔ پہلی روايت امام طحاوی کی ہے اور دوسری روايت ابو عبد اللہ جبر جانی کی ہے۔ حرمت والی روايت کی وجہ ابو قتادہ کی حديث هَلْ عَنْتُمْ هَلْ دَلَلْتُمْ هَلْ أَشَرْتُمْ ہے۔ يہ روايت اول باب احترام ميں با بالتفصيل آچکی ہے۔
Explanation of the issue: If a non-Muhrim hunted and slaughtered, and the Muhrim did not indicate or command the hunt, then according to us if the Muhrim ate the meat, no compensation is obligatory on that Muhrim. Imam Malik said: If a non-Muhrim hunted for the Muhrim intending to feed him, then if the Muhrim ate, compensation for the meat eaten is obligatory, whether the Muhrim commanded the hunt or not. Imam Malik's evidence is the hadith: 'There is no harm in eating game whose meat was neither hunted by him nor hunted for him.' This hadith indicates that if game is hunted for the Muhrim, it is not permissible for him to eat. Our evidence is that once the Companions were discussing this matter, voices rose, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) awoke from his chamber and said: 'What are you arguing about?' They told him, and he said: 'La ba'sa bihi' (there is no harm in eating it). The response to Imam Malik's hadith is that the lam in 'la yusadu lahu' is for ownership. So the meaning is: there is no harm in eating game that he neither hunted himself nor owned the live animal after hunting; i.e., if the non-Muhrim gifted a live animal to the Muhrim, it is not permissible. But if he gifted meat, there is no harm. Or the meaning is that the hunt was not done by the Muhrim's command, because if done by his command, it is not permissible. With these interpretations, the hadith cannot be used as evidence for Imam Malik. The author of Hidayah says: Quduri stipulated not indicating, and this condition clearly indicates that if the Muhrim indicated the game to the non-Muhrim, the game becomes prohibited for the Muhrim. However, the later mashayikh said there are two narrations regarding indication: one that it is prohibited, the other that it is not prohibited. The first is from Imam Tahawi, the second from Abu Abdullah al-Jarjani. The reason for the prohibition is the hadith of Abu Qatada: 'Hal 'antum hal dalaltum hal ashartum?' This has been detailed in the first chapter.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a key inter-madhhab dispute on whether a Muhrim is liable for eating game hunted by a non-Muhrim. The Hanafi position is clear: if the Muhrim did not indicate or command the hunt, he incurs no liability. Imam Malik imposes liability if the hunt was specifically intended for the Muhrim, regardless of command. The text provides the Maliki evidence (a hadith that seems to forbid eating game hunted for the Muhrim) and the Hanafi response (another hadith and reinterpretation of the Maliki hadith). The Hanafi reinterpretation focuses on the grammatical nuance of 'la yusadu lahu' – taking the lam as tamlik (ownership) rather than ajl (for the sake of). This effectively neutralizes the Maliki proof. The passage also notes a later intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf among the mashayikh regarding the ruling when the Muhrim merely indicates the game, with two narrations (prohibition from Imam Tahawi, permissibility from Abu Abdullah al-Jarjani). The weightier narration is not declared here, but the earlier Hidayah text (from Quduri) takes the view that indication makes it prohibited.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Compensation or liability, specifically the penalty (dam) for violating ihram restrictions.
دلالت (dalalat): Indication: when the Muhrim points to or signals the game to the non-Muhrim, facilitating the hunt.
لام تمليک (lam tamlik): The preposition 'lam' used to indicate ownership or transfer of ownership, as opposed to 'lam ajl' (for the sake of).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a Muhrim not liable for eating game hunted by a non-Muhrim?
A) When the non-Muhrim intended the hunt for the Muhrim.
B) When the Muhrim did not indicate or command the hunt.
C) When the hunt took place outside the Haram.
D) When the Muhrim did not participate in the hunt.

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim can eat game hunted by a non-Muhrim without penalty only if he neither commanded nor indicated the hunt; the Maliki focus on the hunter's intent is rejected in Hanafi fiqh.

Ruling on Slaughtering Game in the Haram by a Non-Muhrim
Obligation of paying value for game killed in Haram and distinction from ihram violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a non-Muhrim who kills game in the Haram, explain why it is a financial liability (gharamah) and not a personal expiation (kaffarah), and distinguish the majority view from that of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Killing game in the Haram as a non-Muhrim creates a financial debt, not a personal expiation; fasting cannot substitute.

This lesson addresses a specific case: a person who is not in the state of ihram kills game within the sacred precinct of the Haram. The Hanafi school imposes a financial obligation—payment of the animal's market value—rather than a personal expiation like fasting. The reasoning hinges on the concept of security (amn) that the Haram grants to all creatures. We will explore the textual proof, the distinction from a Muhrim's violation, and an important intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
First, note who is doing the act (non-Muhrim) and where (in the Haram). The ruling: the value of the game must be paid in charity. This is a wajib financial liability, not a kaffarah.
The ruling is from the matn of al-Quduri and al-Hidayah.
2
Examine the dalil and its implication
The proof is a hadith prohibiting even chasing away game of the Haram. The prohibition implies that killing is a greater violation, and compensation is required for destroying the quality of security (amn) that the Haram provides. This makes it a financial matter.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Contrast with the Muhrim's case
In the Muhrim's case, the obligation is a kaffarah for his own action (violating ihram), so fasting can substitute. For the non-Muhrim, the obligation is for damaging the Haram's sanctity in the subject (the game), which is a financial loss, so only wealth compensates.
This distinction answers why a Muhrim killing game in the Haram only pays one kaffarah (the stronger sanctity of ihram subsumes the Haram's).
4
Note the ikhtilaf and its thamarah
Imam Zufar (and Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) analogize to the Muhrim and permit fasting. The Hanafi majority rejects this analogy. The practical difference: a poor non-Muhrim must pay value under the mufta bihi view; he cannot fast.
The text mentions two narrations on whether hady suffices; the mufta bihi is unclear but the stronger view likely requires value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
