Liability for Releasing a Muhrim's Game: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on daman for releasing muhrim's game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on daman for releasing a muhrim's game, explain each proof, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A muhrim's ownership of game caught while halal persists; releasing it is destroying property, not mere non-interference.

The Sahibayn argue that releasing the game is a good deed that absolves liability; Abu Hanifa insists on property rights. This dispute hinges on the precise obligation of a muhrim: is it only to refrain from interfering, or also to divest ownership? Let's follow the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and two positions
The subject is a muhrim who caught game while halal, then another person releases that game. What is the ruling on the releaser's liability? State the two opinions: Abu Hanifa (liable) and Sahibayn (not liable).
Note that the game was lawfully owned before ihram.
2
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the Quranic verse 'There is no blame on the righteous' (9:91) and argue the releaser did a good deed by helping the muhrim avoid sin. The releaser is thus not liable.
This is a dalil naqli (Quranic) supporting the view.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the muhrim's ownership is valid and persists after ihram. Releasing the game destroys that owned property, which generally incurs daman. This is supported by qiyas: destroying another's property requires compensation.
The key distinction: the muhrim's obligation is tarak al-ta'arud (refraining from interference), not removal of ownership. The releaser committed ta'addi.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The text raises an objection: since the muhrim had to avoid the game, the releaser merely did what was required. The response: the muhrim could have kept the game in his house without interference. The releaser ended possession, a transgressions.
The analogy of breaking musical instruments illustrates that even if the item is sinful, the material value is compensable.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the releaser must pay the value of the game. Under Sahibayn, no payment. This affects actual transactions during hajj.
The text does not give a mufta bihi, but the qiyas and response suggest Abu Hanifa's view is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج نہ ہوگا ، کیونکہ اس نے نیک کام کیا ہے اور نیکو کاروں کے حق میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَمَا عَلَى الْمُحْسِنِينَ مِنْ سَبِيل (التوبة: 91) اور نیکوکاروں پر کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی جو لوگ نیک کام کرنے والے ہیں ان پر گرفت و مواخذہ کچھ نہیں ہے ، پس وہ دنیا میں ضامن نہ ہوگا اور آخرت میں عذاب سے محفوظ ہوگا۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص جواب محرم ہے اس نے حلال ہونے کی حالت میں اس شکار کو پکڑ کر اس کی ملک محترم حاصل کی تھی یعنی جب اس نے یہ شکار پکڑا تو اس وقت یہ حلال تھا پس اس ملک کا محترم ہونا اس کے احرام باندھنے کی وجہ سے باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بالا تفاق ابھی ملک بدستور موجود ہے اب اس چھڑانے والے نے شکار کو رہا کر کے اس کی ملک محترم کو تلف کر دیا اور کسی کی مملوکہ چیز کو تلف کرنے سے تلف کر نیوالا اس چیز کا ضامن ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس چھڑانے والے پر اس کا ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب کہ شکار کو حالت احرام میں پکڑا ہو کیونکہ محرم اس کو پکڑنے سے اسکا مالک ہی نہیں ہوا اور جب مالک نہیں ہوا تو چھڑانے والا ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے محرم کی چیز تلف نہیں کی ہے۔ وَالْوَاجِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَرُكُ التَّعَرُّض سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ جب اس نے حالت حلال میں شکار پکڑا تو یہ اس کا مالک ہو گیا لیکن احرام باندھنے کے بعد ترک تعرض کی خاطر اس کو اپنے ملک سے نکالنا ضروری تھا حالانکہ اس نے اپنی ملک سے نہیں نکالا بلکہ دوسرے نے اس کو چھڑا کر اس کی ملک سے نکال دیا تو اس مرسل پر ضمان واجب ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ جو کام محرم کو کرنا چاہئے تھا اس نے وہی کام کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ محترم پر شکار کے ساتھ تعرض ترک کرنا واجب تھا اپنی ملک سے نکالنا واجب نہ تھا اور ترک تعرض محرم کی ملک میں باقی رہتے ہوئے بھی ممکن تھا، بایں طور کہ محرم اس شکار کو اپنے گھر میں چھوڑ دیتا اس صورت میں ترک تعرض بھی ہو جاتا اور محرم کی ملک بھی برابر رہ جاتی مگر جب دوسرے آدمی نے محرم کا قبضہ اس سے ختم کر دیا تو یہ چھڑانے والا تعدی کرنے والا ہوا اور تعدی کرنے والے پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی دوسرے آدمی کے لہو و لعب کے آلات توڑ دیئے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک ضامن ہوگا مگر اس آلہ طنبورہ وغیرہ کے حساب سے ضامن نہ ہوگا بلکہ تراشی ہوئی لکڑی کے حساب سے ضامن ہوگا۔
Will not be liable, because he did a good deed, and regarding the righteous, Allah Almighty said: 'There is no blame on the righteous' (At-Tawbah 91). And there is no path against the righteous, meaning that those who do good deeds are not subject to any accountability or punishment, so he will not be liable in this world and will be safe from punishment in the Hereafter.
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that this person is now a muhrim; he had captured this game while in a state of halal and obtained its respected ownership. That is, when he caught this game, he was halal, so the inviolability of this ownership will not become invalid due to his entering ihram because, by consensus, the ownership still remains. Now, the releaser released the game and destroyed its respected ownership, and whoever destroys someone else's owned property is liable for it. Therefore, this releaser must guarantee it. Contrary to when the game was caught while in ihram, because the muhrim did not become its owner by catching it, and when he is not the owner, the releaser is not liable either because he did not destroy the muhrim's property.
And the phrase 'the wajib upon him is to refrain from interference' answers a question. The question is: We admit that when he caught the game while halal, he became its owner, but after entering ihram, it was necessary to remove it from his ownership in order to refrain from interference. However, he did not remove it from his ownership; rather, someone else released it and removed it from his ownership. So this releaser should be liable because he did exactly what the muhrim was supposed to do. The answer is that the muhrim was only obligated to refrain from interference with the game, not to remove it from his ownership. And refraining from interference was possible while the game remained in his ownership, such as by leaving it in his house. In that case, both refraining from interference would be achieved and his ownership would remain. But when another person terminated the muhrim's possession, this releaser became a transgressor, and the transgressor is liable for guarantee. Therefore, he will be liable. An analogy: if someone breaks another's instruments of entertainment and play, according to the Sahibayn he is liable, but not for the value of the instrument (like a tambourine) as such, but for the value of carved wood.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a muhrim who captured game while he was halal (not in ihram), and then another person released that game from his hand. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the releaser is not liable because his action was a good deed (ihsan) in enabling the muhrim to avoid sin, and Allah says there is no blame on the righteous. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the releaser is liable because the muhrim had valid ownership of the game (since he caught it while halal), and entering ihram does not invalidate that ownership. Releasing it amounts to destroying someone else's property, so the releaser must guarantee its value. The commentary then addresses an objection: if the muhrim was obliged to avoid interference with the game after ihram, and the releaser did that, why is the releaser liable? The response is that the obligation was to refrain from interference (tarak al-ta'arud), not to remove ownership. The muhrim could have kept the game in his house without interference. By releasing it, the other person committed a transgression (ta'addi) by ending the muhrim's possession, thus becoming liable. An analogy follows: breaking someone's musical instruments; the Sahibayn hold the breaker liable for the value of the wood, not the instrument's value as a whole, because the instrument itself is sinful property (lahw wa la'b). This illustrates that liability can be for the material value even if the object is not valued as property in itself.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, to whom hunting is prohibited.
ضمان (daman): Liability to pay compensation for damage or destruction of property.
ترک تعرض (tarak al-ta'arud): Refraining from interference or molestation with the game, i.e., not hunting or capturing it.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression, wrongful act that causes harm and incurs liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Hanifa hold the releaser liable while the Sahibayn do not?
A) Abu Hanifa focuses on the good deed; Sahibayn focus on property rights.
B) Abu Hanifa holds the releaser committed ta'addi by destroying owned property; Sahibayn see only ihsan.
C) Both agree the releaser is liable, but differ on the amount.
D) The Sahibayn rely on qiyas; Abu Hanifa relies on Quran.

Key Takeaway
The dispute hinges on whether the muhrim's obligation is merely to refrain from interference or to also divest ownership; Abu Hanifa's view that ownership persists leads to liability for the releaser.

6 min
No Liability for Releasing Game from a Muhrim's Hand
Establishing the ruling by consensus that a releaser is not liable when a muhrim caught game while in ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a muhrim's caught game is released, and explain the scriptural and analogical evidence.

Core Idea
A muhrim never owns game caught in ihram; releasing it incurs no liability.

Imagine a pilgrim in ihram catches a rabbit. Another person, seeing this, sets it free. Should that person compensate the pilgrim? Common sense might say yes, because the pilgrim caught it first. But Hanafi fiqh says no, by consensus. Why? Because the pilgrim never owned the rabbit in the first place. This lesson unpacks that logic using Quranic evidence and a powerful analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is: a muhrim catches game (sayd) while in ihram, and another person releases it from his hand. The ruling is that the releaser is not liable (la daman) for compensation. This is established by consensus (bil-ittifaq) among the Hanafi imams.
Consensus here means the agreement of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Zufar.
2
Locate the Primary Proof (Dalil Naqli)
The primary proof is the Quranic verse: 'حُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا' (Forbidden to you is hunting of land as long as you are in ihram, Al-Ma'idah 5:96). This verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah. It establishes that game is completely prohibited for the muhrim.
The prohibition is absolute; it does not merely restrict hunting but also prevents ownership.
3
Derive the Legal Implication (Wajh al-Dalalah)
The prohibition (hurmat) means the game is no longer a valid subject of ownership (milk) for the muhrim. Since ownership requires lawful acquisition, and hunting is unlawful, the muhrim does not become owner by capturing the game. Therefore, releasing it does not destroy the muhrim's property—because he never had any.
This is different from a non-muhrim catching game: they can own it.
4
Analyze the Qiyas (Analogy)
The text draws an analogy: the situation is like a Muslim buying wine. Wine is haram li-dhatihi (inherently forbidden), so a Muslim cannot own it. If someone destroys the wine after purchase, the buyer has no claim because he never became owner. Similarly, game for the muhrim is haram li-dhatihi due to the verse, so ownership is impossible.
The analogy highlights that prohibition of the substance itself prevents ownership, unlike cases where prohibition is due to external factors (haram li-ghayrihi).
5
Confirm the Consensus and Authority
The Hanafi school unanimously holds this ruling (it is from Zahir al-Riwayah). There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The ruling is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The consensus strengthens its authority.
Outside the Hanafi school, there may be differences, but within the school it is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محرم کے ہاتھ سے کسی نے شکار کو چھڑا دیا یہ چھڑانے والا بالا تفاق ضامن نہیں
وَإِذَا أَصَابَ مُحْرِمٌ صَيْدًا فَأَرْسَلَهُ مِنْ يَدِهِ غَيْرُهُ لَاضِمَانَ عَلَيْهِ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَمْلِكُهُ بِالْأَخْذِ فَإِنَّ الصَّيْدَ لَمْ يَبْقَ مَحَلَّا لِلسَّمَلُكِ فِى حَقَّ الْمُحْرِم لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرَمَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمَا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا اشْتَرَى
الحمر
ترجمہ اور جب محرم نے شکار پکڑا پھر اس کو اس کے ہاتھ سے دوسرے نے چھڑا دیا تو بالا تفاق چھڑانے والے پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کو پکڑنے سے اس کا مالک نہیں ہوا کیونکہ شکار محرم کے حق میں ملک میں آنے کا محل نہیں رہا اس لئے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے اور تم پر خشکی کا شکار حرام کر دیا گیا جب تک تم محرم ہو پر یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مسلمان نے شراب خریدی۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم نے شکار پکڑا اور پھر اس کے ہاتھ سے دوسرے کسی نے اس کو چھڑا دیا تو بالا تفاق اس چھڑانے والے پر ضمان واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ محرم اس کو پکڑنے کے باوجود مالک نہیں ہوا اور مالک اس لئے نہیں ہوا کہ محرم کے حق میں کوئی شکار ملک میں آنے کا محل نہیں رہا یعنی کسی شکار پر محرم کی ملک ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے حُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُهُ
خرما (المائدة: ۹۶) پس یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ کسی مسلمان نے شراب خریدی تو مسلمان اس کا مالک نہیں ہو گا اب اگر کسی نے اُس شراب کو تلف کر دیا تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ شراب لذاتہ حرام ہے اسی طرح محرم کا شکار اس پر لذاتہ حرام ہے۔
Someone released the game from the hand of a muhrim: this releaser is not liable by consensus.
And when a muhrim catches game, and then someone else releases it from his hand, there is no liability on that person by consensus, because he (the muhrim) did not own it by taking it. For the game is no longer a subject of ownership in respect to the muhrim, due to the saying of Allah: 'And hunting of the land is forbidden to you as long as you are in ihram' (Al-Ma'idah 96). So it becomes like when a Muslim buys wine.
Translation: And when a muhrim catches game, then someone else releases it from his hand, by consensus the releaser is not liable because he did not become its owner by capturing it, because the game is no longer capable of being owned by the muhrim, due to Allah's command: 'And hunting of the land is forbidden to you as long as you are in ihram.' So it becomes like when a Muslim buys wine.
Explanation: The issue is that if a muhrim catches game and then someone else releases it from his hand, by consensus the releaser is not liable because the muhrim did not become owner despite catching it. The reason he did not become owner is that game cannot enter into ownership of a muhrim, i.e., ownership of a muhrim cannot be established over any game, because Allah said: 'Forbidden to you is hunting of the land as long as you are in ihram' (Al-Ma'idah 96). So it is like when a Muslim buys wine; the Muslim does not become owner of it. Now if someone destroys that wine, he is not liable because wine is inherently prohibited. Similarly, game is inherently prohibited for the muhrim.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage states a ruling by consensus (bil-ittifaq) that if a muhrim catches game while in ihram, and another person releases it from his hand, that releaser is not liable for compensation. The reason is that the muhrim never becomes the owner of the game because the prohibition of hunting during ihram (Quran 5:96) makes game incapable of being owned by the muhrim. The text draws an analogy: if a Muslim buys wine, he does not become its owner because wine is inherently haram (haram li-dhatihi). Similarly, game is haram for the muhrim by virtue of ihram. Therefore, releasing it does not destroy the muhrim's property since he never had property. The commentator explains this in Urdu to ensure clarity. The consensus mentioned is of the Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar).

Key Terms
صید (sayd): Game, lawful to hunt when not in ihram but forbidden during ihram.
ملک (milk): Ownership, property right. Here, the muhrim does not acquire milk over game caught in ihram.
لذاتہ حرام (haram li-dhatihi): Inherently prohibited, like wine, as opposed to haram li-ghayrihi (prohibited due to external factors).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a person who releases game from a muhrim's hand (caught while in ihram) not liable by Hanafi consensus?
A) Because the muhrim willingly gave it up
B) Because the muhrim did not own the game due to the prohibition of hunting
C) Because the releaser did a good deed
D) Because the game belongs to the state

Key Takeaway
By Hanafi consensus, a person who releases game caught by a muhrim in ihram is not liable because the muhrim never owned the game.

Both Muhrims Liable When a Second Muhrim Kills Game in the First's Hand
Joint liability and intra-Hanafi dispute on recovery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a second muhrim kills game held by a first muhrim, explain why both are liable, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the catcher's right of recovery.

Core Idea
Both catcher and killer of game in ihram owe a full penalty; the catcher can recover from the killer according to the majority.

In the sacred state of ihram, even indirect interference with game incurs liability. This passage clarifies a nuanced situation: when a first muhrim catches game and a second muhrim kills it, both are held fully responsible. The rule hinges on the principles of interference (ta'arud), confirmation (taqrir), and causation. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known disagreement between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the two seniors (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on one side, and Imam Zufar on the other, regarding whether the catcher can recover his penalty from the killer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the clear ruling
Note that both muhrims are in ihram, the game is caught and then killed. The text states that each owes a complete penalty. Recognize that this is not a case of sharing a single penalty; each is individually liable.
The ruling is explicitly 'ala kulli wahidin minhuma jaza'an' – upon each a full penalty.
2
Understand the reasoning for joint liability
The catcher interfered by removing the game's security (ta'arud). The killer confirmed that interference (taqrir) and made it permanent. Since confirmation is treated like initiation in liability, both are treated as direct participants.
Key principle: 'al-taqrir ka al-ibtida'' (confirmation is like initiation) in imposing liability.
3
Analyze the analogy with witnesses of divorce
The text compares the killer to a witness who retracts after causing loss through false testimony. In that case, the retracting witness is liable even though the initial harm was caused by the testimony. Similarly, the killer's act makes the catcher's interference a cause of destruction.
This analogy (shabah) illustrates how a secondary act can shift or create liability.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on recovery
Imam Zufar holds that the catcher cannot recover because he is accountable for his own action. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the catcher can recover, because the catching only becomes a cause of liability when destruction occurs, and the killer caused that destruction.
The dispute is only about recovery; all agree both are liable for the penalty to Allah.
5
Apply the principle of taqrir to the case
Consider a modern parallel: If a person parks a car illegally and another person drives it into a wall, both may be liable for damage but the second person's act is the direct cause. The first person's act is a condition, not a cause until the second acts.
Note: This is a rational analogy (qiyas) to clarify causation.

Source Text

محرم کے ہاتھ میں شکار کو کسی دوسرے محرم نے قتل کر دیا تو ہر ایک پر پوری جزاء لازم ہے
فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ مُحْرِمٌ أَخَرُ فِي يَدِهِ فَعَلَى كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا جَزَاءً لِأَنَّ الأخذَ مُتَعَرَضَ لِلصَّيْدِ بِازَالَتِهِ الآمَنَ وَالْقَاتِلُ مُقَرَرٌ لِذلِكَ وَالتَّقْرِيرُ كَالْاِبْتِدَاءِ فِي حَقِ الْتَضْمِيْنِ كَشُهُودِ الطَّلَاقِ قَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ إِذَا رَجَعُوا وَيَرْجِعُ الْأَخِذُ عَلَى الْقَاتِلِ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ لَا يَرْجِعُ لأنَّ الآخِذَ مُوَاخَذْ بِصُنْعِهِ فَلا يَرْجِعُ عَلى غَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْأخُذَ إِنَّمَا يَصِيرُ سَبَبًا لِلضّمَان عِندَ اتَصَالِ الْهَلَاكِ بِهِ فَهُوَ بِالْقَتْلِ جَعَلَ فِعْلَ الأَخِذِ عِلَّةٌ فَيَكُونُ فِى مَعْنَى مُبَاشَرَةِ عِلَّةَ الْعِلَّةٍ فَيُحَالُ بالصِّمَانِ عَلَيْهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے دوسرے کسی محرم نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پوری جزا ولازم ہے کیونکہ پکڑنے والا شکار کے امن کو زائل کر کے شکار کے ساتھ تعرض کرنے والا ہوا اور محرم قاتل اس کو ثابت کرنے والا ہوا اور تقرر کرنا ضمان واجب ہونے کے حق میں ابتداء کے مانند ہے جیسے دخول سے پہلے طلاق کے گواہ جب رجوع کرلیں اور پکڑنے والا مار ڈالنے والے سے رجوع کرے گا۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ رجوع نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ پکڑنے والا اپنے فعل کی وجہ سے ماخوذ ہے۔ اس لئے وہ دوسرے سے رجوع نہ کرے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ پکڑنا ضمان کا سبب اسی وقت ہو گا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ ہلاکت متصل ہو۔ پس قاتل نے قتل کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے کے فعل کو علت کر دیا تو گویا یہ علت کی علت کا ارتکاب کرنے کے معنی میں ہوا اس لئے تاوان کا احالہ قائل ہی پر ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم کے ہاتھ میں جو شکار ہے اگر اس کو کسی دوسرے محرم نے قتل کر دیا تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پوری پوری جزاء ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم نے شکار کے ساتھ بایں طور تعرض کی کہ اس کے امن کو زائل کر دیا اور تعرض احترام کے ان ممنوعات میں سے ہے جن کی جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس تعرض کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے محرم پر جزاء واجب ہوگی۔ اور شکار کو قتل کرنے والے محرم نے اس تعرض کو متحکم کر دیا کیونکہ اگر یہ قتل نہ کرتا تو ممکن تھا کہ یہ محرم اس کو چھوڑ کو تعرض ختم کر دیتا۔ لیکن دوسرے محرم کے شکار کو قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے یہ امکان ختم ہو گیا اور تعرض مستقر راور ثابت ہو گیا اور ضمان واجب ہونے کے حق میں تقرر کرنا ابتداء کے مانند ہے یعنی شکار کا قتل بھی تعرض کرنے والے کے مانند ہو گیا اور تعرض کرنے سے چونکہ جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے قاتل پر جزاء واجب ہوگی۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ہندہ نے اپنے شوہر پر دخول کے بعد طلاق واقع ہونے سے پورے مہر کا دعویٰ کیا ہندہ کے شوہر نے دخول کا انکار کیا اور دو گواہوں نے دخول سے پہلے طلاق واقع ہونے پر گواہی دی چنانچہ ہندہ کو پورا مہر نہیں دلایا گیا۔ پھر گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو انہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے جو کچھ ہندہ کا نقصان کیا تھا اس کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ پس ان کا ظلم کرنا اگر چہ ہندہ کے شوہر کے انکار کے بعد ہے مگر ضامن ہونے میں گویا ابتداء ظلم ہے۔ اسی طرح قتل کرنے والا محرم گو یا ابتدائی ظالم ہو کر ضامن ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم نے جو کچھ تاوان دیا ہے وہ قتل کرنے والے سے واپس لے گا۔ اور امام زفر نے
If another muhrim kills it (the game) while in his hand, then upon each one of them is a full penalty (jaza). Because the catcher interfered with the game by removing its security, and the killer confirmed that interference. And confirmation is like initiation in respect of liability, like the witnesses of divorce before consummation when they retract. And the catcher will recover from the killer. Zufar said: He will not recover because the catcher is held accountable for his own action, so he does not recover from another. Our proof: The catching becomes a cause for liability only when destruction is connected to it. So the killer, by killing, made the catcher's action a cause, so it is like directly causing the cause of the cause, so the liability is assigned to him (the killer). Explanation: The issue is that if a second muhrim kills the game that is in the hand of the first muhrim, then each of them owes a complete penalty. The proof: The catcher interfered with the game by removing its security, and interference is among the prohibited acts that incur a penalty. So due to this interference, the catcher owes a penalty. The killer confirmed this interference, because if he had not killed, it was possible the catcher would have released it and ended the interference. But due to the killing, that possibility ended and the interference became established. And in matters of liability, confirmation is like initiation, meaning the killing becomes like the interference, and since interference necessitates penalty, the killer also owes a penalty. An analogy: Hind claimed full mahr from her husband after divorce following consummation; the husband denied consummation, and two witnesses testified that divorce occurred before consummation, so Hind did not get full mahr. Then the witnesses retracted their testimony; they become liable for the loss they caused to Hind. Although their wrong occurred after the husband's denial, in terms of liability it is as if they initiated the wrong. Similarly, the killer muhrim is like an initial wrongdoer and is liable. The author (Sahib al-Quduri) says that the catcher will recover from the killer the compensation he paid. And Imam Zufar said he does not recover.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a second muhrim kills game that is already in the hand of a first muhrim (who caught it either while halal or while in ihram? Actually, the context is that the first muhrim had caught the game, and then the second kills it. The text says 'fi yadihi' - in his hand. The ruling: both muhrims owe the full penalty (jaza) for the game. The catcher is liable because he interfered by removing the game's security; the killer is liable because he confirmed that interference and made it permanent. The analogy with witnesses of divorce is used: witnesses who retract false testimony become liable for the loss they caused, even if their testimony was not the sole cause. Similarly, the killer's act makes the catcher's interference the effective cause of the destruction, so the killer is like the direct cause of the cause. The catcher can recover from the killer the value he paid as compensation, according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn). Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that the catcher is responsible for his own action and cannot recover. The text provides the Hanafi proof: the catcher's act only becomes a cause of liability when destruction follows; the killer's act makes it a cause, so liability is placed on the killer. The commentator elaborates in Urdu, explaining the reasoning and the analogy.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza): Penalty or expiation for violating ihram prohibitions regarding game; usually involves slaughtering an animal and distributing its meat.
تعرض (ta'arud): Interference, molestation – here, the act of catching game or killing it, which violates the sanctity of ihram.
تقریر (taqrir): Confirmation, establishment – the killer's act confirms and renders permanent the catcher's initial interference.
رجوع (ruju'): Recovery, returning – the catcher's right to reclaim the penalty amount from the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (including Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn), what happens when a second muhrim kills game that is in the hand of the first muhrim?
A) Only the killer pays the penalty
B) Only the catcher pays the penalty
C) Both pay the full penalty, and the catcher can recover from the killer
D) Both pay half the penalty each

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two muhrims are involved in killing game, both are fully liable, and the catcher can recover from the killer by majority.

Killing Game in Another Muhrim's Hand: Double Penalty and Recourse
Ruling on double penalty and recourse for game killed in another's hand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Muhrim kills game in another Muhrim's hand, explain the reasoning, and identify the mufta bihi position on recourse.

Core Idea
When two Muhrims contribute to the death of game, each pays a full penalty; the taker can recover from the killer.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a Muhrim seizes game, and another Muhrim kills it. The Hanafi school holds both liable for a full Jaza, and the taker may recourse against the killer. The ruling hinges on the concept of causation (tasabbub) and is analogized to retracted witnesses in divorce cases. Let's unpack the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Two Muhrims: one seizes game (taker), the other kills it while in the taker's hand. Determine the act: killing game, which is prohibited in ihram.
Each Muhrim is an independent legal agent.
2
Determine the ruling for each
The Hanafi ruling is that each Muhrim pays a full Jaza (penalty). The taker is liable because he interfered by removing security; the killer is liable because he confirmed that interference and prevented release.
Confirmation (taqrir) in liability is treated like initiation (ibtida).
3
Examine the recourse dispute
The taker who paid the penalty may recover it from the killer. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing the taker is only responsible for his own act. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) allows recourse.
The mufta bihi position is the majority view.
4
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
The passage uses an analogy to witnesses of divorce before consummation: if witnesses testify and later retract, they are liable for the loss as if they initiated it. Similarly, the killer's act makes the taker's interference causally relevant.
The analogy establishes that confirmation (taqrir) is equivalent to initiation in liability.

Source Text

محرم کے ہاتھ میں شکار کو کسی دوسرے محرم نے قتل کر دیا تو ہر ایک پر پوری جزاء لازم ہے
فَإِنْ قَتَلَهُ مُحْرِمٌ أَخَرُ فِي يَدِهِ فَعَلَى كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا جَزَاءً لِأَنَّ الأخذَ مُتَعَرَضَ لِلصَّيْدِ بِازَالَتِهِ الآمَنَ وَالْقَاتِلُ مُقَرَرٌ لِذلِكَ وَالتَّقْرِيرُ كَالْاِبْتِدَاءِ فِي حَقِ الْتَضْمِيْنِ كَشُهُودِ الطَّلَاقِ قَبْلَ الدُّخُولِ إِذَا رَجَعُوا وَيَرْجِعُ الْأَخِذُ عَلَى الْقَاتِلِ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ لَا يَرْجِعُ لأنَّ الآخِذَ مُوَاخَذْ بِصُنْعِهِ فَلا يَرْجِعُ عَلى غَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْأخُذَ إِنَّمَا يَصِيرُ سَبَبًا لِلضّمَان عِندَ اتَصَالِ الْهَلَاكِ بِهِ فَهُوَ بِالْقَتْلِ جَعَلَ فِعْلَ الأَخِذِ عِلَّةٌ فَيَكُونُ فِى مَعْنَى مُبَاشَرَةِ عِلَّةَ الْعِلَّةٍ فَيُحَالُ بالصِّمَانِ عَلَيْهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر محرم کے ہاتھ میں رہتے ہوئے دوسرے کسی محرم نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پوری جزا ولازم ہے کیونکہ پکڑنے والا شکار کے امن کو زائل کر کے شکار کے ساتھ تعرض کرنے والا ہوا اور محرم قاتل اس کو ثابت کرنے والا ہوا اور تقرر کرنا ضمان واجب ہونے کے حق میں ابتداء کے مانند ہے جیسے دخول سے پہلے طلاق کے گواہ جب رجوع کرلیں اور پکڑنے والا مار ڈالنے والے سے رجوع کرے گا۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ رجوع نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ پکڑنے والا اپنے فعل کی وجہ سے ماخوذ ہے۔ اس لئے وہ دوسرے سے رجوع نہ کرے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ پکڑنا ضمان کا سبب اسی وقت ہو گا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ ہلاکت متصل ہو۔ پس قاتل نے قتل کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے کے فعل کو علت کر دیا تو گویا یہ علت کی علت کا ارتکاب کرنے کے معنی میں ہوا اس لئے تاوان کا احالہ قائل ہی پر ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم کے ہاتھ میں جو شکار ہے اگر اس کو کسی دوسرے محرم نے قتل کر دیا تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پوری پوری جزاء ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم نے شکار کے ساتھ بایں طور تعرض کی کہ اس کے امن کو زائل کر دیا اور تعرض احترام کے ان ممنوعات میں سے ہے جن کی جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس تعرض کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے محرم پر جزاء واجب ہوگی۔ اور شکار کو قتل کرنے والے محرم نے اس تعرض کو متحکم کر دیا کیونکہ اگر یہ قتل نہ کرتا تو ممکن تھا کہ یہ محرم اس کو چھوڑ کو تعرض ختم کر دیتا۔ لیکن دوسرے محرم کے شکار کو قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے یہ امکان ختم ہو گیا اور تعرض مستقر راور ثابت ہو گیا اور ضمان واجب ہونے کے حق میں تقرر کرنا ابتداء کے مانند ہے یعنی شکار کا قتل بھی تعرض کرنے والے کے مانند ہو گیا اور تعرض کرنے سے چونکہ جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے قاتل پر جزاء واجب ہوگی۔ اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ مثلاً ہندہ نے اپنے شوہر پر دخول کے بعد طلاق واقع ہونے سے پورے مہر کا دعویٰ کیا ہندہ کے شوہر نے دخول کا انکار کیا اور دو گواہوں نے دخول سے پہلے طلاق واقع ہونے پر گواہی دی چنانچہ ہندہ کو پورا مہر نہیں دلایا گیا۔ پھر گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو انہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے جو کچھ ہندہ کا نقصان کیا تھا اس کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ پس ان کا ظلم کرنا اگر چہ ہندہ کے شوہر کے انکار کے بعد ہے مگر ضامن ہونے میں گویا ابتداء ظلم ہے۔ اسی طرح قتل کرنے والا محرم گو یا ابتدائی ظالم ہو کر ضامن ہے۔ صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ شکار پکڑنے والے محرم نے جو کچھ تاوان دیا ہے وہ قتل کرنے والے سے واپس لے گا۔ اور امام زفر نے
کہا کہ پکڑنے والا واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والا اپنی حرکت کی وجہ سے ماخوذ ہے اس لئے وہ دوسرے سے واپس کیوں لے گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرم کا شکار کو پکڑنا اسی وقت ضمان کا سبب ہوگا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ ہلاکت متصل ہو۔ یعنی پکڑنے کے ساتھ ہلاکت بھی واقع ہو ۔ حالانکہ پکڑنے والے محرم نے اس کو ہلاک نہیں کیا بلکہ قاتل دوسرا محرم ہے تو قاتل نے قتل کر دینے کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے کے فعل کو علت کر دیا یعنی ہلاکت کا واسطہ بنا دیا۔ اور اصل ہلاکت خود کی ۔ تو گویا قاتل علت العلت کا ارتکاب کرنے والا ہوا کیونکہ اسکے قتل کرنے ہی کی وجہ سے شکار کو پکڑ ناسبب ضمان ہوا ہے اگر وہ قتل نہ کرتا تو گرفتاری سبب ضمان نہ ہوتی اس لئے تاوان قاتل ہی کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ یعنی جو تاوان پکڑنے والے محرم نے دیا ہے وہ قاتل پر جائے گا کہ یہ قاتل سے واپس لے لے۔
If another Muhrim kills it while in his hand, then upon each of them is a full penalty because the taker interferes with the game by removing its security, and the killer confirms that. Confirmation in liability is like initiation, similar to witnesses of divorce before consummation when they retract. The taker will recourse against the killer. Zufar said: He does not recourse because the taker is accountable for his own action, so he does not recourse against another. Our proof: Taking becomes a cause for liability only when destruction is connected to it. So by the killing, he made the taker's action a cause, thus he is in the meaning of directly perpetrating the cause of the cause, so liability is imputed to him. (Urdu translation:) Explanation: If while game is in the hand of a Muhrim, another Muhrim kills it, then each has a full penalty. Reason: The taker interferes by removing security, so penalty is due. The killer confirms that interference, because without killing the taker might have released it. So the killer's action made the interference permanent, and confirmation is like initiation. Analogy: If Hind claimed full mahr after divorce before consummation, and two witnesses testified to divorce before consummation, then retracted, they are liable for the loss; their oppression is like initiation. Similarly, the killer is liable. Al-Quduri says the taker recovers from the killer. Zufar says no. Our proof: Taking causes liability only if connected to destruction; the killer made the taking a cause, so the penalty is turned to him.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a Muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) seizes game and another Muhrim kills it while it is in the first's hand. The Hanafi position is that both incur a full penalty (Jaza). The taker (one who seized) is liable because he interfered with the game by removing its security. The killer is also liable because by killing, he confirmed that interference and prevented the taker from potentially releasing it, thus making the interference permanent. Confirmation in liability is treated like initiation. The passage then addresses the right of recourse: the taker can recover from the killer the penalty he paid. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing the taker is solely responsible for his own act. The majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) holds that the taker can recourse, because the taker's act only becomes a cause for liability when destruction is connected to it; the killer provided that destruction. An analogy is drawn to witnesses of divorce who retract after causing loss—they are liable as if they initiated the harm. The relied-upon fatwa is that the taker may recover the penalty from the killer.

Key Terms
محرم (Muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to prohibitions including hunting.
جزاء (Jaza): A penalty for violating ihram prohibitions, typically the slaughter of an animal or equivalent compensation.
ضمان (Daman): Liability to compensate for harm or loss, often financially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Muhrim A seizes game and Muhrim B kills it while in A's hand, what does the Hanafi mufta bihi position say about recourse?
A) A cannot recourse because A's own act caused the liability.
B) A can recourse from B because B's killing made A's act a cause.
C) Both pay half penalty and no recourse.
D) Only B pays penalty, so no recourse needed.

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim who seizes game and another Muhrim who kills it each owe a full Jaza; the taker may recover the penalty from the killer.

The Obligation to Pay Value for Cutting Fresh Wild Vegetation in the Haram
Ruling on cutting wild grass/trees in Haram, requiring payment of value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting fresh wild vegetation in the Haram, identify when payment of value is required, and explain why fasting does not substitute.

Core Idea
Cutting fresh wild grass or trees in the Haram requires payment of market value in charity; fasting does not suffice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific violation of the sanctity of the Haram: cutting fresh, wild, unowned vegetation. The ruling is a financial penalty (value) given in charity, not a religious act like fasting. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is cutting fresh, wild, unowned grass or trees within the boundaries of the Haram. The context excludes cultivated or owned vegetation.
2
Determine the ruling
The ruling is wajib: the cutter must pay the market value (qimah) of what he cut, except if the vegetation is dry. Dry material incurs no penalty.
Exception for dry: because the sanctity is attached to fresh growth.
3
Examine the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Do not cut its fresh grass and do not break its thorns.' This prohibition establishes the sanctity of Haram vegetation.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning (dalala) is clear and definitive (qati) in prohibiting the act.
4
Understand the distinction from ihram
The prohibition here is due to the place (Haram), not the state (ihram). Therefore, the penalty is financial, not an act of worship like fasting. Fasting only applies when the prohibition is due to ihram.
This distinction is emphasized: 'لا يكون للصوم في هذه القيمة مدخل'.
5
Apply the consequence
The cutter must give the value in charity to the poor. Upon payment, he becomes the owner of the cut material, similar to compensation in financial rights.
The ownership transfer reinforces that this is a financial liability, not a ritual expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرم کا گھاس یا درخت جو کسی کی ملک میں نہیں اور نہ لوگ اگاتے ہیں کاٹا تو اس کی قیمت لازم ہے فَإِنْ قَطَعَ خَشِيْشَ الْحَرَمِ أَوْ شَجَرَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِمُمُلُوكَةٍ وَهُوَ مِمَّا لَا يَسْتُهُ النَّاسُ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيْمَتُهُ إِلَّا فِيْمَا جُفَّ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّ حُرْمَتَهُمَا تَثْبُتُ بِسَبَبِ الْحَرَمِ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يُحْتَلَى خِلَاهَا وَلَا يُعْضَدُ شَوْكَهَا وَلَا يَكُونُ لِلصَّوْمِ فِى هَذِهِ الْقِيْمَةِ مَدْخَلَ لِأَنَّ حُرْمَةَ تَنَاوُلَهَا بِسَبَبِ الْحَرَمِ لَا بِسَبَبِ الْإِحْرَامِ فَكَانَ مِنْ ضِمَانِ الْمَحَالِ عَلَى مَابَيَّنَا وَ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِقِيْمَتِهِ عَلَى الْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِذَا أَداهَا مَلَكَهُ كَمَا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے حرم کی گھاس کاٹی یا ایسا درخت کاٹا جو کسی کی ملک نہیں ہے درانحالیکہ وہ ایسی قسم سے ہے جس کو لوگ نہیں اگاتے تو اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے سوائے ایسی گھاس کے جو اس میں سے خشک ہو گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ گھاس اور درخت کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ثابت ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ حرم کی ہری گھاس نہ کائی جائے اور نہ اس کے کانٹے توڑے جائیں اور اس قیمت میں روزے کو کچھ دخل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کو حاصل کرنے کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ احرام کی وجہ سے۔ پس یہی کل کا مضمان ہو گا جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے
اور اس کی قیمت کو فقراء پر صدقہ کرے اور جب یہ قیمت ادا کر دے تو اس گھاس یا درخت کا مالک ہو گیا جیسے حقوق العباد میں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی نے حرم کی گھاس کاٹی یا ایسا درخت کاٹا جو کسی کی ملک نہیں ہے اور خودرو ہے یعنی اس کو لوگ نہیں اگاتے بلکہ وہ خود اگتا ہے تو ایسی گھاس اور درخت کو کاٹنے کی صورت میں اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر وہ گھاس یا درخت خشک ہو گیا تو اس کے کاٹنے پر قیمت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ گھاس اور درخت کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ نہ تو حرم کی ہری گھاس کائی جائے اور نہ اس کے کانٹے توڑے جائیں۔ الخلاء ہری گھاس کو کہتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حرم کی گھاس اور درخت کی جزاء میں اگر کاٹنے والا روزے رکھ کر اس جزاء کو ادا کرنا چاہے تو کافی نہ ہوگا یعنی روزہ کافی نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ قیمت ادا کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ حرم کی گھاس اور درخت کو کاٹنے کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ احرام کی وجہ سے پس یہی قیمہ - محل کا ضمان ہوا نہ کہ فعل محرم کا۔ اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ روزہ افعال کی جزاء بننے کی صلاحیت تو رکھتا ہے مگر حل کی جزاء بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں اس قیمت کو فقراء پر صدقہ کر دے اور جب اس نے اس کی قیمت ادا کر دی تو اس گھاں یا درخت کا
If he cuts grass of the Haram or a tree that is not owned and is of the type that people do not cultivate, then upon him is its value, except for what has dried of it. Because the sanctity of both is established due to the Haram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not cut its fresh grass and do not break its thorns.' Fasting has no entry in this value, because the prohibition of taking them is due to the Haram, not due to ihram. So it is liability of the place as we have explained. He should give its value in charity to the poor, and when he pays it, he becomes its owner similarly as in rights of servants. (Urdu translation): Explanation: If one cuts grass of the Haram or a tree not owned and wild, he must pay its value, except if dry. Because sanctity is due to Haram. Hadith. Fasting does not suffice because prohibition is due to Haram, not ihram. So it is liability of the place. He gives value in charity; upon payment he owns the material.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage deals with cutting fresh grass or trees of the Haram (sanctuary of Makkah) that are not owned and are wild (self-grown). The ruling: the cutter must pay the market value of what he cuts, except for dry material. The proof is the hadith: 'Do not cut its fresh grass and do not break its thorns.' The commentary emphasizes that the sanctity is due to the Haram itself, not due to ihram. Therefore, the penalty is a monetary compensation (value) paid in charity to the poor, not a religious act like fasting. If the cutter pays the value, he becomes the owner of the cut material, similar to other financial rights. The passage clarifies that fasting cannot substitute for this payment because fasting is only valid as a penalty for acts prohibited due to ihram (like hunting), not for violations of the sanctity of the Haram. The relied-upon position is that the value must be paid and given in charity.

Key Terms
حرم (Haram): The sacred precinct around Makkah, with special prohibitions.
خشيش (Khashish): Grass or herbage that grows wild; the text uses it for green grass.
قيمة (Qimah): Market value of the cut material, estimated by price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for cutting a dry branch from a wild tree within the Haram?
A) Payment of its value in charity is required.
B) No payment is required because it is dry.
C) Payment and fasting are both required.
D) Only fasting is required.

Key Takeaway
Cutting fresh wild vegetation in the Haram requires payment of market value in charity; fasting does not suffice because the prohibition is due to the sanctity of the place, not ihram.

Liability of the Killer When a Muhrim Catches Game
Explains the Hanafi position that the killer compensates, not the catcher.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who is liable when one Muhrim catches game and another kills it, and explain the causal reasoning that supports this view.

Core Idea
The killer, not the catcher, bears liability because the direct cause of death severs the catcher's causal link.

In the rituals of Hajj, a Muhrim is prohibited from hunting or killing game. A classic scenario within the Hanafi school is when one Muhrim catches game alive and another kills it. Who must compensate for the violation? This lesson unpacks the internal Hanafi dispute and clarifies the operative ruling based on causal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon position within the Hanafi school: the killer is liable for compensation, not the catcher.
This is the view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize the dissenting opinion within the school: Imam Zufar holds that the catcher is liable because he initiated the capture.
Imam Zufar's position is based on the catcher being the initial cause (makhudh).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Imam Zufar's rationale: the catcher, by his own action, made the game 'seized' (makhudh), so he should bear the responsibility.
Opponent's proof is rational (dalil aqli).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi counter-argument: the catcher's action becomes a cause for liability only if death is directly connected to it. Since the killer performed the actual killing, he is the true cause (illat al-illah).
The killer's act severs the causal chain, making him directly liable.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if the catcher already paid compensation, he can recover it from the killer.
This shows the killer ultimately bears the financial burden.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کہا کہ پکڑنے والا واپس نہیں لے سکتا۔ یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شکار پکڑنے والا اپنی حرکت کی وجہ سے ماخوذ ہے اس لئے وہ دوسرے سے واپس کیوں لے گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرم کا شکار کو پکڑنا اسی وقت ضمان کا سبب ہوگا جبکہ اس کے ساتھ ہلاکت متصل ہو۔ یعنی پکڑنے کے ساتھ ہلاکت بھی واقع ہو ۔ حالانکہ پکڑنے والے محرم نے اس کو ہلاک نہیں کیا بلکہ قاتل دوسرا محرم ہے تو قاتل نے قتل کر دینے کی وجہ سے پکڑنے والے کے فعل کو علت کر دیا یعنی ہلاکت کا واسطہ بنا دیا۔ اور اصل ہلاکت خود کی ۔ تو گویا قاتل علت العلت کا ارتکاب کرنے والا ہوا کیونکہ اسکے قتل کرنے ہی کی وجہ سے شکار کو پکڑ ناسبب ضمان ہوا ہے اگر وہ قتل نہ کرتا تو گرفتاری سبب ضمان نہ ہوتی اس لئے تاوان قاتل ہی کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔ یعنی جو تاوان پکڑنے والے محرم نے دیا ہے وہ قاتل پر جائے گا کہ یہ قاتل سے واپس لے لے۔
It is said that the catcher cannot take back (the compensation). This is the statement of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Imam Zufar's proof is that the catcher is seized due to his own action, so why would he take back from another? Our proof is that a Muhrim's catching of game is a cause for liability only when destruction is connected to it, i.e., death occurs with the catching. However, the catching Muhrim did not kill it; rather, the killer is another Muhrim. So the killer, by killing, made the catcher's action a cause—that is, an intermediary for destruction—while he himself performed the actual destruction. Thus, the killer committed the cause of the cause, because it was due to his killing that the catching became a cause for liability. If he had not killed, the catching would not have been a cause for liability. Therefore, the compensation is turned back to the killer: that is, the compensation paid by the catching Muhrim will be on the killer, and the catcher will take it back from him.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding liability when one Muhrim catches game and another kills it. The position of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) is that the catcher cannot recover compensation from the killer. Imam Zufar argues that the catcher is liable because his act of catching was the cause. However, the preferred Hanafi position (as argued by the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa) is that the killer is ultimately liable because liability for the catch only arises when it leads directly to death. Since the catcher did not kill, his act is merely an intermediary; the killer's direct action severs the causal link. Thus, the killer must indemnify the catcher for the compensation paid. This is a rational proof without explicit textual evidence.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability for compensation, in this context the payment due for killing game in Ihram.
علت العلت (illat al-illah): Cause of the cause; the killer's action is the ultimate cause that makes the catching a cause for liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if one Muhrim catches game and another Muhrim kills it, who is liable for compensation?
A) The catcher
B) The killer
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The direct cause of death (the killer) bears liability, not the intermediary cause (the catcher).

Compensation for Cutting Wild Grass and Trees of the Haram
Ruling on cutting non-owned, uncultivated vegetation in the Haram: value wajib, no fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for cutting non-owned vegetation in the Haram and explain why fasting is not an acceptable substitute.

Core Idea
Cutting live Haram vegetation requires value; fasting invalid because sanctity is place-based.

The sanctity of the Haram (Makkah sanctuary) extends to its natural vegetation – wild grass and trees that are not owned or cultivated. Cutting such live plants violates a specific prohibition and entails a unique compensation. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: why only monetary value is accepted, not fasting, and how the exception for dry vegetation fits the legal logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the exact act being addressed: cutting grass or trees in the Haram that are non-owned, uncultivated, and live. The ruling is that its market value (qimah) is wajib.
Only live vegetation triggers compensation; dry is exempt.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: “لا يُحتَلى خَلاها ولا يُعضَد شَوكها” (Do not cut its fresh grass nor break its thorns). This is a direct prohibition from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The hadith is ahad, so its transmission is zanni, but its meaning (dalala) is considered qat'i for the Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negative command (لا يُحتَلى) indicates prohibition (haram). Violating a prohibition related to a sanctified place (Haram) triggers a guarantee (daman) of the place's value, not a corporal penalty like fasting.
Hanafi usul: al-nahy yufid al-tahrim, and the violation of a place-based sanctity requires monetary compensation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow fasting as an alternative expiation, analogizing to Ihram violations. The Hanafis reject this because the sanctity here is attached to the place (Haram), not the state of Ihram.
This distinction is crucial: fasting compensates for actions (Ihram violations), not for place-based sanctities.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position (value only) is the mufta bihi and is based on the direct text and the principle of daman al-mahal. The opposing view is considered weak because it overlooks the distinguishing factor of place-based sanctity.
The text cites Hidayah and Quduri, both authoritative in the school, to settle the matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرم کا گھاس یا درخت جو کسی کی ملک میں نہیں اور نہ لوگ اگاتے ہیں کاٹا تو اس کی قیمت لازم ہے فَإِنْ قَطَعَ خَشِيْشَ الْحَرَمِ أَوْ شَجَرَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِمُمُلُوكَةٍ وَهُوَ مِمَّا لَا يَسْتُهُ النَّاسُ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيْمَتُهُ إِلَّا فِيْمَا جُفَّ مِنْهُ لِأَنَّ حُرْمَتُهُمَا تَثْبُتُ بِسَبَبِ الْحَرَمِ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يُحَتلَى خِلَاهَا وَلَا يُعْضَدُ شَوْكَهَا وَلَا يَكُونُ لِلصَّوْمِ الْفُقَرَاءِ وَإِذَا أَداهَا مَلَكَهُ كَمَا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ ترجمہ اگر کسی نے حرم کی گھاس کاٹی یا ایسا درخت کاٹا جو کسی کی ملک نہیں ہے درانحالیکہ وہ ایسی قسم سے ہے جس کو لوگ نہیں اگاتے تو اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے سوائے ایسی گھاس کے جو اس میں سے خشک ہو گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ گھاس اور درخت کی جرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ثابت ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ حرم کی ہری گھاس نہ کائی جائے اور نہ اس کے کانٹے توڑے جائیں اور اس قیمت میں روزے کو کچھ دخل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس کو حاصل کرنے کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ احرام کی وجہ سے۔ پس یہی کل کا مضمان ہو گا جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے اور اس کی قیمت کو فقراء پر صدقہ کرے اور جب یہ قیمت ادا کر دے تو اس گھاس یا درخت کا مالک ہو گیا جیسے حقوق العباد میں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی نے حرم کی گھاس کاٹی یا ایسا درخت کاٹا جو کسی کی ملک نہیں ہے اور خودرو ہے یعنی اس کو لوگ نہیں اگاتے بلکہ وہ خود اگتا ہے تو ایسی گھاس اور درخت کو کاٹنے کی صورت میں اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ ہاں اگر وہ گھاس یا درخت خشک ہو گیا تو اس کے کاٹنے پر قیمت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ گھاس اور درخت کی حرمت حرم کی وجہ سے ثابت ہے کیونکہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ نہ تو حرم کی ہری گھاس کائی جائے اور نہ اس کے کانٹے تو ڑے جائیں۔ الخلاء ہری گھاس کو کہتے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے رکھتا۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں اس قیمت کو فقراء پر صدقہ کر دے اور جب اس نے اس کی قیمت ادا کر دی تو اس گھاں یا درخت کا مالک ہو گیا جیسے حقوق العباد میں ہے۔ مثلاً زید نے عمر کی کوئی چیز غضب کرلی اور قاضی نے زید کو اس کی قیمت ادا کرنے کا حکم دے دیا اور اس نے قیمت دے بھی دی تو زید اس چیز کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔
If one cuts grass of the Haram or a tree that is not owned, and it is of the type that people do not cultivate, then he must pay its value, except for what has dried from it. Because their sanctity is established due to the Haram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Its fresh grass shall not be cut, and its thorns shall not be broken.' And fasting has no entry in this value, because the prohibition of obtaining them is due to the Haram, not due to Ihram. So it falls under the guarantee of places (daman al-mahal) as we explained. He should give its value in charity to the poor, and when he pays it, he becomes the owner of it, as in the rights of humans. Translation: If someone cuts grass of the Haram or cuts a tree that is not owned, while it is of the type that people do not cultivate, then its value is wajib upon him, except for grass that has become dry from it. Because the sanctity of the grass and tree is established due to the Haram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The fresh grass of the Haram shall not be cut, and its thorns shall not be broken.' And fasting has no role in this value, because the prohibition of obtaining them is due to the Haram, not due to Ihram. So this is indeed the guarantee of places (daman al-mahal) as we have explained. He should give its value in charity to the poor, and when he pays this value, he becomes the owner of that grass or tree, as in the rights of humans. Explanation: If someone cuts the grass of the Haram or cuts a tree that is not owned and is wild (self-growing), i.e., people do not cultivate it but it grows on its own, then cutting such grass and tree makes its value wajib upon him. Yes, if that grass or tree has dried, then cutting it does not require value. The proof is that the sanctity of grass and tree is established due to the Haram, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not cut the fresh grass of the Haram, and do not break its thorns.' (Al-Khila refers to fresh grass). The author of Hidayah says: In the expiation for grass and tree of the Haram, if the cutter wants to perform fasting as expiation, it will not suffice; rather, paying the value is necessary, because the prohibition of cutting grass and tree of the Haram is due to the Haram, not due to Ihram; so this is the guarantee of the place (daman al-mahal), not of the act of the Muhrim. It has passed before that fasting has the capacity to be expiation for actions, but does not have the capacity to be expiation for places (al-hal). The author of Quduri says: He should give this value in charity to the poor, and when he has paid its value, he becomes the owner of that grass or tree, as in the rights of humans. For example, Zaid usurped a thing belonging to Umar, and the judge ordered Zaid to pay its value, and he paid it, then Zaid becomes the owner of that thing.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for cutting non-owned, uncultivated grass or trees within the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca). The key points: 1) Cutting live vegetation requires payment of its market value; 2) Dry vegetation is exempt; 3) Fasting (sawm) is not a valid substitute for the value, because the sanctity here is attached to the place (Haram) not to the state of Ihram. The proof is the hadith: 'Do not cut the fresh grass of the Haram, nor break its thorns.' The compensation is classified as daman al-mahal (guarantee of the place) rather than daman al-fi'l (guarantee of an act). The value is given in charity to the poor, and once paid, the cutter becomes the owner of the cut vegetation. This is analogous to usurpation (ghasb): if a usurper is forced to pay the value, he becomes the owner.

Key Terms
خشیش الحرم (khasheesh al-haram): The dry grass or vegetation of the Haram; but in this context it refers to any grass that grows wild.
خلاء (khila'): Fresh green grass that grows in the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No compensation if it is dry

Key Takeaway
Cutting live, non-owned, uncultivated vegetation in the Haram requires payment of its market value in charity; fasting cannot substitute because the violation is place-based.

Ruling on Selling Cut Haram Vegetation
Clarifies the ruling on selling cut Haram vegetation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling cut Haram vegetation, explain the reasoning based on ownership through a prohibited cause, and distinguish it from the ruling on game.

Core Idea
Selling cut Haram grass is makruh but valid; ownership via compensation permits sale.

You have likely learned that cutting vegetation from the Haram is prohibited. But what if someone cuts it, pays its value, and then tries to sell it? Is the sale valid or invalid? This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the Hanafi position: the sale is makruh (disliked) but legally permissible (ja'iz). The reasoning hinges on the fact that ownership is established through compensation, even though the initial act was prohibited. This ruling stands in contrast to game caught in ihram, which cannot be sold at all. Let's explore the legal nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling grass or trees cut from the Haram after cutting. The ruling is makruh (disliked) but the sale itself is permissible (ja'iz).
Makruh here is likely tahrimi (close to haram).
2
Understand the reason for karahah
The karahah is because the seller obtained ownership through a prohibited cause (cutting Haram vegetation). If selling were openly permitted, it would encourage people to cut for profit.
The prohibition is on the means of acquisition, not on the sale itself.
3
Note the validity of the sale
Despite the karahah, the sale is valid because ownership is established via compensation (daman). The seller is the owner, so the contract is effective.
Contrast with stolen goods where ownership never transfers.
4
Contrast with game
The text explicitly distinguishes this from game (sayd) caught in ihram, which cannot be sold even with karahah. The difference will be explained later.
This highlights that the ruling is specific to vegetation.
5
Extract the underlying principle
The principle: ownership through a prohibited cause does not nullify the sale if ownership is real; the sin attaches to the acquisition, not the subsequent disposal.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applied to ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ بَيْعُهُ بَعْدَ القَطِع لِأَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ بِسَبٍ مُّحْظُورٍ شَرْعًا فَلَوْ أَطْلَقَ لَهُ فِي بَيْعِهِ لَتَطَرَّقَ النَّاسُ إِلى مِثْلِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ مَعَ الْكَرَاهَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّيْدِ وَالْفَرْقُ مَا نَذَكُرُهُ ترجمہ اور کاٹنے کے بعد اس کا بیچنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک ایسے سبب سے ہوا ہے جو شرعا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اگر اس کو اس کے بیچنے کی اجازت دے دیجائے تو لوگ اس جیسے کاموں کی طرف راہ پکڑلیں گے مگر کراہت کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے برخلاف شکار کے اور فرق وہ ہے جس کو ہم ذکر کریں گے۔ تشریح مسئلہ حرم کی گھاس یا درخت کاٹ کر اس کو فروخت کرنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص اس کا مالک ایسے سبب سے ہوا ہے جو شرعاً ممنوع ہے۔ اب اگر بیچنے کی اجازت عام کر دی جائے تو جائز ہے اس کے برخلاف شکار کہ اس کو فروخت کرنا مع الکراہت بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ دونوں کے درمیان وجہ فرق آگے بیان کریں گے۔ فانْتَظِرُوا إِنِّى مَعَكُمْ مِنَ الْمُنتَظِرِينَ -
And it is makruh to sell it after cutting, because he owned it through a legally prohibited cause. So if he were given permission to sell it, people would take to similar acts. However, sale is permissible with karahah, unlike game, and the difference we will mention. Translation: And selling it after cutting is makruh, because he became its owner through a cause that is legally prohibited. If permission for its sale were given, people would find a way to do similar things. But sale with karahah is permissible, unlike game, and the difference we will mention. Explanation: Selling the Haram grass or tree after cutting is makruh, because this person became its owner through a cause that is legally prohibited. Now, if permission to sell were made general, it would be permissible. Contrary to game, its sale is not permissible even with karahah. The difference between the two will be mentioned later. So wait, I am among those who wait.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling after one has cut grass or a tree from the Haram and thus owns it (by paying the value). The ruling is that selling such cut vegetation is makruh (disliked) because the ownership was acquired through a prohibited act (cutting Haram vegetation). However, the sale itself is still valid (jā'iz) despite the karahah. This is in contrast to game caught in Ihram, which cannot be sold at all. The text promises to explain the distinction later. The wisdom is that if selling were outright permitted, it would encourage people to cut Haram vegetation for profit; but since compensation was paid, ownership is established, so sale is valid but disliked.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; the act is valid but blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Makruh but permissible
C) Permissible without dislike
D) Only allowed in charity

Key Takeaway
Selling cut Haram vegetation is makruh but valid, unlike game, because ownership is established through compensation.

Cultivated Vegetation in the Haram Is Not Protected
Ruling that cultivated plants in Haram are not protected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why cultivated plants in the Haram are not protected by consensus and apply the reasoning to determine whether compensation is due when cutting such plants.

Core Idea
Only wild, self-growing vegetation in the Haram enjoys inviolability; cultivated plants are exempt from compensation by consensus.

In this passage, the Hanafi author establishes a key distinction between wild and cultivated vegetation within the sacred precincts of Makkah. While wild plants are protected by their natural attribution to the Haram, plants that people grow and tend lose that protective status. The proof is not merely a textual command but a continuous, unobjected practice (ijma) from the time of the Prophet until today. Understanding this distinction is essential for properly applying the rules of hunting and vegetation in the Haram during Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is cutting cultivated vegetation within the Haram. The ruling is that no compensation is required; it is permissible (mubah).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is ijma (consensus) based on the continuous practice of Muslims since the Prophet's time—cultivating and cutting plants in the Haram without any objection.
This ijma is considered qati (definitive) in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The absence of objection to a widespread, continuous practice indicates permissibility and serves as binding evidence in Hanafi usul. The ruling is derived directly from this consensus.
Rational evidence (ta'lil) about attribution to the Haram versus attribution to the cultivator supports the same conclusion.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies only to vegetation that is customarily cultivated (ma yunbituhu al-nas 'adatan). Wild, self-growing vegetation remains protected and cutting it requires compensation.
The distinction hinges on whether the plant's growth is attributed to human action or to the Haram itself.
5
Apply the ruling
In a concrete scenario—e.g., a date palm planted by a farmer in the Haram—cutting it incurs no compensation because it is cultivated. Only if the tree grew naturally would compensation be required.
This demonstrates the practical impact of the ruling for pilgrims and residents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَّذِي يُنْبِتُهُ النَّاسُ عَادَةً عَرَفْنَاهُ غَيْرَ مُسْتَحَقِّ لِلْأَمَنِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَلَأَنَّ المُحمَ المُنسُوب إِلَى الحَرَمِ وَالنِّسَةُ إِلَيْهِ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ عِنْدَ عَدَمِ النِّسْبَةِ إِلى غَيْرِهِ بِالْإِنْبَاتِ وَمَا لَا يُنبَتَ عَادَةً إِذَا أَنْبَتَهُ إِنْسَانُ الْتَحَقَ بِمَا يُنبتُ عَادَةَ ترجمہ ... اور وہ گھاس اور درخت جو کہ لوگ عادت کے طور پر اگاتے ہیں ہم نے اس کا مستحق امن نہ ہونا اجماع سے پہچانا ہے اور اس لئے کہ حرام وہی کیا گیا جو حرم کی طرف منسوب ہے اور حرم کی طرف مکمل طور پر نسبت اس وقت ہے جبکہ اگانے کی نسبت دوسری کی طرف نہ ہو۔ اور جو درخت عادہ بویا نہیں جاتا جب اس کو کسی انسان نے اگایا تو وہ ایسے درخت کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گیا جو بطریق عادت بویا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح جو گھاس اور درخت عادتا اگائے اور بوئے جاتے ہیں ان کا مستحق امن نہ ہونا اجماع سے ثابت ہے۔ کیونکہ لوگ عہدِ رسالت سے لے کر آج تک حرم کی زمین میں کھیتی کرتے ہیں اس کو کاٹتے ہیں اور اس پر کسی نے نکیر نہیں کی ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جس کو لوگ اگاتے ہیں وہ امن کا حقدار نہیں ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس گھاس اور درخت کا کا نا حرام ہے جو حرم کی طرف منسوب ہو۔ اور حرم کی طرف پورے طور سے نسبت اسی وقت ہوگی جبکہ دوسرے کی طرف اگانے کی نسبت نہ ہو۔ اور جو گھاس اور درخت عادہ نہیں بویا جات: اگر ان کوکسی انسان نے بویا تو وہ اسی کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا جس کو عادہ بویا جاتا ہے یعنی اسکے کاٹنے کی وجہ سے قیمت واجب نہ ہوگی۔
And what people customarily cultivate, we have known by consensus (ijma) that it is not deserving of protection (aman). And because what is forbidden is that which is attributed to the Haram, and complete attribution to it occurs when there is no attribution to another through cultivation. And what is not customarily planted, if a person plants it, it becomes attached to what is customarily planted. Translation: ...And that grass and trees which people customarily grow, we have recognized by consensus that they are not deserving of protection. And because the prohibition is only on what is attributed to the Haram, and full attribution to it is when there is no attribution to another through cultivation. And trees that are not customarily planted, if a person plants them, they become attached to what is customarily planted. Explanation: That grass and trees which are customarily grown and planted are not entitled to protection by consensus. Since the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to today, people have cultivated the land of the Haram, cut it, and no one has objected. This shows that what people cultivate is not deserving of protection. The second proof is that the prohibition applies to grass and trees that are attributed to the Haram, and full attribution to the Haram is only when there is no attribution of cultivation to another. And grass and trees that are not customarily planted, if someone plants them, they become attached to what is customarily planted, meaning cutting them does not require payment of value.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage establishes that cultivated vegetation in the Haram is not protected by the special sanctity. The proof is ijma (consensus) from the practice of the Companions and later Muslims who have always farmed in the Haram without reproach. The reasoning is that the prohibition (in the hadith) only applies to vegetation that is naturally attributed to the Haram, i.e., wild growth. When humans cultivate it, the attribution shifts to the cultivator, removing it from the protected category. Therefore, cutting such cultivated plants does not require compensation. This is a crucial limitation: only wild, uncultivated growth is inviolable, not agricultural crops.

Key Terms
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars or the Muslim community; here it refers to the continuous practice from the Prophet's time.
امن (aman): Protection or safe status; vegetation deserving of protection from cutting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Must pay compensation
B) No compensation required
C) Must give charity
D) Only if the tree is dry

Key Takeaway
Cultivated plants in the Haram are not protected by consensus; only wild self-growing vegetation is inviolable.

Selling Grass of Haram After Cutting
Ruling with proof on selling Haram vegetation after cutting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling grass/trees of the Haram after cutting and explain the rationale based on prohibited means of acquisition (sabab mahzur).

Core Idea
Selling Haram grass is valid but disliked due to prohibited ownership means—not invalid.

This lesson addresses a subtle fiqh issue: selling vegetation from the Haram sanctuary that one has cut. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the object itself (which is owned) and the means by which it was obtained. Learn why the sale is permissible yet makruh, and how it differs from hunting in the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is selling grass or trees of the Haram after cutting them. The ruling given is that it is makruh (disliked) but the sale is still valid (sahih).
Makruh here means makruh tanzihi—permissible but better avoided.
2
Understand the reason (ta'lil)
The reason for karahah is that the person owned the grass by a cause that is prohibited in Shariah (cutting Haram vegetation). This prohibited means taints the transaction.
The principle: a prohibited cause does not make the object impure but affects the ruling on transactions.
3
Recognize the sadd al-dhara'i' aspect
If the sale were completely permitted without karahah, people would be encouraged to cut and sell, leading to widespread violation of the sanctity of the Haram.
The karahah serves as a deterrent without making the sale invalid.
4
Distinguish from hunting in the Haram
Hunting in the Haram is different: the sale of game caught in the Haram is not permissible even with karahah. The difference will be explained later in the text.
This shows that not all prohibited causes have the same effect on subsequent transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ بَيْعُهُ بَعْدَ القَطِع لِأَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ بِسَبٍ مُّحْظُورٍ شَرْعًا فَلَوْ أَطْلَقَ لَهُ فِي بَيْعِهِ لَتَطَرَّقَ النَّاسُ إِلى مِثْلِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ مَعَ الْكَرَاهَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّيْدِ وَالْفَرْقُ مَا نَذَكُرُهُ

ترجمہ اور کاٹنے کے بعد اس کا بیچنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک ایسے سبب سے ہوا ہے جو شرعا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اگر اس کو اس کے بیچنے کی اجازت دے دیجائے تو لوگ اس جیسے کاموں کی طرف راہ پکڑلیں گے مگر کراہت کے ساتھ بیچنا جائز ہے برخلاف شکار کے اور فرق وہ ہے جس کو ہم ذکر کریں گے۔

تشریح مسئلہ حرم کی گھاس یا درخت کاٹ کر اس کو فروخت کرنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص اس کا مالک ایسے سبب سے ہوا ہے جو شرعاً ممنوع ہے۔ اب اگر بیچنے کی اجازت عام کر دی جائے تو جائز ہے اس کے برخلاف شکار کہ اس کو فروخت کرنا مع الکراہت بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ دونوں کے درمیان وجہ فرق آگے بیان کریں گے۔ فَانْتَظِرُوا إِنِّى مَعَكُمْ مِنَ الْمُنتَظِرِينَ -
And it is disliked to sell it after cutting, because he owned it by a cause that is prohibited in Shariah. If permission were given for its sale, people would resort to similar acts. However, sale is permissible with dislike, unlike hunting. The difference we will mention. Translation: And selling it after cutting is disliked because he became owner by a cause prohibited in Shariah. If permission were given for its sale, people would take to similar acts. But selling with dislike is permissible, unlike hunting, and the difference we will mention. Commentary: The issue: Selling grass or trees of the Haram after cutting is disliked because the person became owner by a cause prohibited in Shariah. Now if sale were generally permitted, it would be permissible. Contrary to hunting, selling it even with dislike is not permissible. The difference between the two we will mention later. So wait, I am with you among the waiters.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that selling the grass or trees of the Haram after cutting them is makruh (disliked). The reason is that the person owned them through a prohibited cause (i.e., cutting the Haram vegetation, which is forbidden). If such sales were unconditionally allowed, people would be encouraged to cut and sell. However, the sale itself is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi). This is different from hunting in the Haram, where selling the game is completely impermissible even if one owns it. The distinction will be explained later. The Arabic text quotes the matn of Hidayah, and the Urdu provides translation and commentary.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not prohibited; the sale is valid but blameworthy.
سبب محظور (sabab mahzur): A cause that is prohibited in Shariah, e.g., cutting Haram vegetation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling grass from the Haram after cutting it?
A) It is completely haram and invalid.
B) It is permissible but disliked (makruh).
C) It is mustahab.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ownership through a prohibited cause does not render the object impure or unsellable, but the sale is considered makruh to discourage the prohibited action.
