Two Payments for Cutting Trees on Private Land in the Haram
Ruling on cutting self-grown trees on private Haram land.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for cutting a living tree on private land within the Haram and explain the qiyas analogy to owned game.

Core Idea
Cutting a living tree on private land in Haram requires two payments: one for violating the Haram, one for the owner.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a tree that grows spontaneously on private land located within the boundaries of the Haram (the sacred precinct around Makkah). The ruling distinguishes between living (namī) and dried trees, and uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to the case of killing owned game in the Haram. Understanding this ruling reinforces the Hanafi principle that violations of the Haram's sanctity incur a separate penalty beyond ordinary property damages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? Cutting a tree that grows by itself on someone's private land within the Haram. The hukm: two payments are wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites no explicit text but draws qiyas (analogy) to the well-known case of killing owned game in the Haram. That case is the asl (original case) with an established ruling.
The dalil is qiyas, not a direct nass.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The illah (effective cause) is the conjunction of two violations: infringing the sanctity of the Haram (ḥurmat al-ḥaram) and destroying another's property (mal ghayr). Both violations exist in the original case of game and in the new case of trees.
The illah is explicit: violation of Haram + private ownership.
4
Note the exception
The ruling only applies to living (namī) trees. Dried trees are excluded because they are no longer 'growing' (laysa bi-nāmin), thus no guarantee (ḍamān) is due.
The condition of being 'nami' is essential.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The operative position for fatwa is that two prices are due: one as a right of Shariah for the Haram, and one as compensation (ḍamān) to the owner. This is derived from qiyas jaly and is Zahir al-Riwayah.
This ruling is relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ نَبَتَ بِنَفْسِهِ فِي مِلْكِ رَجُل فَعَلى قَاطِعِهِ قِيْمَةٌ لِحُرْمَةِ الْحَرَمِ حَقًّا لِلشَّرْعِ وَقِيمَةً أُخْرَى ضِمَانًا لِمَا لِكه كَالصَّيدِ الْمَمْلُوكِ فِى الْحَرَمِ وَمَا جَفَّ مِنْ شَجَرِ الْحَرَمِ لَا ضِمَانَ فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِنَامٍ

ترجمہ اور اگر ایسا درخت جو عادہ ہو یا نہیں جاتا خود کسی شخص کی ملک میں اگا تو اس کے کاٹنے والے پر ایک قیمت تو حق شرع حرم کی حرمت کی وجہ سے واجب ہے اور دوسری قیمت اس کے مالک کے لئے بطور تاوان واجب ہے جیسے حرم کے اندر مملوک شکار۔ اور حرم کا جو درخت خشک ہو گیا اس میں ضمان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ نامی نہیں ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ، جو درخت عادہ ہو یا نہیں جاتا اگر وہ کسی کی مملوکہ زمین میں اگ آیا اور وہ زمین داخل حرم ہے تو اس درخت کے کاٹنے والے پر دو قیمتیں واجب ہوں گی ۔ ایک تو بحق شرع احترام حرم کی وجہ سے اور دوسری قیمت اس کے مالک کے لئے بطور تاوان واجب ہو گی۔ جیسے حرم کے اندر اگر کسی کا مملوکہ شکار ہو اور دوسرا اس کو قتل کر دے تو قاتل پر دو قیمتیں واجب ہوں گی ۔ ایک احترام حرم کی وجہ سے اور دوسری قیمت مالک کے لئے بطور تاوان واجب ہوگی۔

صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ حرم کی جو گھاس یا درخت خشک ہو گیا اس کے کاٹنے پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ گھاس اور درخت نامی نہیں رہا۔ حالانکہ ضمان نامی ہی کو کاٹنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔
And if it grows by itself in the property of a man, then upon its cutter is a price due to the sanctity of the Haram as a right of Shariah, and another price as a guarantee for what is due to him, like owned game in the Haram. And what dries from the trees of the Haram, there is no guarantee for it, because it is not growing. Translation: And if a tree (whether habitually planted or not) grows by itself in someone's property, then upon the one who cuts it is one price due to the sanctity of the Haram as a right of Shariah, and another price as a guarantee for the owner, like owned game in the Haram. And for dried trees of the Haram, there is no guarantee, because it is not growing. Commentary: The issue: If a tree, whether habitually planted or not, grows in someone's owned land and that land is within the Haram, then upon the cutter are two prices: one is due to the right of Shariah out of respect for the Haram, and the other is a compensation for the owner. Like owned game in the Haram: if someone kills it, two prices are due – one for violating the Haram, one as compensation to the owner. Sahib al-Quduri says: For dried grass or trees of the Haram, cutting does not necessitate guarantee, because they are no longer growing, and guarantee is only for cutting something that is growing.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on cutting a tree that grows spontaneously on private land within the Haram. The cutter must pay two prices: one as a penalty for violating the sanctity of the Haram (a right of Allah), and another as compensation to the owner. This is analogous to killing owned game within the Haram. However, if the tree has dried up, no guarantee is due because it is no longer growing (namā'), and guarantee is only for cutting living vegetation. The commentary by Sahib al-Quduri (Imam al-Quduri) clarifies that dried plants are not subject to this ruling.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or compensation, here the price paid to the owner.
نامی (nami): Growing or capable of growth; dried plants are not nami, so no guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many prices must be paid for cutting a living tree that grows on private land within the Haram?
A) One price to the owner only.
B) One price to the Bait al-Mal only.
C) Two prices: one for Shariah (Haram) and one for the owner.
D) No price, because it is in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
Cutting a living tree on private land in the Haram incurs two compulsory payments: one for the sacred precinct and one for the property owner.

Grazing and Cutting Grass in the Haram: The Idhkhir Exception
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grazing animals in the Haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting and grazing grass in the Haram, explain the exception for Idhkhir, and evaluate Abu Yusuf's necessity argument.

Core Idea
Only Idhkhir may be cut or grazed in the Haram; grazing is prohibited even if some claim necessity.

The sanctity of the Haram extends to its vegetation. The general rule is that no grass may be cut or grazed, except for a specific plant called Idhkhir. This lesson examines the ruling, the proof, and an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding grazing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and exception
State the general prohibition and the sole exception for Idhkhir. Note what the text explicitly permits.
The Arabic reads: 'ولا يرعى حشيش الحرم ولا يقطع إلا الإذخر'.
2
Understand the dispute on grazing
Abu Yusuf permits grazing due to necessity; the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) prohibit it.
Necessity (darurah) argument: preventing animals from grazing is difficult.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The majority's proof includes a hadith and an analogy: cutting with teeth (grazing) is like cutting with scythes.
The hadith is referred to as 'ما روينا' – the established narration on Haram sanctity.
4
Evaluate the necessity claim
Grass can be brought from outside, so genuine necessity is absent. This refutes Abu Yusuf's grounds.
The text says: 'وحمل الحشيش من الجل ممكن فلا ضرورة'.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Yusuf permits grazing; the majority prohibits it. The mufta bihi is prohibition.
The tarjih relies on the majority because the necessity claim is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُرْعَى حَشِيشُ الْحَرَمِ وَلَا يُقْطَعُ إِلَّا الْإِذْحَرَ وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ لَا بَأسَ بِالرَّعَى فِيهِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ ضَرُورَةً فَإِن مَنْعُ الدَّوَاتِ عَنْهُ مُتَعَدَّرُ وَلَنَا مَارَوَيْنَا وَالْقَطْعُ بِالْمُشَافِرِ كَالْقَطِع بِالْمَنَاجِلِ وَحَمْلُ الْحَشِيشِ مِنَ الْجِلِّ مُمْكِنَّ فَلَا ضَرُورَةَ بِخِلَافِ الْإِذْخَرِ لِأَنَّهُ إِسْتَشَنَاهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَيَجُوزُ قَطْعُهُ وَرَعَيُهُ وَبِخِلَافِ الْكَمَاةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ النَّبَاتِ

ترجمہ اور حرم کی گھاس نہ چرائی جائے گی اور نہ کائی جائے گی سوائے اذخر کے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ حرم کی گھاس چرانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چرانے میں ایک ضرورت ہے۔ کیونکہ چوپاؤں کو اس سے روکنا متعذر ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم نے روایت کی۔ اور ہونٹوں اور دانتوں سے کاٹنا ایسا ہے جیسے درانتیوں سے کاٹنا۔ اور حل سے گھاس کالا دولا ناممکن ہے اس لئے حرم کی گھاس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں رہی برخلاف اذخر کے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو مستی کر دیا ہے اس لئے اس کو کاٹنا اور چھرانا جائز ہے اور برخلاف سانپ کی چھتری کے ۔ کیونکہ یہ از قبیلہ گھاس نہیں ہے۔
And the grass of the Haram is not to be grazed nor cut except Idhkhir. And Abu Yusuf said: There is no harm in grazing in it, because there is a necessity, for preventing livestock from it is difficult. And our proof is what we narrated. And cutting with lips and teeth is like cutting with scythes. And carrying the grass from outside is possible, so there is no necessity. Unlike Idhkhir, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) excepted it, so its cutting and grazing are permissible. And unlike truffles (kama'), because it is not from the category of plants. Translation: And the grass of the Haram is not to be grazed nor cut except Idhkhir. And Abu Yusuf said there is no harm in grazing in it because of necessity, as preventing animals is difficult. Our proof is the hadith we narrated. Cutting with lips and teeth is like cutting with scythes. Carrying grass from outside is possible, so no necessity. Unlike Idhkhir because the Prophet excepted it, so cutting and grazing it are permissible. Unlike kama' (truffles) because they are not from the category of plants.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on grazing and cutting grass in the Haram. The general rule is that both are prohibited except for Idhkhir (a type of fragrant grass). Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees regarding grazing, arguing that necessity permits it because preventing animals from grazing is difficult. However, the Hanafi position (supported by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that grazing is also prohibited. Their proof is a hadith (presumably the famous hadith of the Haram's sanctity) and the reasoning that cutting with teeth is like cutting with tools. Furthermore, grass can be brought from outside the Haram, eliminating any claim of necessity. Idhkhir is excepted because the Prophet specifically allowed it. Truffles (kama') are also excepted because they are not considered plants (they are fungi).

Key Terms
اذخر (idhkhir): A type of fragrant grass that the Prophet exempted from the prohibition of cutting in the Haram.
ضرورت (darurah): Necessity that might relax a prohibition; Abu Yusuf uses this argument for grazing.
كمأة (kama'): Truffles (fungi), not considered plants, so they are not covered by the prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of grass is excepted from the prohibition of cutting in the Haram?
A) Kama' (truffles)
B) Idhkhir
C) All grass
D) None

Key Takeaway
In the Haram, only Idhkhir may be cut or grazed; the majority view prohibits grazing despite Abu Yusuf's necessity argument.

Compensation for Cutting Haram Vegetation and Prohibition of Grazing
Rulings on compensations for cutting trees and prohibition of grazing in Haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for cutting trees in the Haram and explain the prohibition of grazing, including the intra-madhhab dispute with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Cutting Haram vegetation requires two compensations; grazing is prohibited as a form of cutting.

The sanctity of the Haram imposes special rules on its vegetation. This passage from the Hidayah sets out the compensations for cutting trees that grow on private land within the Haram, the general prohibition of cutting and grazing grass, and the exception for idhkhir. It also records a difference of opinion with Imam Abu Yusuf on grazing. By understanding these rulings, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school balances the inviolability of the Haram with practical necessities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the basic ruling
Read the passage and note the case: a tree that grows spontaneously on someone's private land inside the Haram. The cutter must pay two compensations – one for the sanctity of the Haram and one to the owner.
This is analogous to killing owned game in the Haram.
2
Examine the exception for dry vegetation
The text states that dry (non-growing) vegetation does not incur compensation. Understand why: compensation is only for things that are 'growing' (nami) because the value is in the potential for growth.
This is a key condition for the ruling.
3
Understand the prohibition of grazing
The passage prohibits grazing (ra'y) in the Haram, analogizing it to cutting. The proof is the hadith 'La yukhtala khaluha' – its plants are not uprooted. Grazing with teeth is equated to cutting with sickles.
This extends the prohibition beyond explicit cutting.
4
Analyze the exception for idhkhir and truffles
Idhkhir (fragrant grass) is exempted by explicit hadith; truffles are exempt because they are not considered plants. These exceptions are clear from the text.
These are the only exceptions to the prohibition of cutting.
5
Address the intra-Hanafi dispute on grazing
Imam Abu Yusuf permits grazing due to necessity. The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rejects this, arguing that necessity can be avoided by bringing grass from outside the Haram. The mufta bihi is the prohibition.
This illustrates how the school weighs practical necessity against a clear textual prohibition.

حرم کا گھاس سوائے اذخر کے نہ کاٹا جائے نہ جانور چرائے جائیں
وَلَا يُرْعَى حَشِيشُ الْحَرَمِ وَلَا يُقْطَعُ إِلَّا الْإِذْحَرَ وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ لَا بَأسَ بِالرَّعَى فِيهِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ ضَرُورَةً فَإِن مَنْعُ الدَّوَاتِ عَنْهُ مُتَعَدَّرُ وَلَنَا مَارَوَيْنَا وَالْقَطْعُ بِالْمُشَافِرِ كَالْقَطِع بِالْمَنَاجِلِ وَحَمْلُ الْحَشِيشِ مِنَ الْجِلِّ مُمْكِنَّ فَلَا ضَرُورَةَ بِخِلَافِ الْإِذْخَرِ لِأَنَّهُ إِسْتَشَنَاهُ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَيَجُوزُ قَطْعُهُ وَرَعَيُهُ وَبِخِلَافِ الْكَمَاةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ النَّبَاتِ
ترجمہ اور حرم کی گھاس نہ چرائی جائے گی اور نہ کائی جائے گی سوائے اذخر کے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے کہا کہ حرم کی گھاس چرانے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چرانے میں ایک ضرورت ہے۔ کیونکہ چوپاؤں کو اس سے روکنا متعذر ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جو ہم نے روایت کی۔ اور ہونٹوں اور دانتوں سے کاٹنا ایسا ہے جیسے درانتیوں سے کاٹنا۔ اور حل سے گھاس کالا دولا ناممکن ہے اس لئے حرم کی گھاس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں رہی برخلاف اذخر کے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کو مستی کر دیا ہے اس لئے اس کو کاٹنا اور چھرانا جائز ہے اور برخلاف سانپ کی چھتری کے ۔ کیونکہ یہ از قبیلہ گھاس نہیں ہے۔

The chapter of the (Haram). If a tree that grows without cultivation grows in someone's property and that land is inside the Haram, then two compensations are obligatory upon the one who cuts it. And if it grows by itself in a man's property, then on its cutter is one compensation due to the sanctity of the Haram, a right of the Law, and another compensation as a guarantee for the owner, like owned game in the Haram. And what has dried from the trees of the Haram has no guarantee because it is not growing. Explanation: The ruling is that if a tree that grows without cultivation grows in someone's owned land and that land is inside the Haram, then two compensations will be obligatory upon the one who cuts it. One is due to the sanctity of the Haram as a right of the Law, and the second is as a guarantee for the owner. Like if someone kills another's owned game inside the Haram, two compensations are obligatory. Sahib al-Quduri says that there is no guarantee for cutting dry grass or trees of the Haram because they are no longer growing. And the grass of the Haram is not grazed nor cut except Idhkhir. Abu Yusuf said: There is no harm in grazing in it because there is necessity; preventing animals from it is difficult. Our proof is the hadith we narrated. And cutting with lips and teeth is like cutting with sickles. And carrying grass from outside is possible, so there is no necessity. Unlike Idhkhir, because the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم exempted it, so cutting and grazing it are permissible. And unlike truffles (kama'ah), because they are not from the category of plants. Explanation: The ruling is that the grass of the Haram cannot be cut nor grazed except Idhkhir. Imam Abu Yusuf says there is no harm in grazing in the Haram; he allows grazing but not cutting. Because there is necessity: when people enter the Haram for Hajj or Umrah with riding animals, it is difficult to prevent them from grazing. Our proof is the hadith: 'Its plants are not uprooted.' As for necessity, it can be fulfilled by cutting grass from outside and bringing it. And the phrase 'cutting with lips' answers the question that the hadith prohibits cutting, not grazing. The response is that cutting with mouth and teeth (grazing) is like cutting with sickles. So if cutting with sickles is prohibited, then grazing is also prohibited. Unlike Idhkhir, because the Prophet himself exempted it. It is narrated that when the Prophet said, 'Its bushes are not uprooted nor its thorns cut,' Sayyiduna Abbas said, 'Except Idhkhir, O Messenger of Allah, for it is for their graves and houses.' He صلى الله عليه وسلم said, 'Except Idhkhir.' And unlike truffles, because they are not from the category of plants.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the penalties for cutting or grazing vegetation in the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah). The text first addresses a scenario where a tree that grows spontaneously (without cultivation) appears on someone's private property within the Haram. The cutter must pay two compensations: one as a right of the Law due to the sanctity of the Haram, and another as a guarantee (daman) to the owner. This is analogized to killing someone's owned game in the Haram. However, if the tree has dried up, no guarantee is owed because it is no longer growing (it is not 'nami' – unable to increase). The second part deals with the general prohibition of grazing or cutting grass in the Haram, except for idhkhir (a fragrant grass). Imam Abu Yusuf differed, arguing that grazing is permissible due to necessity (darurah), as preventing animals from grazing is difficult. The Hanafi response clarifies that necessity can be avoided by bringing grass from outside the Haram. The proof is the hadith 'La yukhtala khaluha' (its plants are not uprooted). Grazing is considered a form of cutting (since teeth cut grass like a sickle), so it is prohibited. The exception for idhkhir is based on the Prophet's explicit exemption (istathna) at the request of Sayyiduna Abbas. Truffles (kama'ah) are also exempt because they are not considered plants (nabat). The ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah; Abu Yusuf's view is recorded but not taken as mufta bihi.

Key Terms
حرم (Ḥaram): The sacred precinct of Makkah, including the Haramayn boundaries.
اذخر (Idhkhir): A fragrant grass used in graves and houses; exempted from the prohibition of cutting.
ضمان (Ḍamān): Guarantee or compensation for damage to property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tree grows on someone's private land within the Haram and another person cuts it, how many compensations are owed according to the Hanafi position?
A) One compensation to the owner only
B) Two compensations: one for the sanctity of the Haram and one to the owner
C) No compensation if the tree grew on its own
D) Only one compensation for the Haram's sanctity

Key Takeaway
Cutting growing vegetation in the Haram incurs two compensations; grazing is prohibited as a form of cutting, with exceptions only for idhkhir and truffles.

Qarin's Double Penalties: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on penalties for Qarin with madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of dams a Qarin must pay for a violation and explain the madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A Qarin pays double the penalty because he holds two separate ihrams, one for each pilgrimage.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the penalties (dam) for a Qarin—one who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single journey. The Hanafi school holds that a Qarin must pay two dams for any violation that would cost one dam for a Mufrid (one performing only Hajj). The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools disagree, maintaining that only one dam is owed. At stake is the very definition of the Qarin's consecration: is he in one ihram or two? Understanding this dispute illuminates how a foundational metaphysical classification (the number of ihrams) directly determines a practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the dispute
The passage states that for any jinaya (violation) requiring a dam for a Mufrid, a Qarin owes two dams. The Shafi'i school says one.
2
Locate the root cause of the disagreement
The difference stems from the nature of the Qarin's ihram. Hanafis: two ihrams (Hajj and Umrah separately). Others: one ihram.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi subtlety
The passage mentions an exception: if the Qarin passes the miqat without any ihram, he owes only one dam (per Imam Muhammad, contra Imam Zufar).
This shows how the school refines its own position.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: double the penalty for the Qarin in the Hanafi school, affecting Hajj rituals for those combining Hajj and Umrah.

And if the Qarin commits any of the mentioned violations, then two dams are obligatory. And every thing that the Qarin does from what we mentioned that on the Mufrid there is a dam, then on him are two dams: a dam for his Hajj and a dam for his Umrah. And Al-Shafi'i said: one dam, based on the fact that he is a Muhrim with one ihram according to him, and according to us with two ihrams, and it has passed before. He (Al-Quduri) said: except that he passes the miqat without being in the state of ihram for Umrah or Hajj, then one dam is obligatory, contrary to Zufar, because what is due at the miqat is one ihram, and by delaying one wajib, only one compensation is obligatory. Explanation: The ruling is that if a Mufrid (one performing Hajj only) commits one of the mentioned violations and owes one dam, then a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah combined) owes two dams: one for his Hajj and one for his Umrah. Imam Shafi'i said that the Qarin owes only one dam, and this is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. The basis of the difference is that according to them the Qarin is a Muhrim with one ihram, while according to us he is a Muhrim with two ihrams. The proofs have passed in the chapter on Qiran. Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with inter-madhhab dispute concerning the penalty (dam) for a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in one journey) when he commits one of the jinayat (violations) previously mentioned (such as shaving hair, wearing sewn clothes, etc.). The text states that if a Mufrid (one performing only Hajj) would owe one dam for such a violation, then a Qarin owes two dams: one for his Hajj and one for his Umrah. This is because in the Hanafi school, the Qarin has two separate ihrams. Imam al-Shafi'i (and also Malik and Ahmad) hold that only one dam is due, because they consider the Qarin to be in a single state of ihram. The Hanafi school bases its position on the principle that the Qarin intends both Hajj and Umrah, each with its own ihram, as established earlier in the chapter on Qiran. The text also includes a special case: if the Qarin passes the miqat without having entered ihram for either Hajj or Umrah (i.e., he delays both), then he owes only one dam, according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (as quoted by Al-Quduri). Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that since only one wajib (the ihram at the miqat) was delayed, only one compensation is needed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Muhammad, as the text mentions. The ruling in the Zahir al-Riwayah is as stated: two dams for each violation, except the miqat case with one dam.

Key Terms
قارن (Qārin): A person performing Hajj and Umrah together in one state of ihram (according to Hanafi: two ihrams).
دم (Dam): A penalty of slaughtering a sheep/goat (or equivalent) for violating ihram rules.
مفرد (Mufrid): A person performing only Hajj (not Umrah) in a separate trip.

Grazing in the Haram: Prohibition and Exceptions
Ruling on grazing in the Haram with hadith proof and objection rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on grazing in the Haram, explain the analogy used to extend the prohibition from cutting to grazing, and identify the exceptions for Idhkhir and non-grass plants.

Core Idea
Grazing in the Haram is prohibited because it is legally equivalent to cutting grass with a tool.

This passage addresses a practical question: is it permissible for animals to graze inside the sacred precincts of Makkah? While the hadith explicitly prohibits cutting grass, grazing is not directly mentioned. By using legal analogy (qiyas), the Hanafi school shows that grazing falls under the same prohibition. The passage also clarifies the well-known exception for Idhkhir grass and another for non-grass plants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the act being ruled upon: grazing animals inside the Haram. What is the initial impression from the hadith?
The hadith only mentions cutting, not grazing.
2
Understand the primary proof
Analyze the hadith 'Its grass is not cut' as a general prohibition. Recognize that this is a clear text but limited to cutting.
The exception for Idhkhir shows the general rule is established.
3
Analyze the objection
Consider the objection: grazing is not explicitly prohibited, so why is it prohibited? This is a common point of confusion.
4
Learn the Hanafi response via analogy
The author uses qiyas: cutting with the mouth is analogous to cutting with a sickle. Since the tool is replaced by the mouth, the act remains prohibited.
The analogy is based on the common cause (illa) of removing grass.
5
Note the exceptions
Identify the two exceptions: Idhkhir grass (explicitly exempted by the Prophet) and snake fungus (not considered grass).
These exceptions confirm that the prohibition applies only to grass-type vegetation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کاٹنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے کیونکہ چرانے میں ضرورت ہے اور ضرورت یہ ہے کہ جب لوگ حج یا عمرہ کے لئے حرم میں داخل ہوں گے اور ان کے ساتھ سواری کے جانور بھی ہوں گے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ جانوروں کو چرنے سے روکنا متعذر ہے۔ اس لئے چرانے کی ضرورت محقق ہوگئی۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو سابق میں روایت کیا گیا۔ یعنی لا یختلى خلاها ۔ اور رہی ضرورت تو وہ اس سے پوری ہو سکتی ہے کہ گھاس حل سے کاٹ کر جانوروں پر لاد کر لائی جائے ۔ وَالْقَطْعُ بِالْمَشافِر سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں حرم کی گھاس کاٹنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے، چرانے سے منع نہیں کیا گیا اس لئے چرانے کی اجازت ہونی چاہئے ۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ منہ اور دانت لگا کر گھاس کاٹنا یعنی چرنا ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ درانتیوں سے کاٹنا۔ پس جب درانتی سے کاٹنا ممنوع ہے تو منہ لگا کر کاٹنا یعنی چرانا بھی ممنوع ہوگا بر خلاف اذخر گھاس کے کیونکہ اسکا خود رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ جب رسول اکرم نے فرمایا لَا يُخْتَلَى خِلاهَا وَلَا يُعْضَدُ شَوْكُها - تو حضرت عباس نے فرمایا إِلَّا الإِذْخَرَ يَا رَسُولَ اللهِ ( صلى الله عليه وسلم ) فَإِنَّهُ لقُبُورِهِمْ وَ بُيُوتِهِمْ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِلَّا الْاِذْخَر یعنی آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ حرم کی گھاس نہ کائی جائے اور نہ اس کے کانٹے توڑے جائیں، حضرت عباس نے کہا اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم سوائے اذخر کے کیونکہ یہ قبروں اور گھروں میں خوشبو کے لئے استعمال کی جانے والی چیز ہے تو آپ نے بھی فرمایا کہ ہاں سوائے اذخر کے۔ اور برخلاف سانپ کی چھتری کے یعنی سانپ کی چھتری جو بالعموم برسمات وغیرہ میں نکلتی ہے حرم کے اندر اس کا کا شنا بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ از قبیلہ گھاس نہیں ہے۔
Permission to cut (grass) is not given, because there is a need for grazing, and the need is that when people enter the Haram for Hajj or Umrah, they have riding animals with them, and it is obvious that preventing the animals from grazing is difficult. Therefore the need for grazing is established. And our proof is the hadith narrated previously: 'Its grass is not cut.' As for the need, it can be fulfilled by cutting grass from the Halal and loading it onto the animals. And 'cutting with the lips' is an answer to an objection. The objection is that the hadith prohibits cutting the grass of the Haram, not grazing, so grazing should be permitted. The answer is that cutting grass with the mouth and teeth, i.e., grazing, is like cutting with sickles. So when cutting with sickles is prohibited, cutting with the mouth, i.e., grazing, is also prohibited, contrary to idhkhir grass, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) himself made an exception for it. Thus it is narrated that when the Messenger said: 'Its grass is not cut and its thorns are not broken,' Abbas said: 'Except idhkhir, O Messenger of Allah, for it is for their graves and homes.' He (peace be upon him) said: 'Except idhkhir.' And contrary to the snake umbrella (a type of fungus), which commonly grows in marshy areas; uprooting it inside the Haram is permissible because it is not of the category of grass.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the prohibition of grazing in the Haram. The author first states the ruling: cutting grass in the Haram is forbidden, but there is an objection that grazing is necessary and not explicitly mentioned in the prohibition. The author answers this by making an analogy: using the mouth to cut grass (grazing) is legally equivalent to using a tool to cut grass, since the act of cutting is the same. Therefore the prohibition covers both. The hadith quoted is famous: 'Its grass is not cut and its thorns are not broken.' The exception for Idhkhir (a fragrant grass) is established by the hadith where Abbas requested it and the Prophet agreed. Another exception is the snake umbrella (a type of fungus), which is not grass, so it can be uprooted. The Hanafi position is that grazing is forbidden, as it falls under the general prohibition of cutting; necessity does not override this because one can bring grass from outside the Haram.

Key Terms
لا یختلى خلاها (lā yukhtalā khilāhā): Its grass is not cut or uprooted; a prohibition from the hadith regarding the Haram's vegetation.
اذخر (idhkhir): A fragrant grass used in graves and homes; the Prophet specifically exempted it from the prohibition of cutting in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
Grazing in the Haram is prohibited via analogy to cutting grass, with explicit exceptions for Idhkhir and non-grass plants.

The Qarin's Double Penalty: Two Dam for Violations
Inter-madhhab dispute: Qarin's double dam vs Shafi'i single dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a Qarin owes two dam for a violation requiring one dam for a Mufrid, and explain why, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A Qarin owes two dam because he has two independent ihrams.

This lesson addresses a key dispute in Hajj penalties: how many blood sacrifices (dam) must a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) offer when he commits a violation that would cost a Mufrid one dam? The Hanafi school, based on the principle that the Qarin has two separate ihrams, holds that he owes two dam. The Shafi'i school disagrees, viewing the Qarin as having a single ihram. Understanding this difference is crucial for correct practice and for appreciating how madhhab principles generate rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default penalty
Start with the Mufrid baseline: any violation during ihram (e.g., hunting, cutting nails) that requires one dam. This is agreed upon.
Violations include those that incur dam for a Mufrid as defined earlier in the text.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for the Qarin
For the same violation, the Qarin owes two dam: one for his Hajj ihram and one for his Umrah ihram, because in the Hanafi view he has two separate states of ihram.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only one dam is due, basing this on his view that the Qarin has a single ihram combining both rituals.
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools generally follow this view.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi Qarin must slaughter two animals for the violation, while a Shafi'i Qarin must slaughter only one.
This directly affects the pilgrim's expenditure and ritual acts.
5
Locate the evidence for the Hanafi view
The proof lies in the established distinction between the Qarin and Mufrid as discussed earlier (Bab al-Qiran). The Qarin is considered muhrim with two ihrams, each independent.
The text references earlier passages: 'It has passed before.'

وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ فَعَلَهُ الْقَارِنُ مِمَّا ذَكَرْنَا أَنَّ فِيهِ عَلَى الْمُفْرِدِ دَمَّا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَان دَم لِحَجَّتِهِ وَدَم لِعُمْرَتِهِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ دَمٌ وَاحِدٌ بِناءً على أنَّهُ مُحْرِمَا بِإحْرَامِ وَاحِدٍ عِندَهُ وَعِندَنَا بِاحْرَامَيْنِ وَ قَدْ مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ قَالَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَجَاوَزَ الْمِيقَاتَ غَيْرُ مُحْرَمِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ أَوِ الْحَجَ فَيَلْزَمُهُ دَمَ وَاحِدٌ خِلَافًا لَزُفَرَ لِمَا أَنَّ الْمُسْتَحَقَ عَلَيْهِ عِندَ الْمِيقَاتِ احرام وَاحِدٌ وَبتَاخِيرِ وَاجِب وَاحِدٍ لَا يَجِبُ الْاجَزَاء وَاحِدٌ ترجمہ اور ہر وہ چیز جس کو قارن نے امور مذکورہ میں سے کیا اگر اس میں مفرد پر ایک دم ہے تو قارن پر دو دم واجب ہوں گے۔ ایک دم اسکے حج کی وجہ یس اور ایک دم اسکے عمرہ کی وجہ سے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ایک دم واجب ہے اس پر بنا ء کرتے ہوئے کہ ان کے نزدیک وہ ایک احترام کے ساتھ محرم ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک دو احراموں کے ساتھ محرم ہے اور ہی پہلے گذر چکا ۔ قدوری نے کہا علاوہ اسکے که قارن بغیر احرام عمرہ یا احرام حج کے میقات سے تجاوز کر جائے۔ تو اس پر ایک دم لازم ہو گا۔ امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ میقات کے وقت اس پر ایک احرام واجب ہے اور ایک واجب کی تاخیر سے ایک ہی جزاء واجب ہوگی۔
And every thing that the Qarin does from what we mentioned that for the Mufrid there is one dam, then upon him are two dam: a dam for his Hajj and a dam for his Umrah. And al-Shafi'i said: one dam, based on the fact that according to him he is muhrim with one ihram, and according to us with two ihrams. And it has passed before. He (al-Quduri) said: Except if he passes the miqat without being muhrim for Umrah or Hajj, then one dam is incumbent upon him, contrary to Zufar, because what is required at the miqat is one ihram, and for delaying one wajib, one recompense is due, not two.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'i, with an intra-Hanafi difference with Zufar. The core issue: when a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) commits a violation that would require a dam for a Mufrid (one performing only one), how many dam does he owe? The Hanafi position, based on the principle that the Qarin has two separate ihrams (one for Hajj, one for Umrah), is that he owes two dam. Shafi'i holds he owes one, considering the Qarin has a single ihram. The author then mentions an exception noted by al-Quduri: if the Qarin passes the miqat without being in ihram for either, then only one dam is due because only one ihram was required at that point. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees and says two dam are due even in that case, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is one dam. The reasoning is that at the miqat, the obligation to enter ihram is one; delaying one wajib only incurs one penalty.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim performing Hajj and Umrah together in one state of ihram (according to Hanafis, two ihrams).
دم (dam): Blood penalty (usually slaughtering a sheep or goat) required for certain violations during ihram.
مفرد (mufrid): A pilgrim performing only Hajj or only Umrah, not both together (the default for which penalties are determined).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many dam does a Qarin owe for a violation that requires one dam for a Mufrid?
A) One dam, because it is one act.
B) Two dam, because he has two ihrams.
C) None, because Qarin is exempt from penalties.
D) One dam, unless he passes the miqat without ihram.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must slaughter two animals for a violation that costs a Mufrid one, because his two ihrams each attract an independent penalty.

The Miqat Exception: When a Qarin Owes Only One Dam
Intra-Hanafi nuance: exception for miqat passing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the exceptional case where a Qarin owes only one dam, explain the reasoning, and contrast the majority Hanafi view with that of Zufar.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram costs only one dam because only one ihram was obligatory at that moment.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a Qarin generally owes two dam for violations. However, there is a notable exception: if the Qarin passes the miqat without assuming ihram for either Hajj or Umrah, he owes only one dam. This exception, derived by al-Quduri, is based on the principle that at the miqat, only one ihram is due. The Hanafi scholar Zufar disagrees and insists on two dam even in this case. This lesson examines the reasoning behind the exception and the intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule
Remember that a Qarin normally owes two dam for any violation that costs a Mufrid one dam. This is due to his two independent ihrams.
Refer to Lesson 1 for the full context.
2
Identify the exceptional scenario
The exception occurs when the Qarin passes the miqat (the boundary for entering ihram) without being in the state of ihram for either Hajj or Umrah. He then must slaughter one dam as a penalty for delaying the ihram.
This scenario is separate from violations during ihram; it concerns the failure to enter ihram at the proper time and place.
3
Understand the reasoning
At the moment of passing the miqat, the pilgrim is obligated to assume only one ihram (since he can enter for either Hajj or Umrah). The Qarin's failure to do so results in delay of one wajib, so only one penalty (one dam) is incurred.
The penalty is for delaying a single obligation, not for violating two ihrams.
4
Contrast with Zufar's view
Zufar, a well-known Hanafi scholar, held that even in this case, two dam are due. He argued that the Qarin still has two ihrams to assume, so delaying both should incur two penalties.
Zufar's view is rejected by the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as stated in the source.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that only one dam is owed in this exceptional case. This is the view of al-Quduri and the three major Imams.
The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as it aligns with the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ فَعَلَهُ الْقَارِنُ مِمَّا ذَكَرْنَا أَنَّ فِيهِ عَلَى الْمُفْرِدِ دَمَّا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَان دَم لِحَجَّتِهِ وَدَم لِعُمْرَتِهِ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ دَمٌ وَاحِدٌ بِناءً على أنَّهُ مُحْرِمَا بِإحْرَامِ وَاحِدٍ عِندَهُ وَعِندَنَا بِاحْرَامَيْنِ وَ قَدْ مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ قَالَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَجَاوَزَ الْمِيقَاتَ غَيْرُ مُحْرَمِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ أَوِ الْحَجَ فَيَلْزَمُهُ دَمَ وَاحِدٌ خِلَافًا لَزُفَرَ لِمَا أَنَّ الْمُسْتَحَقَ عَلَيْهِ عِندَ الْمِيقَاتِ احرام وَاحِدٌ وَبتَاخِيرِ وَاجِب وَاحِدٍ لَا يَجِبُ الْاجَزَاء وَاحِدٌ ترجمہ اور ہر وہ چیز جس کو قارن نے امور مذکورہ میں سے کیا اگر اس میں مفرد پر ایک دم ہے تو قارن پر دو دم واجب ہوں گے۔ ایک دم اسکے حج کی وجہ یس اور ایک دم اسکے عمرہ کی وجہ سے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ایک دم واجب ہے اس پر بنا ء کرتے ہوئے کہ ان کے نزدیک وہ ایک احترام کے ساتھ محرم ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک دو احراموں کے ساتھ محرم ہے اور ہی پہلے گذر چکا ۔ قدوری نے کہا علاوہ اسکے که قارن بغیر احرام عمرہ یا احرام حج کے میقات سے تجاوز کر جائے۔ تو اس پر ایک دم لازم ہو گا۔ امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے کیونکہ میقات کے وقت اس پر ایک احرام واجب ہے اور ایک واجب کی تاخیر سے ایک ہی جزاء واجب ہوگی۔
And every thing that the Qarin does from what we mentioned that for the Mufrid there is one dam, then upon him are two dam: a dam for his Hajj and a dam for his Umrah. And al-Shafi'i said: one dam, based on the fact that according to him he is muhrim with one ihram, and according to us with two ihrams. And it has passed before. He (al-Quduri) said: Except if he passes the miqat without being muhrim for Umrah or Hajj, then one dam is incumbent upon him, contrary to Zufar, because what is required at the miqat is one ihram, and for delaying one wajib, one recompense is due, not two.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'i, with an intra-Hanafi difference with Zufar. The core issue: when a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) commits a violation that would require a dam for a Mufrid (one performing only one), how many dam does he owe? The Hanafi position, based on the principle that the Qarin has two separate ihrams (one for Hajj, one for Umrah), is that he owes two dam. Shafi'i holds he owes one, considering the Qarin has a single ihram. The author then mentions an exception noted by al-Quduri: if the Qarin passes the miqat without being in ihram for either, then only one dam is due because only one ihram was required at that point. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees and says two dam are due even in that case, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is one dam. The reasoning is that at the miqat, the obligation to enter ihram is one; delaying one wajib only incurs one penalty.

Key Terms
ميقات (mīqāt): The designated boundary for entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
جنایات (jināyāt): Violations or offences committed during ihram (e.g., hunting, cutting nails, applying perfume).
تاخير واجب (ta'khīr wājib): Delaying an obligatory act (here, entering ihram at the miqat), which incurs a compensatory dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how many dam does a Qarin owe for passing the miqat without entering ihram?
A) Two dam, because he is a Qarin.
B) One dam, because only one ihram was required at that point.
C) None, because the act is not a violation.
D) Two dam, as Zufar holds.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who passes the miqat without ihram owes only one dam, contrary to Zufar's two, because the immediate obligation was a single ihram.

Two Muhrims Sharing in Killing Game: Full Penalty Each
Ruling on joint hunting penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that each muhrim who participates in killing game owes a full penalty, and distinguish it from shared liability.

Core Idea
Joint action does not divide guilt: each muhrim pays a full penalty.

In the state of ihram, hunting is prohibited. But what happens when two muhrims together kill a single game animal? Does the penalty get split? The Hanafi school rules clearly: each is fully liable. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is two muhrims jointly killing one game animal. The ruling: each owes a complete penalty (jaza').
Penalty means sacrificing an animal or its equivalent value.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) based on the principle that each participant commits an independent violation (jinayah).
The dalil is aqli (rational) not naqli.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: each muhrim becomes a perpetrator of a violation. Since the violation is personal, the penalty is not shared. Multiple violations lead to multiple penalties.
This contrasts with cases where the act is considered a single shared violation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may split the penalty, viewing the joint killing as a single violation. The Hanafi school insists on full penalty per person.
The difference arises from how each school defines the 'cause' of the penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ مُحْرِمَان فِى قَتْلِ صَيْدٍ فَعَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا جَزَاء كَامِل لِأَنَّ كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالشِّرَكَةِ يُصِيرُ جَانِيًا حِنَايَةً تَفَوُّقُ الدَّلَالَةَ فَيَتَعَدَّدُ الْجَزَاء بِتَعَددِ الْجَنايَةِ ترجمہ اور اگر ایک شکار کے قتل کرنے میں دو محرم شریک ہو گئے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پوری جزاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک شرکت کی وجہ سے ایسی جنایت کرنے والا ہو گیا جو دلالت سے بڑھ کر ہے۔ پس تعدد جنایت کی وجہ سے جزاء بھی متعدد ہوگی۔
And if two muhrims participate in killing a game animal, then upon each one of them is a complete penalty (jaza'), because each one of them, by participation, becomes a perpetrator of a violation that is beyond indication (i.e., a full violation). So the penalty multiplies with the multiplicity of the violation.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage states a ruling with proof via reasoning. The ruling: if two persons in the state of ihram jointly kill one game animal, each must pay a full penalty (like slaughtering a sheep or its equivalent in value). The reasoning: each person is individually committing a violation (the act of hunting while in ihram). The fact that they are partners does not reduce the violation; each is fully liable. The penalty is not divided because the violation is personal. This is analogous to jointly killing a human in ihram? Actually it's specific to hunting violations. The Hanafi school applies the principle of multiple violations leading to multiple penalties.

Key Terms
جزاء (jazā'): The penalty for hunting or killing game while in ihram; it is usually an animal sacrifice or its equivalent value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One penalty divided between them.
B) Each owes half a penalty.
C) Each owes a full penalty.
D) No penalty because they acted together.

Key Takeaway
Each muhrim who participates in killing game owes a full penalty; participation does not split liability.

Two Halalis Killing Game of Haram: One Penalty
Ruling that two non-muhrim persons jointly killing Haram game owe one penalty together

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two non-muhrim persons jointly kill Haram game and explain the qiyas proof that yields one collective penalty.

Core Idea
When two non-muhrims kill one game in the Haram, they owe one collective penalty because it is compensation for the animal, not punishment for the act.

In this passage, al-Hidayah clarifies a specific case of hunting in the Haram: two people who are not in ihram (halali) together kill a single game animal. The ruling is that they owe only one penalty between them. The author explains the reasoning and supports it with a clear analogy to accidental killing of a human. Understanding this distinction — between the penalty as compensation (daman) versus expiation — is essential for correctly applying the rules of hunting in the sanctuary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is two non-muhrim persons (halalis) participating in killing a game animal of the Haram. The ruling: upon them is one penalty (jaza') collectively.
Note that the subject is 'halali' (non-muhrim), not muhrim — this is key.
2
Understand the underlying reason (illah)
The penalty is described as daman (compensation) for the 'mahal' (the animal), not as a penalty for the violation (jinaayah). Since the compensation is for the animal, and the animal is one, the compensation is one.
Contrast with the muhrim case where the penalty is for the violation itself, so each muhrim owes a full penalty.
3
Trace the qiyas (analogy)
The author draws an analogy: two men who accidentally kill one man owe one diyah (blood money) collectively, but each also owes an individual kaffarah. The diyah is shared because it compensates the loss of one life; the kaffarah is individual because it is an expiation for each act.
In the Haram game case, the ruling only mentions the collective jaza', not individual kaffarah. The passage focuses on the daman aspect.
4
Apply the distinction between halali and muhrim
If the hunters were muhrim (in ihram), each would owe a separate penalty because the penalty is for the sin (jinaayah) of hunting while in ihram, not just compensation for the animal.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh; other schools may rule differently.
5
Recognize the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that two halalis owe one penalty together. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is operative for fatwa.
There is no intra-Hanafi dispute recorded in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ حَلَالَانِ فِى قَتْلِ صَيْدِ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِمَا جَزَاء وَاحِدٌ لِأَنَّ الصَّمَانَ بَدَلَّ عَنِ الْمَحَلَّ لَأَجَزَاء عَنِ الْجَنَايَةِ فَيَتَّحِدُ بِاتِّحَادِ الْمَحَل كَرَجُلَيْنِ قَتَلَا رَجُلًا خَطَأَ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِمَا دِيَةٌ وَاحِدَةً وَعَلَى كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا كَفَّارَةٌ ترجمہ اور اگر دو حلال آدمی ایک حرم کے شکار کے قتل میں شریک ہوئے تو ان دونوں پر ایک جزاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ضمان تو محل یعنی شکار کا بدل ہے نہ کہ جنایت کی جزاء ۔ پس محل کے متحد ہونے سے اسکا تاوان بھی واحد ہو گا۔ جیسے دو آدمیوں نے ایک آدمی کو خطا قتل کیا تو دونوں پر ایک دیت واجب ہوگی۔ اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر کفارہ واجب ہو گا۔
And if two halalis (non-muhrim persons) participate in killing a game animal of the Haram, then upon them both is one penalty (jaza'), because the compensation (daman) is a substitute for the thing (the animal), not a penalty for the violation. So it is united by the unity of the thing, like two men who accidentally kill a man: one blood-money (diyah) is required from them both, and upon each one of them is a kaffarah (expiation).
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof by analogy. The ruling: if two persons who are not in ihram (halali) jointly kill a game animal that is sacred due to being in the Haram (Sanctuary) area, they owe only one penalty (jaza') between them. The reason: the penalty here is not a punishment for a violation (like in the case of a muhrim), but rather a compensation for the value of the animal. Since the animal is one, the compensation is one. The author draws an analogy with the case of two people accidentally killing one person: they owe one diyah (blood-money) collectively, but each owes a kaffarah individually because the kaffarah is for the act of killing. Similarly here, the one penalty is for the animal, but each may owe a separate kaffarah if there is one? The passage does not explicitly mention kaffarah for this case, but the analogy implies that the kaffarah applies per person. However, the ruling specifically says one jaza' on both.

Key Terms
حلال (ḥalāl): A person not in the state of ihram (i.e., non-muhrim).
صید الحرم (ṣayd al-ḥaram): Game animals or birds that are protected within the boundaries of the Haram (Makkah and its sanctuary).
ضمان (ḍamān): Compensation; a financial liability for destroying property. Here it means the value of the killed animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Each owes a full penalty.
B) They owe one penalty shared between them.
C) No penalty because they are not in ihram.
D) Each owes a half penalty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two non-muhrims jointly kill Haram game, the penalty is one collective because it compensates for the animal, not for the act of hunting.

Nullity of Muhrim's Sale of Game
Ruling on the invalidity of a muhrim's sale or purchase of game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's sale of game and explain the two-part reasoning (ta'lil) that renders the sale batil.

Core Idea
For a muhrim, game is not tradeable—selling it alive violates its inviolability, selling it dead is selling carrion.

This lesson examines a specific prohibition during ihram: the invalidity of any transaction involving game (sayd) by a muhrim. The Hanafi madhhab holds that such a sale is absolutely void (batil), not merely prohibited. The reasoning is tied to the loss of the animal's security (amn) and the status of dead game as carrion (maytah). Understanding this ruling reinforces the comprehensive nature of ihram restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? A muhrim selling or buying game (sayd). The ruling is batil (void).
Note that both sale and purchase are included.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the author's ta'lil (reasoning) based on the nature of the act: the game's inviolability and the status of dead game.
The proof is not a specific text but a legal rationale.
3
Analyze the first scenario: selling alive
Selling a live game animal during ihram removes its security (amn), which the muhrim must preserve. This renders the transaction an encroachment (ta'arud).
The game's amn is a legal inviolability during ihram.
4
Analyze the second scenario: selling dead
If the muhrim kills the game and then sells it, it becomes maytah (carrion). Selling maytah is impermissible and void.
Maytah is not legally valuable (ghayr mutaqawwim).
5
Conclude the overall ruling
In both cases, the subject matter is not legally valuable for the muhrim, so the sale is batil.
This is the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا بَاعَ الْمُحْرِمُ الصَّيْدَ أَوِ ابْتَاعَهُ فَالْبَيْعُ بَاطِلٌ لأنَّ بَيعَهُ حَيًّا تَعرُّضُ لِلصَّيدِ بتفويت الأمن وبيعه بِتَفْوِيْتِ وَبَيْعَهُ بَعْدَ مَا قَتَلَهُ بيع ميتةٍ
And when a muhrim sells game or buys it, the sale is invalid because his selling it alive is an encroachment upon the game by removing its security, and his selling it after he has killed it is the sale of a dead thing.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi madhhab: any transaction involving game by a muhrim (whether buyer or seller) is absolutely invalid (batil). The reasoning is twofold: if the animal is sold alive, the muhrim violates the inviolability (amn) that the game enjoys in the state of ihram; if sold after killing, the meat is carrion (maytah), which cannot be sold. Hence, the sale is void in either case. The Urdu commentary adds that the game is a non-fungible property (ghayr mutaqawwim) for the muhrim, thus its sale is invalid.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to prohibitions including hunting.
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are permissible to hunt outside ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a muhrim's sale of a living game animal invalid?
A) Because the animal is sacred and cannot be owned
B) Because it removes the animal's security (amn) which is a violation
C) Because the muhrim is not the owner
D) Because the sale is done for profit

Key Takeaway
A muhrim's sale or purchase of game is utterly void (batil) because it violates the inviolability of the game or involves carrion.

Penalty for Removing Game from Haram: The Transfer of 'Amn' to Offspring
Ruling on penalty for removing game from Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for removing a game animal from the Haram, explain the legal reasoning for the transfer of security (amn) to offspring, and apply the exception when the penalty is paid before birth.

Core Idea
Removing game from the Haram incurs a penalty for both mother and unborn offspring, but paying the mother's penalty removes the claim.

This lesson examines a specific case from Hanafi fiqh: a person removes a pregnant gazelle from the Haram, and the offspring born later dies. What penalty is due? The ruling hinges on a key legal attribute—the inviolability (amn) that the Haram grants to game animals. Understanding how this attribute transfers to the offspring and when it ceases is essential for correctly applying the penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act (removing a gazelle from the Haram)? The ruling: wajib penalty (jaza') for both mother and offspring if they die.
The act itself is prohibited; the penalty is a compensation.
2
Understand the legal basis
Why must a penalty be paid? Because the game retains a legal right to security (amn) even after removal; returning it is obligatory.
The amn is a shar'i attribute that persists.
3
Analyze the transfer of the attribute
The 'amn' is a shar'i attribute that transfers to the offspring, so the offspring is also protected.
This is stated explicitly in the text: 'وهذا صفة شرعية فتر إلى الولد'.
4
Identify the exception
If the penalty for the mother is paid before she gives birth, the offspring is no longer protected because the substitute (khalaf) is like the original.
Payment of the penalty removes the amn attribute entirely.
5
Apply to hypothetical scenarios
For example, if only the mother dies, penalty for her; if offspring die before penalty paid, penalty for them as well.
The rule is consistent: amn transfers until the debt is settled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَخْرَجَ ظَبْيَةً مِّنَ الْحَرَمِ فَوَلَدَتْ أَوْلَادًا فَمَاتَتْ هِيَ وَأَوْلَادُهَا فَعَلَيْهِ جَزَاؤُهُنَّ لأنَّ الصَّيدَ بَعْدَ الإخراجِ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ بَقِيَ مُسْتَحَقَّا لِلأُمْنِ شَرْعًا وَلِهَذَا وَجَبَ رَدُّهُ إِلى مَأْمَنِهِ وَهَذَا صِفَةٌ شَرْعِيَّةٌ فَتَسْرى إِلَى الْوَلَدِ فَإِنْ أَدَّى جَزَاءَهَا ثُمَّ وَلَدَتْ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ جَزَاءُ الْوَلَدِ لِأَنَّ بَعْدَ أَدَاءِ الْجَزَاءِ لَمْ تَبْقَ آمِنَةً لِأَنَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلَفِ كَوُصُولِ الْأَصْلِ
And whoever removes a gazelle from the Haram, and she gives birth to offspring, then she and her offspring die, then upon him is their penalty because the game after removal from the Haram remains entitled to security (amn) legally, and therefore it is obligatory to return it to its place of security, and this is a legal characteristic that extends to the offspring. Then if he pays her penalty and then she gives birth, there is no penalty upon him for the offspring because after paying the penalty she is no longer secure, since the arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage discusses the penalty (jaza') due from a person who removes a game animal (here a gazelle) from the sacred precincts of the Haram (Mecca or Madina). The penalty is required for both the mother and any offspring born after removal, even if the offspring die. The reasoning is that the characteristic of being entitled to security (amn) is a legal attribute that transfers to the offspring. However, if the person has already paid the penalty for the mother before she gives birth, then no further penalty is due for the offspring because the payment of the substitute (khalaf) is equivalent to returning the original. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this applies whether the person is muhrim or not.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation or penalty for harming a game animal in the Haram or in ihram, typically by sacrificing an equivalent animal.
أمن (amn): Security or inviolability granted to game within the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone removes a gazelle from the Haram and later pays its penalty, then the gazelle gives birth and dies, what is the ruling?
A) No penalty for the offspring
B) Penalty for the offspring as well
C) Only penalty for the mother
D) The person is free from all penalties

Key Takeaway
Removing game from the Haram incurs a penalty for both mother and offspring, but paying the mother's penalty before birth exempts the offspring.

Crossing the Miqat Without Ihram: Three Hanafi Views on Returning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nullifying dam by returning to miqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on whether returning to the miqat after entering ihram nullifies the dam, and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
Returning to the miqat in ihram can nullify the dam, but Abu Hanifa requires talbiyah; Zufar says it never does.

When an afaqi crosses the miqat without ihram, a dam becomes wajib. But what if he later enters ihram and returns to the miqat before performing Umrah? Does the penalty drop? The Hanafi school has three views, each grounded in a different understanding of tadarak (making up) and the rights of the miqat. This lesson unpacks the dispute, its proofs, and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial obligation
The miqat is crossed without ihram → a dam becomes wajib. Then the person enters ihram elsewhere and returns to the miqat. What happens to the dam?
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: dam nullified only if he returns and recites talbiyah. Sahibayn: dam nullified merely by returning in ihram. Zufar: dam never nullified by return.
These are the three views within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the qiyas reasoning
Zufar analogizes to leaving Arafat early: returning after sunset does not cancel the penalty. The majority reject this because in Arafat the omitted act cannot be made up, whereas crossing the miqat without ihram can be remedied by returning before Umrah actions.
The key distinction is whether the omitted act can be made up in its proper time.
4
Examine the internal difference between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
Sahibayn say returning in ihram is enough because it shows respect to the miqat. Abu Hanifa adds talbiyah because the concession of delaying ihram requires initiating talbiyah to fulfill the miqat's right.
This difference hinges on what 'making up' entails: mere presence or active talbiyah.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If a person returns in ihram without talbiyah, Abu Hanifa says dam remains, Sahibayn say it is removed. The practical fatwa often follows the more precautionary view.
Know the operative ruling for fatwa in your context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابٌ مُجَاوَزَةِ الْوَقْتِ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامِ
وَإِذَا أَتَى الْكُوفِيُّ بُسْتَانَ بَنِي عَامِرٍ فَأَحْرَمَ بِعُمْرَةٍ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَى ذَاتِ عِرْقٍ وَلَبَّى بَطَلَ عَنْهُ دَمُ الْوَقْتِ وَإِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ وَلَمْ يُلَبِّ حَتَّى دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ وَطَافَ لِعُمْرَتِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا إِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ مُحْرِمًا فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ لَبَّى أَوْ لَمْ يُلَبِّ وَقَالَ زُفَرُ لَا يُسْقِطُ لَبَّى أَوْ لَمْ يُلَبِّ لِأَنَّ جِنَايَتَهُ لَمْ تَرْتَفِعْ بِالْعَوْدِ وَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَفَاضَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ ثُمَّ عَادَ إِلَيْهِ بَعْدَ الْغُرُوبِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ تَدَارَكَ الْمَتْرُوكَ فِي أَوَانِهِ وَذَلِكَ قَبْلَ الشُّرُوعِ فِي الْأَفْعَالِ فَيَسْقُطُ الدَّمُ بِخِلَافِ الْإِفَاضَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَتَدَارَكِ الْمَتْرُوكَ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ غَيْرَ أَنَّ التَّدَارُكَ عِنْدَهُمَا بِعَوْدِهِ مُحْرِمًا لِأَنَّهُ أَظْهَرَ حَقَّ الْمِيقَاتِ كَمَا إِذَا مَرَّ بِهِ مُحْرِمًا سَاكِتًا وَعِنْدَهُ بِعَوْدِهِ مُحْرِمًا مُلَبِّيًا لِأَنَّ الْعَزِيمَةَ فِي حَقِّ الْإِحْرَامِ مِنْ دَوَيْرَةِ أَهْلِهِ فَإِذَا تَرَخَّصَ بِالتَّأْخِيرِ إِلَى الْمِيقَاتِ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ فِضَاءُ حَقِّهِ بِإِنْشَاءِ التَّلْبِيَةِ وَكَانَ التَّلَافِي بِعَوْدِهِ مُلَبِّيًا وَعَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَافِ إِذَا أَحْرَمَ بِحَجَّتِهِ بَعْدَ الْمُجَاوَزَةِ مَكَانَ الْعُمْرَةِ فِي جَمِيعِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلَوْ عَادَ بَعْدَ مَا ابْتَدَأَ الطَّوَافَ وَاسْتَلَمَ الْحَجَرَ لَا يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ الدَّمُ بِالِاتِّفَاقِ وَلَوْ عَادَ إِلَيْهِ قَبْلَ الْإِحْرَامِ يَسْقُطُ بِالِاتِّفَاقِ وَهَذَا الَّذِي ذَكَرْنَا إِذَا كَانَ يُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ أَوِ الْعُمْرَةَ
Chapter on crossing the miqat without ihram. When a Kufi comes to Bustan Bani Amir and enters into ihram for Umrah, then if he returns to Dhat Irq and recites the talbiyah, the dam of the miqat is nullified for him. And if he returns to it and does not recite the talbiyah until he enters Makkah and performs tawaf for his Umrah, then upon him is a dam. This is according to Abu Hanifah. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If he returns to it while in ihram, nothing is upon him, whether he recited the talbiyah or did not recite. And Zufar said: It is not nullified whether he recited the talbiyah or did not, because his offense is not removed by the return, and it becomes like one who left Arafat before its time then returned to it after sunset. And our proof is that he made up the omitted act in its proper time, and that is before commencing the actions, so the dam is dropped, unlike the departure from Arafat, because he did not make up the omitted act as has passed. However, according to them (the two), the making up is by his returning while in ihram, because he has manifested the right of the miqat, as if he passed by it in ihram silently. According to him (Abu Hanifah), it is by his returning while in ihram and reciting the talbiyah, because the determined duty regarding ihram is from the dwellings of his people, so when he takes the concession of delaying to the miqat, it becomes obligatory upon him to fulfill its right by initiating the talbiyah, and the compensation is by his returning reciting the talbiyah. And upon this dispute is the case when he enters into ihram for Hajj after crossing instead of Umrah in all that we mentioned. And if he returns after he has begun the tawaf and touched the Black Stone, the dam is not dropped by agreement. And if he returns to it before ihram, it is dropped by agreement. And this which we mentioned is when he intends Hajj or Umrah.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah discusses the ruling for a person from beyond the miqat (afaqi) who crosses the miqat without assuming ihram, then later enters ihram for Umrah. The key issue is whether returning to the miqat after entering ihram can nullify the dam (sacrificial penalty) that became obligatory due to crossing without ihram. Three Hanafi positions are presented: Abu Hanifa holds that returning to the miqat and reciting the talbiyah nullifies the dam. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that simply returning in a state of ihram suffices, regardless of talbiyah. Zufar holds that the dam is never nullified by return, drawing an analogy to someone who leaves Arafat before sunset and returns after sunset—the penalty for leaving early remains. The text then explains the reasoning: the majority (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) argue that the omission (crossing without ihram) was made up in its proper time (before beginning the actions of Umrah), so the penalty drops. The difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is about what constitutes 'making up': Sahibayn say simply returning in ihram is sufficient because it shows respect to the miqat; Abu Hanifa says talbiyah is necessary because the concession of delaying ihram to the miqat requires initiating talbiyah to fulfill the right. The passage concludes that the same dispute applies if one intends Hajj instead of Umrah, and that if one returns after beginning tawaf or after touching the Black Stone, the dam is not dropped by consensus; if one returns before ihram, it is dropped by consensus (i.e., because no ihram-related penalty yet).

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial penalty (usually a sheep or goat) required for certain violations during Hajj or Umrah, such as crossing the miqat without ihram.
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary beyond which one intending Hajj or Umrah must assume ihram. For people of Kufa, it is Dhat Irq.
تدارك (tadarak): Making up or remedying an omitted obligatory act within its proper time or before subsequent actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what must a person do when returning to the miqat after entering ihram for Umrah in order for the dam to be nullified?
A) Simply return to the miqat in a state of ihram.
B) Return to the miqat, recite the talbiyah, and perform two rak'ahs of prayer.
C) Return to the miqat and recite the talbiyah.
D) Return to the miqat before beginning any Umrah actions and perform a sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three views on nullifying the dam by returning to the miqat, with Abu Hanifa requiring talbiyah, the Sahibayn only requiring return in ihram, and Zufar denying nullification entirely.

Passing the Miqat Without Ihram: Does Returning Waive the Sacrifice?
Ruling on compensation for crossing miqat without ihram and effect of returning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether returning to the miqat after crossing it without ihram waives the sacrifice, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar using the concept of tadaruk.

Core Idea
Not all returns to the miqat are equal: talbiyah may be the decisive factor in waiving the sacrifice.

Crossing the miqat without ihram is a violation that generally requires a sacrifice (dam). But what if the pilgrim returns to the miqat before starting the acts of Hajj or Umrah? The Hanafi imams differ on whether this return cancels the obligation, and their disagreement turns on the concept of tadaruk — making up an omitted act at the proper time. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the act in question? Crossing the miqat without ihram incurs a dam. The dispute is whether returning to the miqat before starting acts waives that dam.
The offense is jinayah before ihram; tadaruk is possible before starting the main acts.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa requires returning with talbiyah; the Sahibayn hold that mere return in ihram suffices; Imam Zufar says return does not waive the dam.
These are all Hanafi views, with Zufar's aligning with Malik and Shafi'i.
3
Follow the proofs (qiyas analogy)
Zufar analogizes to leaving Arafat before the Imam: return after sunset does not waive the dam. The Hanafi response distinguishes because tadaruk is possible before starting acts.
The illa is the possibility of making up the omitted act at its proper time.
4
Analyze the Hanafi concept of tadaruk
Tadaruk means making up a missed wajib within its time frame. Here, the omitted wajib is crossing the miqat with ihram; the time for tadaruk exists before any act of Hajj/Umrah.
Abu Hanifa adds that talbiyah completes the ihram, thus fully making up the omission.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, if a pilgrim crosses the miqat, ties ihram later, and returns saying talbiyah before any act, no dam is due. Sahibayn waive dam even without talbiyah. Zufar requires dam regardless of return.
The mufta bihi in the later Hanafi school typically follows the Sahibayn.
