میقات سے بغیر احرام تجاوز کرنے کے بعد عمرہ کی جگہ حج کا احرام باندھا۔ ( یہ اختلاف) مذکورہ تمام امور میں ہے۔ اور اگر میقات کی طرف طواف شروع کرنے کے اور حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینے کے بعد لونا تو بالا تفاق اس سے قربانی ساقط نہ ہو گی۔ اور اگر وہ احرام باندھنے سے پہلے میقات کی طرف لوٹا تو بالا تفاق قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہ سب جو ہم نے ذکر کیا اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے۔ تشریح جنایات اور اس کے انواع کے ذکر سے فراغت کے بعد بغیر احرام میقات سے گذر جانے کے احکام ذکر کئے گئے ہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی جنایات میں سے ہے لیکن یہ جنایت احرام سے پہلے ہے۔ عبارت میں کوفی سے مراد آفاقی یعنی میقات سے باہر کا رہنے والا شخص ہے۔ بستان بنی عامر میقات سے قریب میقات کے اندر اور حرم سے باہر ایک جگہ کا نام ہے۔ ذات عرق اہل کوفہ کا میقات ہے۔ اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہوگی کہ اگر کوئی آفاقی بغیر احرام باندھے میقات سے گذر گیا اور پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھ لیا تو دیکھا جائے کہ احرام کے بعد اس نے کوئی عمرہ کا فعل شروع کیا ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر کوئی فعل شروع نہیں کیا اور وہ لوٹ کر میقات پر آ گیا اور تلبیہ کہا تو بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے جو قربانی واجب ہوئی تھی وہ ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر وہ میقات کی طرف لوٹا مگر تلبیہ نہیں کہا یہاں تک کہ جا کر مکہ میں داخل ہوا اور طواف عمرہ کیا یعنی فعل عمرہ شروع کر دیا تو اس پر قربانی لازم ہے۔ گویا میقات کی طرف لوٹنے میں تلبیہ کہنا ضروری ہے۔ اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ اگر وہ میقات کی طرف احرام کی حالت میں لوٹا تو اس پر کچھ لا زم نہیں رہا۔ خواہ اس نے تلبیہ کہا ہو یا نہ کہا ہو۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ قربانی ساقط نہ ہوگی تلبیہ کہے یا نہ کہے۔ یہی قول امام مالک اور امام شافعی کا ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا جرم میقات کی طرف لوٹنے سے مرتفع نہیں ہوا اور جب جرم مرتفع نہیں ہوا تو دم جنایت بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کوئی حاجی امام سے پہلے ہی میدان عرفات سے کوچ کر گیا۔ پھر غروب آفتاب کے بعد عرفات واپس آگیا اور امام کے ساتھ کوچ کیا تو امام سے پہلے کوچ کرنے کی وجہ سے جو قربانی واجب ہوئی تھی واپس آنے سے وہ قربانی ساقط نہ ہو گی۔ اسی طرح بغیر احرام میقات سے گذر جانے کی صورت میں جو قربانی واجب ہوئی ہے میقات کی طرف لوٹنے سے وہ ساقط نہ ہوگی۔ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کی مشتر کہ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے متروک یعنی احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کا تدارک اپنے وقت پر کر لیا ہے اور تدارک کا وقت افعال شروع کرنے سے پہلے موجود ہے اور مدارک وقت پر کرنا مفید ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ تدارک بھی مفید ہوگا اور جب یہ تدارک مفید ہے تو واجب شدہ دم ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ بر خلاف امام سے پہلے میدان عرفات سے کوچ کرنے کے کیونکہ اس نے متروک کا تدارک نہیں کیا۔ کیونکہ متروک غروب آفتاب تک وقوف کا برابر رہنا ہے اور غروب کے بعد اس کے لوٹنے سے اس کا تدارک کس طرح ہو جائے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ متروک کا تدارک نہیں ہوا اور جب متروک کا تدارک نہیں ہوا تو غروب سے پہلے امام سے پہلے کوچ کرنے کی وجہ سے جو دم واجب ہوا تھا وہ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک تو امام صاحب اور صاحبین کی دلیل مشترک تھی ۔ غَيْرَ اُنَّ التَّدَارُكَ الخ سے فرق ہے کیا چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک مدارک اسکے احرام کے ساتھ لوٹنے میں حاصل ہے تلبیہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے میقات کا حق یعنی احترام ظاہر کر دیا تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے وہ میقات پر احرام کے ساتھ خاموش گذرا اور تلبیہ نہیں کہا تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنا ضروری نہیں ہے اور امام اعظم کے نزدیک تدارک اس کے احرام کے ساتھ تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنے میں حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ احرام کے حق میں عزیمت یہ ہے کہ اپنے وطن کی آبادی سے احرام باندھے اور رخصت یہ ہے کہ میقات سے احرام باندھے۔ پس جب اس نے میقات تک مؤخر کرنے کی رخصت اختیار کر لی تو تلبیہ پیدا کر کے احرام کا پورا کرنا اس پر واجب ہے۔ پس جرم یعنی بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی تلافی تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنے سے ہوگی بغیر تلبیہ کے محض لوٹنے سے تلافی نہ ہوگی ۔ مذکورہ تمام چیزوں میں یہی اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ کسی نے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کے بعد بجائے عمرہ کے حج کا احرام باندھا یہ سب تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ احرام کے بعد افعال عمرہ شروع کرنے سے پہلے میقات کی طرف لوٹ گیا۔ لیکن اگر وہ طواف شروع کرنے اور حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینے کے بعد میقات کی طرف لوٹا تو بالا تفاق اس سے دم ساقط نہ ہو گا ۔ اور اگر وہ احرام باندھنے سے پہلے ہی میقات کی طرف لوٹ آیا تو بالا تفاق قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اور یہ جو ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی صورت میں دم واجب ہوتا ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ اس کا ارادہ حج یا عمرہ کا ہو۔
He entered into ihram for Hajj instead of Umrah after crossing the miqat without ihram. This disagreement is in all mentioned matters. And if after starting tawaf and kissing the Black Stone he returns to the miqat, then by consensus the sacrifice is not waived. And if he returns to the miqat before tying ihram, then by consensus the sacrifice is waived. And all that we have mentioned is when he intends Hajj or Umrah. Explanation: After finishing the mention of offenses and their types, the rulings on crossing the miqat without ihram are mentioned, because this too is among offenses, but this offense is before ihram. In the text, 'Kufi' means an afaqi, a person living outside the miqat. Bustan Bani Amir is a place near the miqat, inside the miqat and outside the Haram. Dhat Irq is the miqat of the people of Kufa. Now the case is: if an afaqi passes the miqat without ihram and then ties ihram for Umrah, it is seen whether after ihram he has started any act of Umrah or not. If he has not started any act, and he returns to the miqat and says the talbiyah, then the sacrifice that became obligatory due to crossing the miqat without ihram is waived. And if he returns to the miqat but does not say the talbiyah until he enters Mecca and performs tawaf of Umrah, i.e., starts the act of Umrah, then the sacrifice is incumbent upon him. So saying the talbiyah upon returning to the miqat is necessary. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: if he returns to the miqat in the state of ihram, then nothing remains incumbent upon him, whether he said the talbiyah or not. Imam Zufar said: the sacrifice is not waived whether he says the talbiyah or not. This is the same saying of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i. Imam Zufar's proof is that the crime of crossing the miqat without ihram is not removed by returning to the miqat, and when the crime is not removed, the blood of offense is not waived. This is like a pilgrim who leaves Arafat before the Imam, then after sunset returns to Arafat and leaves with the Imam; the sacrifice that became obligatory due to leaving before the Imam is not waived by returning. Similarly, in the case of crossing the miqat without ihram, the sacrifice that became obligatory is not waived by returning to the miqat. The common proof of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is that he has made up (tadaruk) the omitted act, i.e., crossing the miqat with ihram, at its proper time, and the time for making up exists before starting the acts, and making up on time is beneficial, so this make-up will be beneficial, and when it is beneficial, the obligatory blood is waived. Unlike leaving Arafat before the Imam, because he has not made up the omitted act. For the omitted act is continuous standing until sunset, and after sunset, how can returning make it up? The conclusion is that the omitted act is not made up, and thus the blood that became obligatory due to leaving before sunset before the Imam is not waived. Up to here, the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn was common. But there is a difference: the Sahibayn hold that the make-up is achieved by returning with ihram, without the need for talbiyah, because he has manifested the respect of the miqat, so it is as if he passed the miqat silently with ihram and did not say talbiyah, which is unanimously permissible. Similarly here, returning with talbiyah is not necessary. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the make-up is achieved by returning with ihram while saying the talbiyah, because regarding ihram, the 'azimah (stringent) is to tie ihram from one's hometown, and the rukhsa (concession) is to tie ihram from the miqat. So when he took the concession of deferring to the miqat, it is obligatory upon him to complete the ihram by producing talbiyah. Thus, the compensation for the crime of crossing the miqat without ihram occurs by returning while saying talbiyah, not by mere return without talbiyah. This disagreement in all mentioned matters is when someone after crossing the miqat tied ihram for Hajj instead of Umrah. All this detail is when he returned to the miqat after tying ihram but before starting the acts of Umrah. But if after starting tawaf and kissing the Black Stone he returns to the miqat, then by consensus the sacrifice is not waived from him. And if he returns to the miqat before tying ihram, then by consensus the sacrifice is waived. And what we have mentioned that a sacrifice becomes obligatory in the case of crossing the miqat without ihram is when his intention is Hajj or Umrah.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi legal discussion (inter-madhhab dispute) about a person who crosses the miqat without ihram and later returns to the miqat. The core issue is whether returning to the miqat before starting the acts of Hajj/Umrah cancels the obligation of a sacrifice (dam) incurred for crossing the miqat without ihram. The text presents the positions of four authorities: Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), Imam Zufar, and the external schools of Malik and Shafi'i. Abu Hanifa holds that returning to the miqat with talbiyah waives the sacrifice; returning without talbiyah does not. The Sahibayn hold that returning to the miqat in a state of ihram waives the sacrifice regardless of talbiyah. Zufar, Malik, and Shafi'i hold that the sacrifice is never waived by returning, because the offense has already occurred. The text then provides proofs for each position using qiyas. The Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa use the concept of 'tadaruk' (making up the omitted act at its proper time), analogizing to the case of leaving Arafat early. However, they differ on whether talbiyah is part of the make-up. The text concludes by clarifying that this dispute applies when the person crosses the miqat intentionally for Hajj or Umrah, and that if the person has already started the acts (tawaf), the sacrifice is not waived by consensus. If the person returns before tying ihram, the sacrifice is waived by consensus.

Key Terms
تدارک (tadaruk): Making up or rectifying an omitted obligatory act at its proper time before the act's time expires.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' which is a wajib of ihram according to Abu Hanifa, obligatory for completing the ihram.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) offered as expiation for a violation (jinayah) during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what condition must be met for the sacrifice (dam) to be waived when a person returns to the miqat after crossing it without ihram?
A) The person must return before tying ihram.
B) The person must return while saying the talbiyah.
C) The person must return in a state of ihram.
D) The sacrifice is never waived.

Key Takeaway
The concept of tadaruk (making up an omitted wajib at its proper time) is central to the Hanafi ruling on returning to the miqat.

Entering Bustan Bani Amir Without Ihram: The Hanafi Exception
Ruling on entering the miqat area without ihram for a need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that entering Bustan Bani Amir without ihram for a need is permissible and explain the legal reasoning (dalil aqli) that treats the entrant like a resident.

Core Idea
If you enter Bustan Bani Amir for a need, you become a resident of the miqat — no ihram required.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a person from outside the miqat (afaqi) enters a place called Bustan Bani Amir for a legitimate need such as trade. The Hanafi school provides a ruling that may seem surprising: such a person does not need to put on ihram and can later enter Mecca without ihram. Why? The key is that Bustan Bani Amir is not a place that commands the same veneration as the miqat boundary, and entering it for a need makes the person legally equivalent to a resident (Bustani). In this lesson, we will unpack the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Entering Bustan Bani Amir without ihram for a need. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) and no penalty is incurred.
The act is not a pillar or obligatory action; it is a dispensation.
2
Understand the legal rationale (dalil aqli)
Why is it permissible? Because Bustan Bani Amir is not 'wajib al-ta'zim' (obligatory of respect). The requirement of ihram is attached to the act of entering the Haram or the miqat with the intention of performing Hajj/Umrah, not for a casual entry for a need.
The illa (effective cause) is the lack of veneration required for that place.
3
Apply the analogy with the resident (Bustani)
The text says the entrant becomes 'joined to its people'. Legally, he is treated like a resident of that area, whose miqat is right there. Therefore, he may enter Mecca without ihram just as a Bustani may.
This is an application of istihsan based on need and custom.
4
Trace the consequences for future Hajj/Umrah
If the person later wants to perform Hajj, he can tie ihram from the Bustan (or the hill area) and no additional sacrifice (dam) is required because he started from his valid miqat.
This reinforces that the miqat for such a person is the Bustan itself.

Source Text

کوئی اپنی حاجت کے لئے بغیر احرام بستان بنی عامر میں داخل ہوا مکہ میں داخل ہونے کے لئے یہی بستان اس کے لئے موضع میقات ہے فَإِن دَخَلَ الْبُسْتَانَ لِحَاجَتِهِ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ مَكَّةَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامِ وَوَقَتَهُ الْبُسْتَانُ وَهُوَ وَصَاحِبُ المنزل سَوَاءٌ لأنَّ الْبُسْتَانَ غَيْرُ وَاجِبِ التَّعْظِيمِ فَلَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْإحْرَامُ بِقَصْدِهِ وَإِذَا دَخَلَهُ الْتَحَقِ بِأهْلِهِ وَلِلْبُسْتَانِى أَنْ يَدْخُلَ مَكَةً بِغَيْرِ إحْرَامِ لِلْحَاجَةِ فَكَذَلِكَ لَةَ وَالْمُرَادُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَوَقْتُهُ الْبُسْتَانَ جَمِيعَ الْحِلِ الَّذِى بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْحَرَمِ وَقَدْ مَرَّ مِنْ قَبل فَكَذَا وَقتَ الدَّاخِلَ الْمُلْحِق بِهِ فَإِنْ أَحْرَمَا مِنَ الْحِلَ وَوَقَفَا بِعَرَفَةَ لَم يَكُنْ عَلَيْهِمَا شَيْءٍ يُرِيدُ بِهِ الْبُسْتَانِيُّ وَالدَّاخِلُ فِيْهِ لِأَنَّهُمَا أَحْرَمَا مِنْ مِيقَاتِهِمَا ترجمہ پس اگر وہ بستان بنی عامر میں اپنی ضرورت سے داخل ہوا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہو اور اس کا میقات یہی موضع بستان ہے اور یہ شخص جو بستان میں داخل ہو گیا اور جو شخص کہ بستان کا رہنے والا ہے دونوں یکساں ہیں ۔ کیونکہ بستان غیر واجب التعظیم ہے۔ اس لئے بستان کا قصد کرنے سے اس پر احرام باندھنا لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب بستان میں داخل ہو گیا تو بستان والوں کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گیا اور بستانی کے واسطے اپنی ضرورت کی خاطر بغیر احرام مکہ میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے۔ پس اس کے لئے بھی جائز ہے اور دو وقته البستان سے مراد تمام حل ہے جو اس کے اور حرم کے درمیان واقع ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اس کا میقات جو بستان میں داخل ہو کر بستانی کے ساتھ لاحق کیا گیا ہے۔ پھر اگر دونوں نے حل سے احرام باندھا اور وقوف عرفہ کیا تو ان دونوں پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ ان دونوں سے مراد بستانی اور بستان میں داخل ہونے والا شخص ہے کیونکہ دونوں نے اپنے میقات سے احرام باندھا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی آفاقی اپنی کسی ضرورت تجارت و غیرہ کی غرض سے بستان بنی عامر یعنی داخل میقات میں بغیر احرام کے داخل ہوا تو اس پر کوئی جرم نہیں ہے۔ اب اگر وہ بستان بنی عامر سے مکہ معظمہ میں داخل ہونا چاہے تو اس کو بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل
Someone entered Bustan Bani Amir without ihram for his need. For entering Mecca, this Bustan is his miqat. So if he enters the Bustan for his need, he may enter Mecca without ihram, and his miqat is the Bustan. He and the owner of the house are equal, because the Bustan is not wajib al-ta'zim (obligatory of respect), so ihram is not necessary upon him by intending it. When he enters it, he is joined to its people. And for the Bustani (resident of Bustan), it is permissible to enter Mecca without ihram for a need. So likewise for him. And what is meant by 'his time is the Bustan' is all the hill (unconsecrated area) that lies between him and the Haram, and it has passed previously. So similarly is the time of the entrant who is joined to him. Then if both of them tie ihram from the hill and stand at Arafah, there is no (obligation) upon them. He intends by 'both' the Bustani and the one who entered it, because they both tied ihram from their miqat. Translation: So if he enters Bustan Bani Amir for his need, he has the option to enter Mecca without ihram, and his miqat is this place Bustan. And this person who entered the Bustan and the person who is a resident of Bustan are equal. Because Bustan is not wajib al-ta'zim. Therefore, intending Bustan does not make ihram necessary upon him. And when he entered the Bustan, he is joined to the residents of Bustan. And for the Bustani, it is permissible to enter Mecca without ihram for his need. So it is permissible for him as well. And 'waqtuhu al-bustan' refers to all the hill that lies between him and the Haram. So similarly, his miqat who is joined to the Bustani after entering the Bustan. Then if both of them tie ihram from the hill and perform wuquf at Arafah, nothing is wajib upon them. 'Both' means the Bustani and the person who entered the Bustan, because they both tied ihram from their miqat. Explanation: The issue is that if a non-resident (afaqi) enters Bustan Bani Amir, which is inside the miqat, without ihram for some need like trade, then there is no offense upon him. Now if he wants to enter Mecca from Bustan Bani Amir, he may enter Mecca without ihram.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a clear ruling statement (with proof) regarding a non-resident (afaqi) who enters Bustan Bani Amir (a place within the miqat but outside the Haram) without ihram for a legitimate need such as trade. The key principle is that Bustan Bani Amir is not a place that commands respect (ghayr wajib al-ta'zim) in the sense that one must be in ihram to enter it. Therefore, entering it without ihram is not an offense. Furthermore, once a person enters this area for a need, he is considered joined to the residents (Bustaniyin) of that area, and thus his miqat becomes Bustan Bani Amir itself. Consequently, he may enter Mecca without ihram, just as the Bustani can. If he later decides to perform Hajj or Umrah, he can tie ihram from his miqat (the Bustan or the hill area) and proceed, and no additional sacrifice is required because he started ihram from his valid miqat. The text also clarifies that 'waqtuhu al-bustan' refers to all the hill area between Bustan and the Haram, which is the effective miqat for such a person. The ruling is based on the rationale that the Bustan is not a place of veneration like the miqat proper, and entering it for a need does not incur the obligation of ihram.

Key Terms
بستان بنی عامر (Bustan Bani Amir): A specific place within the miqat (the boundary for ihram) but outside the Haram (sanctuary of Mecca). It is a known location in the region of the miqat.
غیر واجب التعظیم (ghayr wajib al-ta'zim): Not obligatory to venerate or respect (in the sense that entering it does not require ihram).
آفاقی (afaqi): A person who resides outside the miqat boundaries (i.e., comes from distant lands).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The person who lives outside the miqat (afaqi).
B) The person who lives in the Haram.
C) The person who lives in Bustan (Bustani).
D) The person who intends to perform Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Entering Bustan Bani Amir without ihram for a legitimate need is permissible, and the entrant is treated like a resident, allowing entry into Mecca without ihram.

When Does Returning to the Miqat Waive the Dam?
Detailed ruling on when dam is waived upon returning to miqat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the dam for crossing the miqat without ihram is waived, and apply the Hanafi position that returning with talbiyah before starting Umrah acts is necessary for compensation.

Core Idea
Returning to the miqat without talbiyah does not waive the dam; talbiyah is the operative act of compensation.

In this passage from the Hidayah commentary, we examine a detailed scenario: a pilgrim who crosses the miqat without ihram and later returns to make amends. The ruling hinges on timing and the recitation of talbiyah. Understanding this teaches us how the Hanafi school balances the original ruling ('azimat) with the concession (rukhsat) and what constitutes valid compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is crossing the miqat without ihram while intending Hajj or Umrah. The ruling (hukm) is that dam becomes wajib upon the person.
This is the default ruling.
2
Locate the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
The text provides a ta'lil based on 'azimat and rukhsat: the original duty ('azimat) is to assume ihram from home; the concession (rukhsat) allows ihram from the miqat. By choosing the rukhsat, the person must complete ihram with talbiyah.
The ta'lil explains why talbiyah is essential for compensation.
3
Determine the condition for compensation
Compensation (waiving the dam) is achieved by returning to the miqat and reciting talbiyah while in ihram. Mere physical return without talbiyah is insufficient according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the exceptions based on timing
If the person returns after starting tawaf and kissing the Black Stone, the dam is not waived by consensus. If the person returns before performing ihram at all, the dam is waived by consensus.
These exceptions show that the compensation window is before the Umrah acts begin.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that returning with talbiyah before starting Umrah acts waives the dam. Returning without talbiyah or after commencing tawaf does not waive it.
This is based on the authority of Al-Hidayah and Imam Abu Hanifa.

دیا تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے وہ میقات پر احرام کے ساتھ خاموش گذرا اور تلبیہ نہیں کہا تو یہ بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنا ضروری نہیں ہے اور امام اعظم کے نزدیک تدارک اس کے احرام کے ساتھ تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنے میں حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ احرام کے حق میں عزیمت یہ ہے کہ اپنے وطن کی آبادی سے احرام باندھے اور رخصت یہ ہے کہ میقات سے احرام باندھے۔ پس جب اس نے میقات تک مؤخر کرنے کی رخصت اختیار کر لی تو تلبیہ پیدا کر کے احرام کا پورا کرنا اس پر واجب ہے۔ پس جرم یعنی بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی تلافی تلبیہ کہتے ہوئے لوٹنے سے ہوگی بغیر تلبیہ کے محض لوٹنے سے تلافی نہ ہوگی۔ مذکورہ تمام چیزوں میں یہی اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ کسی نے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کے بعد بجائے عمرہ کے حج کا احرام باندھا یہ سب تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ احرام کے بعد افعال عمرہ شروع کرنے سے پہلے میقات کی طرف لوٹ گیا۔ لیکن اگر وہ طواف شروع کرنے اور حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینے کے بعد میقات کی طرف لوٹا تو بالا تفاق اس سے دم ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر وہ احرام باندھنے سے پہلے ہی میقات کی طرف لوٹ آیا تو بالا تفاق قربانی ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہ جو ہم نے ذکر کیا کہ بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی صورت میں دم واجب ہوتا ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ اس کا ارادہ حج یا عمرہ کا ہو۔
He gave [something] then it became like he passed the miqat with ihram silently and did not say talbiyah, so this is permissible by consensus. Similarly here, returning while saying talbiyah is not necessary, and according to Imam A'zam, the compensation is achieved by returning while saying talbiyah with his ihram. Because in respect of ihram, 'azimat is that he perform ihram from his home town, and rukhsat is that he perform ihram from the miqat. So when he chose the rukhsat of delaying until the miqat, then completing the ihram by producing talbiyah is wajib upon him. Therefore, the compensation for the offense of crossing the miqat without ihram will be achieved by returning while saying talbiyah; returning without talbiyah will not achieve compensation. This difference in all mentioned matters is when someone after crossing the miqat performed ihram for Hajj instead of 'Umrah. All this detail is when he returned to the miqat after ihram but before starting the acts of 'Umrah. However, if he returned to the miqat after starting tawaf and kissing the Black Stone, then by consensus the dam is not waived from him. And if he returned to the miqat before performing ihram, then by consensus the sacrifice is waived. And what we mentioned that dam is wajib when crossing the miqat without ihram is when his intention is for Hajj or 'Umrah.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling expansion from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It addresses a specific scenario: a person who passed the miqat without entering ihram and then later returns to the miqat to make up for the omission. The key ruling is that if he returns to the miqat after having performed ihram (e.g., for 'Umrah or Hajj) but before starting the actual rituals of 'Umrah (like tawaf), then his return with talbiyah (the proclamation of labbayk) serves as compensation and the dam (sacrificial penalty) is waived. However, if he returns after having begun tawaf or after kissing the Black Stone, the dam is not waived by consensus. If he returns even before performing ihram at all, again by consensus the sacrifice is waived. The text then clarifies that this entire discussion applies only when the person intended Hajj or 'Umrah; someone who enters the miqat for a non-religious purpose is not liable for dam. The reasoning (ta'lil) provided is based on the distinction between 'azimat (the original ruling of performing ihram from home) and rukhsat (the concession of performing ihram from miqat). By choosing the rukhsat, the person becomes obligated to complete ihram with talbiyah, and merely returning physically is insufficient without the verbal proclamation.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The proclamation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited during ihram.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) required as penalty for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.
میقات (miqat): The specific boundary from which pilgrims must assume ihram for Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is dam not waived upon returning to the miqat?
A) When one returns before performing any act of 'Umrah
B) When one returns after starting tawaf and kissing the Black Stone
C) When one returns before performing ihram
D) When one returns with talbiyah

Key Takeaway
Dam for crossing the miqat without ihram is waived only if one returns before starting the Umrah acts and recites talbiyah; mere physical return without talbiyah is insufficient.

Ruling on Entering Bustan Bani 'Amir Without Ihram for Need
Ruling on Bustan Bani 'Amir as a miqat for an Afaqi with need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for an Afaqi who enters Bustan Bani 'Amir for a need and identify the correct miqat for entering Makkah.

Core Idea
Entering Bustan Bani 'Amir for a need shifts an Afaqi's miqat to the Hal, but ihram remains obligatory before entering Makkah.

The outer miqats are fixed boundaries for Hajj, but the Hanafi school provides a concession for those who enter the miqat area for a legitimate need. This lesson examines how Bustan Bani 'Amir functions as a miqat for an Afaqi who enters it for a purpose like trade. The source passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling and its rationale, emphasizing that the obligation of ihram is not lifted.

Guided Path
1
Determine the status of Bustan Bani 'Amir
Recognize that Bustan Bani 'Amir is a specific garden located within the miqat boundaries, not a designated outer miqat station. It is not a place of veneration (ghayr wajib al-ta'dhim).
2
Identify the ruling for an Afaqi entering for a need
An Afaqi (person living outside miqat) may enter Bustan Bani 'Amir without ihram if he enters for a legitimate need (e.g., trade). Doing so does not incur any penalty.
The need must be genuine; casual entry without purpose may not qualify.
3
Establish the correct miqat for entering Makkah
Upon entering for need, the Afaqi becomes assimilated to the residents (Bustani). His miqat for entering Makkah shifts from the outer miqat to the entire Hal area (the region between the garden and the Haram), not just the garden itself.
The Hal includes the garden and surrounding area up to the Haram boundary.
4
Recognize the universal obligation of ihram
Despite the shifted miqat, the obligation to assume ihram before entering Makkah remains. The concession only changes the location from which ihram is assumed, not the requirement itself.
Ibn al-Humam emphasizes that entering Makkah without ihram is prohibited for everyone.

داخل ہو گیا اور جو شخص کہ بستان کا رہنے والا ہے دونوں یکساں ہیں ۔ کیونکہ بستان غیر واجب التعظیم ہے۔ اس لئے بستان کا قصد کرنے سے اس پر احرام باندھنا لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب بستان میں داخل ہو گیا تو بستان والوں کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گیا اور بستانی کے واسطے اپنی ضرورت کی خاطر بغیر احرام مکہ میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے۔ پس اس کے لئے بھی جائز ہے اور دو وقته البستان سے مراد تمام حل ہے جو اس کے اور حرم کے درمیان واقع کے داخل ہوا تو اس پر کوئی جرم نہیں ہے۔ اب اگر وہ بستان بنی عامر سے مکہ معظمہ میں داخل ہونا چاہے تو اس کو بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونے کی اجازت ہے۔ اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اس کو میقات سے احرام باندھنے کی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ اسی جگہ سے احرام باندھ کر مکہ میں داخل ہو سکتا ہے۔ یہ مطلب ہرگز نہیں ہے کہ بغیر احرام کے مکہ میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ علامہ ابن الہمام نے لکھا ہے کہ تمام کتا ہیں، ناطق ہیں کہ جو کوئی مکہ میں داخل ہونا چاہے اس پر احرام لازم ہے خواہ حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ کرے یا تجارت وغیر کا۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ بستانی کے واسطے میقات یہی موضع بستان ہے۔ یعنی بستان سے احرام باندھنا اس کے حق میں میقات سے احرام باندھنے کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور یہ شخص جو بستان بنی عامر میں داخل ہو گیا اور جو شخص بستان بنی عامر کا رہنے والا ہے دونوں اس بات میں یکساں ہیں کہ ان کے واسطے میقات یہی موضع بستان ہے اور اس آفاقی کو آفاقیوں کے میقات سے احرام باندھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بستان کوئی واجب التعظيم مقام نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بستان کا قصد کرنے سے اس پر احرام باندھنالازم نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ جائز نہ ہوگا اس لئے یہ آفاقی واسطے بھی بغیر احرام کے کسی اپنی ضرورت سے مکہ میں داخل ہونا جائز ہے۔ بقول ابن الہام کے اس کا مطلب بھی یہی ہے کہ بستانی بغیر میقات سے احرام باند ھے مکہ میں داخل ہو سکتا ہے۔ رہابستان سے احرام باندھنا تو یہ ضروری ہے کیونکہ بغیر احرام مکہ میں داخلہ ممنوع ہے۔ اور یہ جو فرمایا ہے کہ بستانی کا میقات بستان ہے اس سے مراد پورا حل کا علاقہ ہے جو اس کے اور حرم کے درمیان واقع ہے۔ خاص طور پر بستان مراد نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اس شخص کا میقات جو بستان میں داخل ہو کر ابستانی کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا گیا حل کا پورا علاقہ ہے جو ا سکے اور حرم کے درمیان واقع ہے بستان کی کوئی تخصیص نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر بستانی اور بستان میں داخل ہونے والے نے حل سے احرام باندھا تو ان پر کوئی جرم نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں نے اپنے میقات سے احرام باندھا ہے اور ان دونوں کا میقات حل ہے۔
Someone entered Bustan Bani 'Amir without ihram for his need; for entering Makkah this same garden is his miqat. If he entered the garden for his need, then he may enter Makkah without ihram, and his miqat is the garden, and he and the owner of the residence are equal, because the garden is not a place deserving veneration, so it is not necessary for him to assume ihram by intending it. When he enters it, he becomes attached to its inhabitants. And for the gardener, it is permissible to enter Makkah without ihram for need, so likewise for him. And what is meant by 'his miqat is the garden' is all of the Hal (area between the Haram and the miqat) that lies between him and the Haram. So likewise the miqat of the entrant attached to him. If both perform ihram from the Hal and stand at Arafat, nothing is due upon them, meaning the gardener and the entrant, because they performed ihram from their miqat. Translation: So if he entered Bustan Bani 'Amir for his need, he has the option to enter Makkah without ihram, and his miqat is this garden location, and this person who entered the garden and the person who is a resident of the garden are both equal. Because the garden is not a place deserving veneration. Therefore, by intending the garden, it is not necessary for him to assume ihram. And when he entered the garden, he became attached to the garden people, and for the gardener it is permissible to enter Makkah without ihram for his need, so it is also permissible for him. And the meaning of 'his miqat is the garden' is all of the Hal area between him and the Haram. So similarly, his miqat who entered the garden and became attached to the gardener is the entire Hal. Then if both performed ihram from the Hal and did wuquf at Arafat, nothing is due upon them. By 'both' are meant the gardener and the person who entered the garden, because they both performed ihram from their miqat. Explanation: The issue is that if an Afaqi enters Bustan Bani 'Amir, which is inside the miqat, without ihram for some need like trade etc., then there is no offense on him. Now if he wants to enter Makkah from Bustan Bani 'Amir, he is permitted to enter Makkah without ihram. This means he does not need to assume ihram from the miqat, but can assume ihram from that place and enter Makkah. It does NOT mean that entering Makkah without ihram is permissible. Because Allamah Ibn al-Humam wrote that all books are vocal that whoever wants to enter Makkah, ihram is necessary upon him whether he intends Hajj, 'Umrah, trade, or something else. Sahib al-Quduri said that for the gardener, his miqat is this garden location, meaning performing ihram from the garden is in the ruling of performing ihram from the miqat. And this person who entered Bustan Bani 'Amir and the person who is a resident of Bustan Bani 'Amir are equal in that for them the miqat is this garden location, and this Afaqi does not need to assume ihram from the miqat of the Afaqis. Because the garden is not a place deserving veneration. Therefore, intending the garden does not make ihram necessary for him; rather, it is not allowed. So this Afaqi will enter Bustan Bani 'Amir without ihram. And when he entered the garden, he became attached to the garden people, and for the garden people it is permissible to enter Makkah without ihram for some need, so likewise entering Makkah without ihram for some need is permissible for him too. According to Ibn al-Humam, the meaning is that the gardener can enter Makkah by performing ihram from the garden, not without ihram. As for performing ihram from the garden, that is necessary because entering Makkah without ihram is prohibited. And what is said that the gardener's miqat is the garden, by that is meant the entire Hal area between him and the Haram, not specifically the garden. Similarly, the miqat of the person who entered the garden and became attached to the gardener is the entire Hal area between him and the Haram, no specific garden. So if the gardener and the entrant performed ihram from the Hal, there is no offense on them because both performed ihram from their miqat, and their miqat is the Hal.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah concerning the treatment of Bustan Bani 'Amir (a garden within the miqat boundary) as a miqat for certain people. The key ruling: if a person who is not a resident of Makkah (an Afaqi) enters Bustan Bani 'Amir for a need (e.g., trade) without ihram, he does not commit an offense. Thereafter, if he wishes to enter Makkah, he does not need to go back to the outer miqat of the Afaqis; rather, his miqat becomes the garden itself (meaning the entire Hal area between the garden and the Haram). He must still assume ihram from that place before entering Makkah, because entering the Haram without ihram is universally prohibited. The passage clarifies that this concession is because Bustan Bani 'Amir is not a place deserving special veneration (ghayr wajib al-ta'dhim), so entering it without ihram is permissible. By entering it for a need, the Afaqi is assimilated to the residents of the garden (the Bustani), who have the same miqat. The commentary emphasizes that 'garden' refers broadly to the entire Hal region, not just the physical garden. The passage cites Ibn al-Humam and Sahib al-Quduri to reinforce the point.

Key Terms
بستان بنی عامر (Bustan Bani 'Amir): A specific garden located within the miqat boundaries near Makkah, mentioned in Hadith as a point where pilgrims may enter ihram.
آفاقی (afaqi): A person who lives outside the miqat boundaries, not a resident of Makkah or its immediate vicinity.
حل (hal): The area outside the Haram (sanctuary) but within the miqat boundaries, where non-muqim pilgrims may be.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for an Afaqi who enters Bustan Bani 'Amir for a need and then wants to enter Makkah?
A) He must return to the outer miqat to assume ihram
B) He may enter Makkah without ihram
C) He must assume ihram from the Bustan (Hal) before entering Makkah
D) He must perform a sacrifice as penalty

Key Takeaway
An Afaqi who enters Bustan Bani 'Amir for a need assumes the miqat of the Hal, but he must still assume ihram before entering Makkah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Compensation for Entering Makkah Without Ihram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for entry without ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for entering Makkah without ihram when a wajib Hajj is performed in the same year, and explain the qiyas argument of Imam Zufar and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
A wajib Hajj in the same year compensates for entering Makkah without ihram because the omission is made up in its time.

This passage presents a disagreement within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if a person enters Makkah without ihram and then, before the year ends, performs a wajib Hajj, that suffices and no additional penalty is due. Imam Zufar, however, argues by qiyas that it does not suffice because the obligation becomes like a debt. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how temporal boundaries affect compensation in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa rules regarding the person who enters Makkah without ihram and later performs a wajib Hajj in the same year.
What is the practical outcome? Does a dam become necessary?
2
Identify Zufar's objection
Determine what Imam Zufar rules and the basis for his disagreement.
He uses qiyas; what is he analogizing to?
3
Trace Zufar's qiyas
Break down the analogy: what is the original case (asl) and what is the new case (far')? What is the effective cause (illa)?
The analogy involves an obligation that becomes a debt due to a vow.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school (lana) rebut Zufar's qiyas? What is the key distinction?
Focus on the temporal element: same year vs. year change.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference in rulings between Abu Hanifa and Zufar.
Does an additional penalty apply or not?

مکہ میں بغیر احرام کے داخل ہوا پھر اسی سال نکل گیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا اس پر بغیر احرام داخل ہونے سے کچھ لازم ہوگا یا نہیں ومن دخل مكة بِغَيْرِ الْحَرَامٍ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنْ عَامِهِ ذَلِكَ إِلَى الْوَقْتِ وَأَحْرَمَ بِحَجَّةٍ عَلَيْهِ أَجْزَاهُ ذَلِكَ مِن دُخُولِهِ مَكَة بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ وَقَالَ زُفُرُ لَا يُجْزِيهِ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ إِعْتِبَارًا بِمَا لَزَمَهُ بِسَبَبِ التَّدْرِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا تَحَولَتِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ تَلاقَى الْمَتَرُوكَ فِي وَقَتِهِ لأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ عَلَيْهِ تَعْظِيمُ هذه البقعة بِالْإِحْرَامِ كَمَا إِذَا أَتَاهُ مُحْرِمًا بِحَجَةٍ الإِسْلَامِ فِي الْإِبْتَدَاءِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا تَحَوَّلَتِ السَّنَةَ لِأَنَّهُ صَارَ دَيْنَا فِي أُمَّتِهِ فَلَا يَتَادَى إِلَّا بِإِحْرَامٍ مَقْصُودٍ كَمَا فِي الإِعْتِكَافِ المَنْدُورِ فَإِنَّهُ يَتَاَدَّى بِصَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ مِنْ هَذِهِ السَّنَةِ دُونَ الْعَامِ الثَّانِي ترجمہ اور جو شخص مکہ میں بغیر احرام کے داخل ہو گیا پھر وہ اسی سال نکل کر میقات پر گیا اور اس نے ایسے حج کا احرام باندھا جو اس پر وا جب سے تو اس کو بغیر احرام مکہ میں داخل ہونے سے یہ نسک واجبہ کافی ہو گیا۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ کافی نہ ہوگا اور یہی قیاس ہے۔ اس پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے جو اس کو نذر کی وجہ سے لازم ہوا ہے۔ تو ایسا ہو گیا یا مال پلٹ گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے متروک کی تلافی اپنے وقت میں کر لی ہے کیونکہ اس پر احرام کے ساتھ اس بقعہ کی تعظیم کرنا واجب ہے جیسے اگر ابتداء میں فریضہ حج کا احرام باند ھے آتا۔
One who entered Makkah without ihram, then left in that same year to the miqat and performed ihram for a Hajj that was wajib upon him, that [Hajj] suffices for his entering Makkah without ihram. And Imam Zufar said: it does not suffice him, and this is the qiyas, analogizing to what became necessary upon him due to a vow, so it becomes like when the year changed. And our proof is that he has compensated for the omitted act in its time, because the wajib upon him was to venerate this place by ihram, just as if he came in the beginning with ihram for the obligatory Hajj. Contrary to when the year changed, because it becomes a debt in his dhimma, so it is not fulfilled except by an intended ihram, like a vowed i'tikaf which is fulfilled by Ramadan fast of this year but not of the second year. Translation: And the person who entered Makkah without ihram, then he left in the same year and went to the miqat and assumed ihram for a Hajj that was wajib upon him, then this wajib ritual is sufficient for his entering Makkah without ihram. Imam Zufar said: it will not be sufficient, and this is the qiyas, drawing an analogy to what became necessary upon him due to a vow, so it becomes like if the year changed. And our proof is that he has compensated for the omitted act in its time, because what was wajib upon him was to venerate this place by ihram, just as if he came initially with ihram for the obligatory Hajj. Unlike if the year changed, because it becomes a debt in his dhimma, so it is not fulfilled except by an intended ihram, like a vowed i'tikaf which is fulfilled by the fast of Ramadan in that year but not the second year.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar regarding a person who enters Makkah without ihram and later, in the same year, leaves to the miqat and performs a Hajj that is obligatory upon him (e.g., the Hajj of Islam). The question is whether this Hajj compensates for the violation of entering Makkah without ihram. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does compensate, because the person has performed the required veneration (ta'dhim) of the sacred precincts with ihram within the same year, thus making up for the omission in its time. His reasoning is analogous to a person who comes for Hajj from the start with ihram. In contrast, Imam Zufar argues by qiyas that it does not compensate, because the obligation to enter with ihram becomes a debt (dayn) like a vow; once the time passes, it requires a specific intended ihram. He compares it to a vowed i'tikaf which is fulfilled by the Ramadan fast of the same year but not of a subsequent year. The text gives the Hanafi response (lana) that since the compensation is done in the same year, it is valid, unlike after the year changes.

Key Terms
تَادَّى (ta'addaa): To be fulfilled or compensated; used here to mean that the obligation of entry with ihram is fulfilled by the later Hajj.
متروك (matruk): The omitted act; here, the act of entering Makkah with ihram that was missed.
الْمَنْدُور (al-mandhur): That which is vowed (nadhr). Used in the analogy with vowed i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does performing a wajib Hajj compensate for entering Makkah without ihram?
A) Only if the Hajj is performed in the same year
B) Only if the Hajj is performed in a later year
C) Only if the person had not made a vow
D) Only if the Hajj is performed with talbiyah

Key Takeaway
A wajib Hajj in the same year compensates for entering Makkah without ihram; after the year changes, it becomes a debt requiring specific intention.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Entering Makkah without Ihram and Later Hajj in the Same Year
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on sufficiency of later Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a later Hajj performed in the same year suffices for the wajib incurred by entering Makkah without ihram, and explain Zufar's opposing qiyas and the Hanafi response based on istihsan.

Core Idea
A later Hajj in the same year suffices because the missed reverence is compensated within its time.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about a person who enters Makkah without ihram, thereby incurring an obligation to perform Hajj or Umrah. The question is: if that person later performs another Hajj (whether fard, nafl, or Umrah) within the same Hijri year, does that later Hajj fulfill the earlier obligation? The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) says yes, relying on istihsan. Imam Zufar disagrees, using qiyas to vowed obligations. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that the later Hajj performed within the same year suffices for the obligation incurred by entering Makkah without ihram. Note that this is the position of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
This is the mufta bihi ruling.
2
Identify the opponent and their qiyas
Zufar holds that it does not suffice. He draws an analogy to a vowed Hajj (nadhr), which requires separate fulfillment and is not satisfied by a later obligatory Hajj.
Zufar's analogy: just as a fard Hajj does not fulfill a vowed Hajj, the later Hajj does not fulfill the wajib from entering without ihram.
3
Analyze the Hanafi istihsan response
The Hanafi response uses istihsan (juristic preference). The underlying rationale is that the obligation is to honor the Haram with ihram, and this is achieved by any ihram performed within the same year, whether for fard or nafl. The missed reverence is compensated 'in its time'.
The key distinction: within the same year, it is not yet a debt; after the year elapses, it becomes a debt requiring specific intent.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the Hanafi position, no separate Hajj/Umrah is needed; under Zufar's view, a separate act is required.
This difference affects the responsibility of the individual.

ساتھ یہ اعتکاف ادا نہ ہوگا بلکہ ضروری ہوگا کہ رمضان کے علاوہ کسی ماہ میں اعتکاف کے روزوں کے ساتھ اعتکاف کی قضاء کرے۔
Whoever enters Makkah without ihram, then goes out that same year to the miqat and dons ihram for a Hajj that is obligatory upon him, that suffices him from his entry into Makkah without ihram. And Zufar said: it does not suffice him, and that is the analogy, considering what became obligatory upon him due to the vow, so it becomes like when the year elapses. And our proof is that he made up the missed reverence in its time, because the duty upon him is to honor this place with ihram, like when he comes as a Muhrim for the Hajj of Islam in the beginning. Contrary to when the year elapses, because it becomes a debt upon his responsibility, so it is not fulfilled except with a intended ihram, like in the case of a vowed i'tikaf, for it is fulfilled by the fast of Ramadan of this year, not of the second year. Translation: And whoever enters Makkah without ihram, then goes out that same year to the miqat and dons ihram for a Hajj that was obligatory upon him, then this obligatory rite suffices for his entry without ihram. Imam Zufar said it will not suffice, and this is the analogy. He analogizes it to what becomes obligatory due to a vow, so it becomes like the case when the year elapses. And our proof is that he has compensated for the missed reverence in its time, because it was obligatory upon him to honor this place with ihram, just as if he had come in the beginning with the ihram of the obligatory Hajj. Unlike the case when the year elapses, because it becomes a debt upon his responsibility, so it is not fulfilled except with a specific intended ihram, as in the case of a vowed i'tikaf, for it is fulfilled by the fast of Ramadan of this year, not of the second year. Clarification: The issue is that if a person enters Makkah without ihram, then Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory upon him, as per our madhhab. Then if he goes out the same year and goes to the miqat and dons ihram for obligatory Hajj, or voluntary Hajj, or Umrah, then that Hajj or Umrah will suffice for the Hajj or Umrah that became obligatory due to entering without ihram; he does not need to perform it separately. Imam Zufar said it will not suffice, and this is the analogy. The analogy is that if a person had a Hajj become obligatory due to a vow, and he performs the obligatory Hajj, then the vowed Hajj is not dropped by that obligatory Hajj; rather it must be performed separately. Similarly, here by performing the obligatory Hajj, that Hajj which became obligatory due to entering Makkah without ihram is not fulfilled. And this becomes like the case when the year elapses. That is, if a person enters Makkah without ihram and then performs the obligatory Hajj the following year, that obligatory Hajj will not stand in place of the Hajj that became obligatory due to entering without ihram. Our proof is that he has compensated for the missed reverence, i.e., the Hajj or Umrah that became obligatory due to entering Makkah without ihram, within the time—i.e., the same year—in the sense that he performed it within the obligatory Hajj, because it was obligatory upon him to honor the sacred place with ihram in any manner, and that was achieved, so he does not need to perform another separate Hajj or Umrah. Just as if he had come in the beginning with the ihram of the obligatory Hajj, that obligatory Hajj (which he intended) and the Hajj that became obligatory due to entering without ihram would both be fulfilled. Contrary to when the year elapses, because the Hajj that became obligatory due to entering Makkah becomes a debt upon his responsibility, so it will only be fulfilled by a distinct intended ihram—i.e., it will be fulfilled by an ihram that is intended specifically to fulfill that debt, like in the case of a vowed i'tikaf: if someone made a vow for i'tikaf in Ramadan of this year, and fasting in i'tikaf is necessary, then for him the i'tikaf will be fulfilled by the fasts of Ramadan, but it will not be fulfilled by the fasts of Ramadan of the next year; rather it is necessary to make up the i'tikaf in some month other than Ramadan with the fasts of i'tikaf.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who enters Makkah without ihram, thereby incurring an obligation of Hajj or Umrah. If, within the same year, he goes to the miqat and performs another Hajj (whether fard, nafl, or Umrah), the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) states that the later Hajj suffices for the earlier obligation. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing by qiyas (analogy) that it does not suffice, similar to a vowed (nadhr) Hajj that requires separate fulfillment. The Hanafi response relies on istihsan (juristic preference): the missed reverence (entering without ihram) is made up within its time—the same year—by performing any Hajj or Umrah with ihram, which achieves the required honor of the Haram. This ruling applies only if the person performs the later Hajj within the same Hijri year; if the year changes, it becomes a debt that requires a specific ihram with the intention to fulfill that debt. The commentary clarifies the reasoning by analogy to vowed i'tikaf: a vow to observe i'tikaf in Ramadan of the current year is fulfilled by the Ramadan fasts of that year, but not by those of the following year.

Key Terms
إِحْرَام (ihram): The sacred state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, consisting of intention and reciting the talbiyah, along with prohibitions on certain actions.
مِيقَات (miqat): The designated boundary or time for entering ihram; here, the spatial miqat for those coming from outside the Haram.
بُسْتَانِيّ (bustani): A person from the area of Bustan (Batan), i.e., a resident of the orchard region near Makkah, who is allowed to enter Makkah without ihram from the usual miqat but must still wear ihram from his own area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person enters Makkah without ihram and then performs Hajj in the same year, what is the ruling?
A) The later Hajj does not suffice; a separate Hajj is required.
B) The later Hajj suffices for the wajib incurred.
C) The person must sacrifice an animal as a penalty.
D) The person must leave Makkah and re-enter with ihram.

Key Takeaway
A later Hajj (or Umrah) performed in the same Hijri year suffices for the wajib incurred by entering Makkah without ihram, per the majority Hanafi view.

Passing the Miqat and Corrupting Umrah: Dam or No Dam?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on passing the miqat and corrupting umrah, explain Zufar's opposing view and its analogy, and apply the distinction between compensating for the miqat and other prohibitions.

Core Idea
Ihram in qada compensates for missing the miqat; no dam is required for that separate violation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced scenario: a person passes the miqat without ihram, then performs umrah, and then corrupts it (e.g., by intercourse). The Hanafi school rules that he must complete the umrah and do a qada umrah, but no dam for passing the miqat. Imam Zufar differs, analogizing it to corrupting Hajj after passing the miqat. Let’s unpack the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Contested Issue
First, identify the factual situation: passing the miqat without ihram, then entering umrah, then corrupting it. The dispute is whether a dam (sacrifice penalty) is also required for having passed the miqat.
The corruption here means invalidating the umrah by a prohibited act like intercourse.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Basis
The Hanafi position holds that no dam is owed. The basis: when the person performs the qada umrah and enters ihram from the miqat, that revives the missed right of the miqat, compensating for the earlier omission.
The key concept: ihram in qada 'revives' (yuḥyī) the missed obligation.
3
State Zufar's Position and His Analogy
Zufar argues that the dam does not drop. He analogizes to the case of one who passes the miqat, then performs Hajj, and then corrupts the Hajj. In that case, the dam for passing the miqat remains despite the corruption. Zufar sees the passing as a separate prohibition that incurs its own penalty.
His reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy).
4
Examine the Hanafi Response: Why the Analogy Fails
The Hanafi response distinguishes the cases. In the Hajj analogy, the corruption of Hajj does not involve a subsequent qada that re-enters ihram from the miqat. But here, in the qada umrah, the pilgrim performs ihram from the miqat, thereby fulfilling the right of the miqat. The corruption of the original umrah is a separate matter that requires qada, but does not affect the compensation for the miqat.
The crucial difference: the qada umrah itself re-engages the miqat, whereas a corrupted Hajj does not automatically include a corrective ihram from the miqat.
5
Conclude with the Mufta Bihi Ruling and Thamarah al-Khilaf
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is: no dam. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Zufar's follower would require an additional dam, while the mainstream Hanafi position does not.
Tarjih authority: Al-Hidayah supports the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میقات سے تجاوز کر کے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور اسے فاسد کر دیا افعال عمرہ پورے کرے اور عمرہ کی قضا کا حکم وَ مَنْ جَاوَزَ الْوَقْتَ فَأَحْرَمَ لِعُمْرَةٍ وَ أَفْسَدَهَا مَضَى فِيْهَا وَ قَضَاهَا لِأَنَّ الإِحْرَامَ يَقَعُ لَازِمًا فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَفْسَدَ الْحَجَّ وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِتَرْكِ الْوَقْتِ وَعَلَى قِيَاسِ قَوْلِ زُفَرَ لَا يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ الْإِخْتِلَافِ فِي فَائِتِ الْحَجِّ إِذَا جَاوَزَ الْوَقْتَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ وَفِيمَنْ جَاوَزَ الْوَقْتَ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامٍ وَأَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَفْسَدَ حَجَّتَهُ إِنَّمَا يَعْتَبِرُ الْمُجَاوَزَةَ هَذِهِ بِغَيْرِهَا مِنَ الْمَحْظُورَاتِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ قَاضِيًا حَقَّ الْمِيقَاتِ بِالْإِحْرَامِ مِنْهُ فِي الْقَضَاءِ وَهُوَ يُحْيِي الْفَائِتَ وَلَا يَنْعَدِمُ بِهِ غَيْرُهُ مِنَ الْمَحْظُورَاتِ فَوَضَحَ الْفَرْقُ ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے میقات سے تجاوز کر کے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور عمرہ کو فاسد کر دیا تو عمرہ کے افعال پورے کرے اور اس کی قضا کرے۔
Ruling on one who passes the miqat and performs umrah and corrupts it: He should complete its actions and perform qada for it. Because the ihram becomes binding, just as when he corrupts Hajj. And there is no dam upon him for leaving the miqat. And according to Zufar's qiyas, it does not drop from him. And it is similar to the difference in the case of a missed Hajj when one passes the miqat without ihram, and in the case of one who passes the miqat without ihram and performs ihram for Hajj and then corrupts his Hajj. Indeed, he considers this passing over to be like other prohibitions. And our proof is that he becomes a fulfiller of the right of the miqat by performing ihram from it in the qada, and that revives the missed obligation, and that does not void other prohibitions, so the difference is clear. Translation: And whoever passes the miqat and performs ihram for umrah and corrupts it, he should complete the actions of the umrah and make qada for it.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation of a person who passes the miqat without ihram, then enters ihram for Umrah, and then corrupts that Umrah (e.g., by having sexual intercourse). The Hanafi ruling is that he must complete the current Umrah (perform its remaining actions) and also perform a qada (make-up) Umrah. This is because the ihram becomes binding once entered, similar to corrupting Hajj. He does not owe a dam for passing the miqat because the ihram itself, even in qada, fulfills the right of the miqat. Imam Zufar analogizes this to the case of passing the miqat without ihram and then corrupting Hajj; in that case, Zufar says the dam for passing the miqat is not dropped. However, the Hanafi response distinguishes: when one makes up the missed ihram by performing ihram from the miqat in the qada, that revives the missed obligation, and the dam for passing the miqat is waived. The prohibition of passing the miqat without ihram is separate from the corruption of the original umrah; the latter requires qada, but the former is compensated by performing ihram in the qada from the miqat.

Key Terms
إِفْسَاد (ifsad): Corruption of Ihram or Hajj/Umrah by engaging in prohibited acts (e.g., sexual intercourse) that invalidate the state of consecration.
قَضَاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated religious obligation; here, performing a substitute Umrah after corrupting the original.
دَم (dam): A sacrifice (animal) required as a penalty for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah, such as passing the miqat without ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only a dam for passing the miqat.
B) Complete the umrah and perform qada; no dam.
C) Abandon the umrah and perform only qada.
D) Complete the umrah and then perform Hajj as qada.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that performing ihram from the miqat in the qada umrah compensates for having passed it earlier, so no additional dam is required.

Fulfilling the Obligation of Hajj/Umrah After Entering Makkah Without Ihram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fulfilling obligation of entering Makkah without ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when a subsequent Hajj or Umrah fulfills the obligation from entering Makkah without ihram, and evaluate Imam Zufar's counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Any Hajj or Umrah in the same year fulfills the obligation; after the year it becomes a separate debt.

Entering Makkah without ihram creates an obligation to perform Hajj or Umrah. But does a later act in the same year cancel that obligation? The Hanafi majority says yes, while Imam Zufar disagrees using analogy to vowed acts. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the school's reliance on istihsan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) that any Hajj or Umrah in the same year suffices.
The obligation is tied to the same year — think of it as a seasonal duty.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar argues by qiyas: just as a vowed Hajj remains a separate debt, so too the obligation from entering without ihram remains separate.
His qiyas uses the asl (vowed Hajj) where the ruling is that it is not fulfilled by a later obligatory Hajj.
3
Follow Zufar's proof
Trace his analogy: asl = vowed Hajj, hukm = not fulfilled by obligatory Hajj; far' = obligation from entering without ihram; illa = both are independent obligations.
He treats the obligation as a debt similar to a vow regardless of timing.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school uses istihsan: the obligation is to honor the sacred mosque with ihram in the same year; any ihram achieves that. If the year passes, it becomes a debt like a vow.
They distinguish the case based on the time factor — the obligation is not absolute but seasonal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if one enters without ihram and performs Hajj in the same year, no extra act needed per Hanafi; Zufar requires a separate Hajj/Umrah.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position, overriding strict qiyas with istihsan.

اعتکاف میں روزہ رکھنا لازم ہے تو اس کے لئے رمضان کے روزوں کے ساتھ تو اعتکاف ادا ہو جائے گا لیکن دوسرے سال کے رمضان کے روزوں کے ساتھ یہ اعتکاف ادا نہ ہوگا بلکہ ضروری ہوگا کہ رمضان کے علاوہ کسی ماہ میں Contrary to the case when the year has passed, because it becomes a debt upon him, so it will not be fulfilled except with an intended ihram, like in the case of a vowed i'tikaf. Because it is fulfilled with the fast of Ramadan of that same year, not with the fast of the next year. Explanation: The issue is that if a person enters Makkah without ihram, then Hajj or Umrah becomes obligatory upon him, as per our school. Then if he leaves that same year and goes to the miqat and contracts ihram for obligatory Hajj, supererogatory Hajj, or Umrah, then that Hajj or Umrah will suffice for the obligation that became due from entering Makkah without ihram; there is no need to perform it separately. Imam Zufar said it will not suffice, and this is analogy. Analogy: If a person had a vowed Hajj obligatory, and he performed the obligatory Hajj, the vowed Hajj is not cancelled by that obligatory Hajj; rather he must perform it separately. Similarly here, performing the obligatory Hajj will not fulfill the Hajj that became due from entering Makkah without ihram. And this becomes like when the year has passed, i.e., if a person entered Makkah without ihram and then performed the obligatory Hajj the following year, that obligatory Hajj will not stand in place of the Hajj that became due from entering without ihram. Our proof is that he compensated for the omitted (i.e., the Hajj or Umrah that became due from entering Makkah without ihram) within the time, i.e., in the same year, by performing it within the obligatory Hajj, because he was obligated to honor this noble spot with ihram in any way, and that was achieved; therefore, there is no need to perform another Hajj or Umrah separately. Just as if, from the beginning, he had come contracting ihram for obligatory Hajj, it would have sufficed for both the obligatory Hajj he intended and the one due from entering without ihram. Contrary to when the year has passed, because the Hajj due from entering Makkah becomes a debt upon him, so it will only be fulfilled by an intended ihram, i.e., by an ihram contracted with the intention of fulfilling that debt, as in the case of a vowed i'tikaf. For example, if someone vowed i'tikaf in Ramadan of this year and i'tikaf requires fasting, then the i'tikaf is fulfilled with the fasts of Ramadan, but it is not fulfilled with the fasts of the next Ramadan; rather, he must make up the i'tikaf in some other month with the fasts of i'tikaf.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the obligation of Hajj or Umrah that becomes due upon a person who enters Makkah without ihram is fulfilled by a subsequent Hajj or Umrah performed in the same year. The author explains the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and the majority) that if the person performs any Hajj or Umrah (whether obligatory, supererogatory, or Umrah) in the same year, it suffices for the obligation. The key is that the obligation is not considered a separate debt but rather an immediate duty to honor the sacred precinct with ihram, which is achieved by any valid ihram in that year. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing by analogy to a vowed Hajj: just as a vowed Hajj remains a separate debt even after performing the obligatory Hajj, so too the obligation from entering without ihram remains separate. The Hanafi response distinguishes based on timing: if the substitute act occurs within the same year, it compensates the obligation as part of the same season; if the year passes, the obligation becomes a debt requiring a specific intention (like a vow). This reasoning is grounded in istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.

Key Terms
احرام مقصود (ihram maqsud): An ihram contracted with the specific intention of fulfilling a particular obligation (like a debt or vow).
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; Zufar uses qiyas to argue that the obligation from entering without ihram is like a vowed Hajj.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; the Hanafi school prefers this over qiyas in this case to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Umrah does not fulfill the obligation; a separate Hajj is needed.
B) The Umrah suffices for the obligation from entering without ihram.
C) The person must repeat the Umrah with intention for the debt.
D) The obligation is cancelled automatically.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the obligation from entering Makkah without ihram is fulfilled by any Hajj or Umrah performed in the same year; after the year, it becomes a separate debt requiring a specific intention.

The Effect of Qada on Dam for Passing Miqat Without Ihram
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether qada from miqat drops the dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether qada of Hajj/Umrah from the miqat drops the dam for passing the miqat without ihram, compare it with Imam Zufar’s view, and explain the legal reasoning (ta‘līl) behind each position.

Core Idea
Making qada from the miqat compensates the miqat violation, dropping the dam—unlike other ihram prohibitions.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school. When a pilgrim passes the miqat without ihram, a dam becomes wajib. But what if the pilgrim later makes qada of the Hajj or Umrah from the miqat? Does the dam fall? Abu Hanifa and the majority say yes; Imam Zufar says no. The reasoning turns on the nature of the violation and the role of qada. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply usul al-fiqh principles to fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
Determine the specific point of disagreement: whether qada of Hajj/Umrah from the miqat removes the obligation of dam incurred by passing the miqat without ihram.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi between Abu Hanifa (and Sahibayn) and Imam Zufar.
2
State the Hanafi Majority Position
Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad hold that the dam is dropped because qada from the miqat fulfills the right of the miqat and stands in place of the original act, making it as if no violation occurred.
This view is mufta bihi.
3
State Imam Zufar’s Position
Imam Zufar holds that the dam is not dropped. He analogizes passing miqat without ihram to other ihram prohibitions (perfume, sewn clothes) where qada does not remove the dam because those violations are independent.
He uses qiyas on other prohibitions.
4
Analyze the Proof (Dalil) for Each Side
For Abu Hanifa: qada from miqat compensates the specific harm of miqat violation, and dam is only for compensation. For Imam Zufar: the violation is independent; analogy with other prohibitions shows dam remains.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between miqat-related and non-miqat prohibitions.
5
Apply the Thamarah (Practical Consequence)
If a pilgrim passes miqat without ihram, then makes qada from miqat, according to Abu Hanifa no dam is due; according to Imam Zufar, the original dam remains obligatory. In fatwa, the majority view is followed.
Thus a mufti would not obligate a second dam after qada.

Source Text

کتاب الحج
کتاب الحج
۴۹۰
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
کرے۔ کیونکہ احرام تو لازم ہو کر واقع ہوتا ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے حج کو فاسد کر دیا اور اس پر میقات چھوڑنے سے قربانی لازم نہ ہوگی اور امام زفر کے قول کے قیاس پر اس سے دم ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ اور یہ اختلاف نظیر ہے اس اختلاف کی جو جج فوت کرنے والے کے حق میں ہے جبکہ اس نے بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز کیا۔ اور اس شخص کے بارے میں ہے جو بغیر احرام میقات سے گذر گیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا پھر اپنے حج کو فاسد کر دیا امام زفر اس تجاوز کرنے کو اس کے علاوہ دوسرے ممنوعات پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء میں وہ شخص میقات سے احرام باندھنے میں میقات کا حق ادا کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ اور قضاء فوت شدہ کی حکایت کرتا ہے اور قضاء کے ذریعہ دوسرے ممنوعات معدوم نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ اس لئے فرق واضح ہو گیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز کر گیا پھر اس نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور عمرہ کو فاسد کر دیا تو اس مسئلہ میں تین احکام میں ایک یہ کہ افعال عمرہ پورے کرے، دوم یہ کہ میقات سے احرام باندھ کر اس کی قضاء کرے۔ سوم یہ کہ اس کے ذمہ سے وہ کرے۔سوم دم ساقط ہو جائے گا جو بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تھا۔ اول کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام ایک عقد لازم ہے آدمی شروع کرنے کے بعد بغیر افعال ادا کئے اس سے نہیں نکل سکتا۔ اس لئے افعال پورے کرے۔ دوم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے صحیح طور پر عمرہ ادا کرنے کا التزام کیا تھا حالانکہ صحیح طور پر عمرہ نہیں کیا اس لئے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ اور سوم یعنی سقوط دم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اسنے میقات سے احرام باندھ کر قضا کی تو اس سے اس نقصان کی تلافی ہو جائے گی جو نقصان بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوا تھا۔ پس جب پیدا شدہ نقصان کی تلافی ہو گئی تو دم ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ دم نقصان کی تلافی ہی کے لئے واجب کیا گیا تھا۔ جیسے کسی کو نماز میں سہو ہو گیا اس نے نماز کو فاسد کر کے نماز کی قضا کر لی تو سجدہ سہو ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ حضرت امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ عمرہ کی قضاء کر لینے کے باوجود دم ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب کوئی شخص بغیر احرام کے میقات سے تجاوز کر گیا پھر حج کا احرام باندھا مگر اس کو حج مل نہ سکا بلکہ حج فوت ہو گیا پھر اس نے آئندہ سال اس حج کی قضا کر لی تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کے ذمہ سے وہ دم ساقط ہو جائے گا جو بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے واجب تھا۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک ساقط نہیں ہو گا۔ اور یہی اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب کوئی شخص بغیر احرام کے میقات سے گذر گیا اور حج کا احرام باندھا پھر وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع وغیرہ کے ذریعہ حج کو فاسد کر دیا پھر اس کی قضا کی تو ہمارے نزدیک بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے جو دم واجب ہوا تھا وہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ امام زفر بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز کرنے کو دوسرے ممنوعات احرام پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی اگر کسی پر خوشبو لگانے یا سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنے کی وجہ سے دم واجب ہوا ہو اور پھر حج فوت ہو گیا تو یہ دم قضاء کی وجہ سے ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ اسی طرح جب میقات سے بغیر احرام تجاوز کرنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تو وہ بھی حج فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے قضا کے اندر میقات سے احرام باندھ کر میقات کا حق ادا کر دیا اور قضا بھی فوت شدہ کا قائم مقام ہے پس گویا اس نے بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز نہیں کیا اور جب بغیر احرام میقات سے تجاوز نہیں کیا تو دم بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ دم اس کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا تھا۔ اور دوسرے ممنوعات یعنی خوشبو وغیرہ لگانا حج کے فوت ہونے اور اس کی قضا کرنے سے معدوم نہیں ہوتے بلکہ باقی رہتے ہیں اور جب ممنوع احرام باقی رہا تو ہم بھی باقی رہے گا ساقط نہ ہو گا۔ پس بغیر احرام تجاوز کرنے اور دوسرے ممنوعات کے درمیان
فرق واضح ہو گیا۔
Book of Hajj. ... He should perform. Because ihram occurs as a binding contract. So it becomes as if he corrupted the Hajj, and leaving the miqat does not necessitate a sacrifice. And according to the analogy of Imam Zufar's statement, the blood (dam) will not be dropped. And this difference is analogous to the difference regarding the one who lost the Hajj when he passed the miqat without ihram. And it concerns the person who passed the miqat without ihram and then put on ihram for Hajj and then corrupted his Hajj. Imam Zufar analogizes this transgression to other prohibitions. And our proof is that in the qada, that person will be fulfilling the right of the miqat by putting on ihram from the miqat. And qada replicates the missed act, and through qada other prohibitions are not eliminated. So the difference is clear. Explanation of the issue: If a person passes the miqat without ihram, then puts on ihram for Umrah and corrupts the Umrah, then in this issue there are three rulings: first, he should complete the actions of Umrah; second, he should make qada of it by putting on ihram from the miqat; third, the blood (dam) that had become obligatory due to passing the miqat without ihram will be dropped from his liability. The proof of the first is that ihram is a binding contract; a person cannot exit from it without performing the actions after starting. Therefore he should complete the actions. The proof of the second is that he had undertaken to perform Umrah correctly while he did not do so, so qada is obligatory. And the proof of the third, the dropping of dam, is that when he made qada by putting on ihram from the miqat, this compensates for the harm that arose from passing the miqat without ihram. So when the arising harm is compensated, the dam is dropped because the dam was made obligatory only for compensating harm. Just as if someone had an error (sahw) in prayer, he corrupted the prayer and made qada, then the sajdah sahw is dropped. Imam Zufar says that despite making qada of Umrah, the dam is not dropped. The same difference occurs if a person passes the miqat without ihram, then puts on ihram for Hajj but the Hajj is not attained, but rather the Hajj is missed, then in the following year he makes qada of that Hajj—according to us the dam that was obligatory due to passing the miqat without ihram will be dropped; according to Imam Zufar it will not be dropped. And the same difference occurs if a person passes the miqat without ihram and puts on ihram for Hajj, then before standing at Arafah he corrupts the Hajj through intercourse etc., then makes qada—according to us the dam obligatory due to passing the miqat without ihram will be dropped; according to Imam Zufar it will not be dropped. Imam Zufar analogizes passing the miqat without ihram to other prohibitions of ihram. That is, if dam became obligatory on someone due to applying perfume or wearing sewn clothes, and then the Hajj is missed, this dam is not dropped by qada. Similarly, when it became obligatory due to passing the miqat without ihram, it will also not be dropped by missing the Hajj. Our proof is that he, in the qada, fulfilled the right of the miqat by putting on ihram from the miqat, and qada stands in place of the missed act, so it is as if he did not pass the miqat without ihram, and when he did not pass without ihram, the dam will not be obligatory because the dam was obligatory due to that. And other prohibitions, like applying perfume, are not eliminated by missing Hajj and making qada, but remain; and when the prohibition of ihram remains, the dam also remains, not dropped. So the difference between passing without ihram and other prohibitions is clear.
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of qada of Hajj or Umrah on the dam (sacrificial animal) that became obligatory due to passing the miqat without ihram. The issue is whether making qada from the miqat removes the obligation of dam. Abu Hanifa and his school (including Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the dam is dropped because qada from the miqat compensates for the violation. Imam Zufar analogizes this to other prohibitions of ihram (like perfume, sewn clothes) where qada does not remove the dam because those prohibitions are independent violations. The Hanafis distinguish: passing the miqat without ihram is a violation specific to the miqat, and qada from the miqat rectifies that specific deficiency. The passage also explains three rulings when someone passes miqat without ihram, then makes Umrah, corrupts it: (1) complete the corrupt Umrah, (2) make qada of Umrah from miqat, (3) the original dam for passing miqat is dropped. The analogy with sajdah sahw in prayer is given.

Key Terms
میقات (mīqāt): The boundary station where pilgrims must enter ihram; in this passage, the specific miqat for a Makki is the Haram itself.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) obligatory as penalty for certain violations of Hajj/Umrah, including passing miqat without ihram.
قضا (qaḍā): Making up a missed or invalid Hajj/Umrah by performing it again correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to the dam for passing the miqat without ihram if the person later makes qada of Hajj from the miqat?
A) It remains obligatory
B) It is dropped
C) It is doubled
D) It must be paid but can be delayed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qada of Hajj/Umrah from the miqat drops the dam for passing miqat without ihram because qada compensates the miqat violation; other prohibitions are not similarly rectified.
